# 素问六气玄珠密语

*The Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi from the Plain Questions*
**Title:** *The Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi from the Plain Questions* (abbreviated as *Mysterious Pearl Whispers*)
**Attributed to:** Wang Bing of the Tang Dynasty
**Volume Count:** Seventeen
**Source Edition:** *Daoist Canon of the Orthodox Unity*, Supreme Mystery Section
**Collated Edition:** Ming Dynasty manuscript copy held at the National Library of China (hereafter referred to as "the manuscript")

**Preface to *The Mysterious Pearl’s Esoteric Discourse***

In my youth, I devoted myself to the Dao, resolute in my pursuit of learning, undeterred by winter’s cold at my desk or summer’s scorching heat. Later, when the principles of heaven’s governance were established, I withdrew from scholarly pursuits, passing my days in leisure, my heart dwelling in the supreme Dao. Often, I pondered the great reckoning, fearing the fleeting years left me without refuge; I longed to fathom the true essence, yet dreaded time’s swift passage. Thus, I focused my mind on seeking the Dao, steadfast in my quest for the wise, until I encountered the Mysterious Pearl and became his disciple.

For years, I dared not inquire into the gate of the supreme and wondrous Dao. Gradually, I delved into its depths, and he expounded its profound principles, instructing me: *"In a century, one may transmit this to but a single person. To those without the resolve to seek it, do not recklessly divulge it."* Upon meeting the Master of the Mysterious Pearl, he awakened my understanding, and so I styled myself "Awakener of the Mysterious," for I had sought enlightenment from the Master of the Mysterious Pearl.

Now, I have directly transcribed five copies, each comprising ten volumes. Though the headings and categories share the same meaning, their title is *The Mysterious Pearl’s Esoteric Discourse*—the very words the Master of the Mysterious Pearl secretly imparted by mouth. Over a hundred years, I have not encountered a single seeker of true resolve, yet I dared not conceal the sage’s teachings. Thus, I transcribed five copies and concealed them within the deep caves of the Five Peaks, first offering them to the mountain spirits before sealing them away. I did this so that future seekers might chance upon them. Should one find them, they must treasure and cherish them, transmitting them only to those of extraordinary worth, never lightly bestowing them upon the unworthy. Such was the Master of the Mysterious Pearl’s earnest admonition.

These ten volumes reveal heaven’s decrees, the transformations of the cosmic cycles, the products of the earth, and the calamities yet to come—all of which may be foreseen. The abstruse words of the *Suwen* may be directly elucidated through them. They teach the cultivation of the five viscera, the nourishment of all life, the methods for reinforcing the weak and rectifying imbalance, and the arts of dispelling evil to preserve the upright. Thus, the sage declared: *"Heaven gives life, heaven takes it away—such is the principle of the Dao."* One who fathoms the meaning of the Mysterious Pearl may, upon perceiving heaven’s life-giving forces, prolong life, and upon perceiving heaven’s destructive forces, evade death. As the *Yinfu Jing* states: *"To observe heaven’s Dao and grasp its movements is perfection."* This means that one who aligns with the great cycles of the five phases and six qi may fulfill heaven’s allotted span of one hundred and twenty years. Those who die prematurely do so because the five phases and six qi alternately punish and cut short life. Thus, the ancestral masters taught: *"The Dao of the six qi originates in heaven’s mechanism. Its advent may be discerned, its departure traced."* It should be inscribed on jade tablets, stored in golden caskets, and transmitted only to the worthy—lest misfortune befall nine generations.

---

**Volume I of *The Mysterious Pearl’s Esoteric Discourse on the Six Qi of the Suwen***
*Recorded by the Awakener of the Mysterious*

**The Record of the Fivefold Movements’ Primordial Penetration**

The movement governs qi, thus occupying the central position—between heaven above and earth below, within the convergence of qi, amid the myriad transformations, where all things and humanity arise. Movement is motion, revolution—cyclical and unceasing. When the Supreme Ultimate first divided, the five movements were arrayed horizontally at the center, revolving to this day, endlessly repeating.

The sages observed and discerned: since the opening of heaven and earth, they saw a green qi spanning *ding* and *ren*—thus *ding* and *ren* govern the Wood movement; a red qi spanning *wu* and *gui*—thus *wu* and *gui* govern the Fire movement; a yellow qi spanning *jia* and *ji*—thus *jia* and *ji* govern the Earth movement; a white qi spanning *yi* and *geng*—thus *yi* and *geng* govern the Metal movement; a black qi spanning *bing* and *xin*—thus *bing* and *xin* govern the Water movement. First, the five movements revolve, then the celestial regulators are recorded.

The celestial regulator serves as the guest, while the movement’s qi is the host. The in-ground regulator also serves as the guest, with the intermediate qi as the secondary guest. Thus, the qi of the five movements ascends to unite with heaven. The qi of the Wood movement ascends to unite with the Azure Heaven; the qi of the Fire movement ascends to unite with the Vermilion Heaven; the qi of the Earth movement ascends to unite with the Yellow Heaven; the qi of the Metal movement ascends to unite with the White Heaven; the qi of the Water movement ascends to unite with the Mysterious Heaven.

The qi of the Azure Heaven courses through *Gui*, *Liu*, *Wei*, and *Shi*—corresponding to the *ding* and *ren* divisions. The qi of the Vermilion Heaven courses through *Jiao*, *Kang*, *Niu*, and *Nü*—corresponding to the *wu* and *gui* divisions. The qi of the Yellow Heaven courses through *Xin*, *Wei*, *Shen*, and *Jing*—corresponding to the *jia* and *ji* divisions. The qi of the White Heaven courses through *Kang*, *Di*, *Bi*, and *Zi*—corresponding to the *yi* and *geng* divisions. The qi of the Mysterious Heaven courses through *Zhang*, *Yi*, *Lou*, and *Wei*—corresponding to the *bing* and *xin* divisions.

Within the Azure Heaven, a green qi courses through four lodges, descending to unite with the Wood movement, aligning with *ding* and *ren*. Within the Vermilion Heaven, a red qi courses through four lodges, descending to unite with the Fire movement, aligning with *wu* and *gui*. Within the Yellow Heaven, a yellow qi courses through four lodges, descending to unite with the Earth movement, aligning with *jia* and *ji*. Within the White Heaven, a white qi courses through four lodges, descending to unite with the Metal movement, aligning with *yi* and *geng*. Within the Mysterious Heaven, a black qi courses through four lodges, descending to unite with the Water movement, aligning with *bing* and *xin*.

Amidst the five movements and five colors, within the flowing qi, the six qi are distinguished. Within the green qi, heaven generates wind, and wind generates Wood upon the earth. Within the red qi, heaven generates warmth and heat—both sovereign and ministerial Fire—thus heat generates Fire upon the earth. Within the yellow qi, heaven generates dampness, and dampness generates Earth upon the earth.

Within the white qi, heaven generates clarity and dryness, and dryness generates Metal upon the earth. Within the black qi, heaven generates cold, and cold generates Water upon the earth.

Thus, the six qi of heaven are wind, warmth, heat, dampness, dryness, and cold. The five movements produced by earth are Water, Fire, Earth, Metal, and Wood. When the six qi and five movements unite above and below, all transformations and creations arise from them, and the flourishing, decline, birth, and dominance of the five creatures all depend on them.

The five creatures are furred creatures, feathered creatures, naked creatures, armored creatures, and scaled creatures. Thus, the *shi* and *zi* (master and disciple) serve as the leaders of furred creatures, corresponding to Wood; the phoenix serves as the leader of feathered creatures, corresponding to Fire; humans serve as the leaders of naked creatures, corresponding to Earth; the tortoise serves as the leader of armored creatures, corresponding to Metal; and the dragon serves as the leader of scaled creatures, corresponding to Water. These five encompass all categories of beings.

Thus, in the movements: *ding* and *ren* govern the Wood movement, with *ren* presiding over hardness and *ding* over softness. Hardness signifies excess, while softness signifies insufficiency. Excess means the Wood qi harms Earth, while insufficiency leads to self-decline, and self-decline results in receiving Metal’s punishment. *wu* and *gui* govern the Fire movement, with *wu* presiding over hardness and *gui* over softness. Hardness signifies excess, while softness signifies insufficiency. Excess means the Fire qi harms Metal, while insufficiency results in receiving Water’s punishment. *jia* and *ji* govern the Earth movement, with *jia* presiding over hardness and *ji* over softness. Hardness signifies excess, while softness signifies insufficiency. Excess means the Earth qi harms Water, while insufficiency results in receiving Wood’s punishment. *yi* and *geng* govern the Metal movement, with *geng* presiding over hardness and *yi* over softness. Hardness signifies excess, while softness signifies insufficiency. Excess means the Metal qi harms Wood, while insufficiency results in receiving Fire’s punishment. *bing* and *xin* govern the Water movement, with *bing* presiding over hardness and *xin* over softness. Hardness signifies excess, while softness signifies insufficiency. Excess means the Water qi harms Fire, while insufficiency results in receiving Earth’s punishment. These describe the hardness and softness of the movements and the meaning of their flourishing and decline.

The movements arise from the heavenly stems. There are ten stems—five yang and five yin—which pair with earth’s six yin and six yang to form the sixty *jiazi* cycles. Thus, *jia*, *wu*, *bing*, *geng*, and *ren* are yang stems, governing yang years. Yang years correspond to *zi*, *yin*, *chen*, *wu*, *shen*, and *xu*, and in these six years, yang stems converge, all signifying excess. *Yi*, *ding*, *ji*, *xin*, and *gui* are yin stems, governing yin years. Yin years correspond to *chou*, *mao*, *si*, *wei*, *you*, and *hai*, and in these six years, yin stems converge, all signifying insufficiency.

Yet insufficiency may include balanced qi. Balanced qi occurs, for example, in a *ding-mao* year of the Wood movement—this is called balanced qi. Why? Though *ding* is the soft aspect of Wood, and *mao* is a yin year, *mao* assists *ding*’s softness, thus achieving balanced qi. Another example: in a *yi-you* year of the Metal movement—this is called balanced qi. Why? Though *yi* is the soft aspect of Metal, and *you* is a yin year, *you* assists *yi*’s softness, thus achieving balanced qi. Another example: in a *xin-hai* year of the Water movement—this is also called balanced qi. Why? Though *xin* is the soft aspect of Water, and *hai* is a yin year, *hai* assists *xin*’s softness, thus achieving balanced qi. Another example: in a *gui-si* year of the Fire movement—this is also called balanced qi. Why? Though *gui* is the soft aspect of Fire, and *si* is a yin year, *si* assists *gui*’s softness, thus achieving balanced qi. Another example: when a *ji* year encounters *chou* or *wei* years—though *ji* is the soft aspect of Earth, and *chou* and *wei* are yin years, *chou* and *wei* assist *ji*’s softness, thus achieving balanced qi. *Chen* and *xu* are also Earth positions, but these two years are yang years, each signifying excess.

Another method: Each year, the transition of qi occurs on the day of Major Cold preceding the new year. For example, in a *ding* year, if the day of transition coincides with the first day of the lunar month and falls on a *ren* day, *ding* meeting *ren* is called the "stem-virtue correspondence." Correspondence means union, thus achieving balanced qi. If this alignment is missed by even a single day, it will not be effective. If, at the time of transition, the hour coincides with the *ren* stem, the same applies; beyond this, it will not be effective. The rest follow this pattern. Thus, *ji* meeting *jia*, *xin* meeting *bing*, *gui* meeting *wu*, and *yi* meeting *geng* are all "stem-virtue correspondences." Outside the day and hour of transition, this alignment does not occur.

Furthermore, in years of insufficiency, if the month’s stem aligns, correspondence is achieved, though it may not be effective. If one encounters a stem alignment before the victorious qi prevails, it results in balanced qi. If, after the victorious qi has acted and the restorative qi has completed its course, the month’s stem aligns, it regains its proper position. Detailed explanations follow in the secret texts.

**Anticipation and Response, Supplementation and Drainage: A Record**

The five movements and six qi each have their victories and restorations. Thus, when Wood is about to prevail, green mists first appear among the forests, and the trees emit sounds—this is the omen of the radiant *Zhen* star. Furthermore, when Wood is about to prevail, the *gong* tone loses its harmony, naked creatures fail to thrive, and the rains and dampness lose their season. In the twelfth month, one first seizes its source of transformation—this is called "anticipation."

Anticipation means seizing in advance what is yet to come. Seizing means draining; one drains its source with needles. Thus, when the Wood qi is about to prevail, one first drains the source of the Liver, located at *Taichong*, in the depression three *cun* behind the base of the big toe—this is where the Liver meridian passes, serving as its source. First, press the source point with the left hand; when the moving qi is felt, insert the needle. The needle enters three *fen*, the position of yang, and upon receiving the heavenly qi, retain the needle for three breaths—this corresponds to Wood’s generative number, three.

Then, tap the area around the point with the hand to guide the qi to the needle’s tip. Push the needle inward to a depth of five *fen* and retain it for eight breaths—this corresponds to Wood’s completion number, eight. Here, one draws the heavenly qi to receive the earthly qi. When the needle’s tip seems to move, the qi has connected. Quickly withdraw the needle and immediately press the point with the hand. This is how one anticipates Wood’s excess by draining the Liver’s source, preventing it from overwhelming Earth.

For medicinal treatment, use acrid and balanced herbs to restrain Wood’s excess, and sweet herbs to support Earth’s deficiency. Avoid sour foods, which would aid Wood’s dominance.

When Fire is about to prevail, the distant horizon glows with a crimson hue, mountains, rivers, grasses, and trees first wither and dry, and creatures of the *jia* category develop widespread dry scabs. The *shang* tone loses its harmony—this occurs in the third month. One anticipates and seizes its source of transformation, draining Fire’s source before Wood’s ascendance. Thus, the Heart’s source emerges at *Tailing*, in the depression between the two bones behind the palm—where the Heart meridian passes, serving as its source. First, press the source point with the left hand; when the moving qi is felt, insert the needle. The needle enters three *fen*, the position of yang, and upon receiving the heavenly qi, retain the needle for two breaths—this corresponds to Fire’s generative number.

Then, tap the area around the point with the hand to guide the qi to the needle’s tip. Push the needle inward to a depth of five *fen* and retain it for seven breaths—this corresponds to Fire’s completion number. Here, one draws the heavenly qi to connect with the earthly qi. When the needle’s tip seems to move, the qi has connected. Quickly withdraw the needle to drain the excess qi. This drains the source of the Pericardium and lesser Heart, addressing the excess of ministerial Fire. The source of sovereign Fire is called the "source of Lesser Yin." The Lesser Yin’s source emerges at *Duigu*, the true source of the Heart, located in the depression at the tip of the *dui* bone behind the palm—also named *Shenmen* or *Zhongdu*. The needling method follows the previous procedure.

For medicinal treatment, use salty and balanced herbs to restrain Fire’s excess, and acrid herbs to supplement Metal’s deficiency. Avoid bitter foods, which would aid Fire’s dominance.

When Earth is about to prevail, mountains and stones first moisten, yellow dust rises on all sides, oppressive heat arises, the *lei* and *mai* qi become agitated, mist and haze spread, and the *yu* tone diminishes—these are its signs. In the fifth month, one anticipates and seizes its source of transformation, first draining the Spleen’s source. Thus, the Spleen’s source emerges at *Taibai*, in the depression at the inner side of the foot’s *jiao* bone—where the Foot Greater Yin meridian passes, serving as its source. First, press the source point with the left hand; when the moving qi is felt, insert the needle. The needle reaches three *fen*, the position of yang, and is retained for five breaths—this corresponds to Earth’s number.

Tap the area around the point with the hand to guide the qi to the needle’s tip. Push the needle inward to a depth of five *fen* and retain it for five breaths—also corresponding to Earth’s number. This is called drawing the heavenly qi to connect with the earthly qi. When the needle’s tip seems to move, quickly withdraw the needle to drain the excess qi, preventing the Spleen’s qi from becoming excessive and harming the Kidneys.

For medicinal treatment, use sour and balanced herbs to restrain Earth’s excess, and salty herbs to supplement the Kidneys’ deficiency. Avoid sweet foods, which would aid Earth’s dominance.

When Metal is about to prevail, western winds arise frequently, pines and bamboos rustle, the earth generates white salt efflorescence, the earthly qi first dries, mountains manifest white vapors, a killing force arises, trees wither and grasses fade, and the *jiao* tone wanes—these are its omens. In the sixth month, one anticipates and seizes its source of transformation, first draining the Lung’s source. Thus, the Lung’s source emerges at *Taiyuan*, in the depression one *cun* and five *fen* behind the large tendon of the palm—where the Hand Greater Yin meridian passes, serving as its source. First, press the source point with the left hand; when the moving qi is felt, insert the needle. The needle reaches three *fen*, the position of yang, and is retained for four breaths—this corresponds to Metal’s generative number.

Tap the area around the point with the hand to guide the qi to the needle’s tip. Push the needle inward to a depth of five *fen* and retain it for nine breaths—this corresponds to Metal’s completion number. This is called drawing the heavenly qi to connect with the earthly qi. When the qi is obtained, quickly withdraw the needle to drain the Lung’s excess qi, preventing it from harming the Liver.

For medicinal treatment, use bitter and balanced herbs to restrain Metal’s excess, and sour herbs to supplement the Liver’s deficiency. Avoid acrid foods, which would aid Metal’s dominance.

When Water is about to prevail, the sky becomes heavily overcast, crows fall silent, the great void darkens, the yang light fails to govern, cold qi arrives first, the *zhi* tone falls short, and Mars disappears—these are its omens. In the ninth month, one anticipates and seizes its source of transformation, first draining the Kidneys’ source. Thus, the Kidneys’ source emerges at *Taixi*, in the depression below the inner ankle at the prominence of the large bone—where the Foot Greater Yin meridian passes, serving as its source. First, press the source point with the left hand; when the moving qi is felt, insert the needle. The needle enters three *fen*, the position of yang, and is retained for one breath—this corresponds to Water’s generative number.

Tap the area around the point with the hand to guide the qi to the needle’s tip. Push the needle inward to a depth of five *fen* and retain it for six breaths—this corresponds to Water’s completion number. This is called drawing the heavenly qi to connect with the earthly qi. When the qi is obtained, quickly withdraw the needle to drain the Kidneys’ excess qi, preventing it from harming the Heart’s qi.

For medicinal treatment, use sweet herbs to balance and restrain the Kidneys’ excess, and bitter herbs to supplement the Heart’s deficiency. Avoid salty foods, which would aid the Kidneys’ dominance.

Why does one regulate these sources of transformation? To regulate means to supplement; to seize means to drain. One drains the excess of the prevailing phase and supplements the deficiency of the weakened phase. For example, when Wood’s qi prevails, Earth becomes deficient. Thus, one drains the Liver’s source and supplements the Spleen’s source.

When Fire’s qi prevails, Metal becomes deficient. Thus, one drains the Heart’s source and supplements the Lungs’ source. When Earth’s qi prevails, Water becomes deficient. Thus, one drains the Spleen’s source and supplements the Kidneys’ source. When Metal’s qi prevails, Wood becomes deficient. Thus, one drains the Lungs’ source and supplements the Liver’s source. When Water’s qi prevails, Fire becomes deficient. Thus, one drains the Kidneys’ source and supplements the Heart’s source.

To regulate and supplement the sources of transformation, first press the source point with the left hand. When the moving qi is obtained, insert the needle to a depth of five fen, reaching the yin division—Earth’s qi. Retain the needle for the duration of one exhalation, corresponding to the generative number of the Five Phases. When the movement of Earth’s qi is felt, withdraw the needle to three fen, reaching the yang division—Heaven’s qi. This is called drawing yin to yang, a method of regulating and supplementing the sources of transformation. Retain the needle for the duration of one exhalation, corresponding to the completion number of the Five Phases.

Thus, when the needle is inserted from the exterior to the interior and then withdrawn, it is called draining. When the needle is inserted from the interior to the exterior and then withdrawn, it is called supplementing. Supplementing is therefore regulating, and seizing is draining. One drains the excess of the prevailing phase and regulates the deficiency of the weakened phase. *Suwen Liuqi Xuanzhu Miyu*, Scroll One, concludes.

*Suwen Liuqi Xuanzhu Miyu*, Scroll Two
By Qi Xuanzi
"Yunfu Tiandi Ji" Chapter

In the year of *jiazi*, the central phase is Earth, governed by the Grand Palace (*Taigong*). Earth-qi is in excess, and this is called "Abundant Mounds" (*Dunfu*). Earth’s motion brings rain and transformation, resulting in excessive dampness throughout the year. This injures the kidney viscus and, over time, affects the bladder. Scaled creatures (*linchong*) fail to thrive, while shelled creatures (*baochong*) flourish excessively—this is the triumph of spleen-qi. The people suffer from abdominal pain, cold limbs, melancholy, heaviness of body, and vexing oppression. Above, this corresponds to the Star of Saturn (*Zhenxing*). In severe cases, muscles wither, feet become limp and unresponsive, walking induces cramping, pain arises beneath the feet, fluid retention causes central fullness, digestion weakens, and the four limbs fail to rise. When transformation arises from its proper position, the viscus-qi lies concealed in its workings, and qi rules alone. Springs surge, rivers overflow, dried marshes teem with fish, and great winds and rains arrive. Earth collapses, scaled creatures appear on land, and diseases manifest as abdominal fullness, rumbling intestines, and severe diarrhea. The transformation of rain is five—this is the mandate of excessive Earth.

The year of *jiamu* shares the same transformative mandate.

In the year of *yichou*, the central phase is Metal, governed by Lesser Shang (*Shaoshang*). Disaster strikes the seventh palace (*qigong*), which is the West, corresponding to *dui* (Lake) in the directions, the lung in the human body, and autumn in the four seasons. This signifies Metal’s insufficiency, and it is called "Following Transformation" (*Congge*). Fire’s triumphant mandate prevails over Metal, causing all things to flourish, while dryness and desiccation spread. The people suffer from heaviness in the shoulders and back, frequent sneezing, and bloody diarrhea. The qi of contraction (*shouqi*) lags behind its mandate, and the triumph of the conqueror grows extreme. Metal’s child is Water, and Water comes to rescue its mother—this is called "Counter-Triumph" (*Fusheng*). In counter-triumph, cold rains arrive violently, bringing hail, snow, frost, and killing qi. Yin cold ascends to the head and brain, causing pain that extends to the chest and nape, fever, and failure of the cinnabar valley (*dangu*) to form. The people suffer from mouth sores and, in severe cases, heart pain. The transformation of desiccation is four, following the generative number.

The year of *yiwei* shares the same correct transformative mandate.

In the year of *bingyin*, the central phase is Water, governed by Grand Yu (*Taiyu*). Water-qi is in excess, and this is called "Flowing Overflow" (*Liuyan*). It punishes Heaven’s mandate, preventing transformation, and the heart viscus is afflicted. Cold qi spreads, harming the heart’s fire. The people suffer from fever, vexation, palpitations, yin cold in the upper, middle, and lower regions, delirium, forgetfulness, and heart pain. Cold arrives early, and in severe cases, the abdomen swells, channels become distended, wheezing and coughing arise, night sweats occur, and one is struck by *meng* wind. Great rains fall, and dust and mist gather densely. The transformation of cold is six, following the completion number—this is the governance of excess.

The year of *bingshen* follows the same mandate as before. Why does Water’s transformative mandate grow even stronger? Because *shen* (Metal) generates Water, and in a *shen* year, the surplus of Water’s phase becomes even more pronounced.

In the year of *dingmao*, the central phase is Wood, governed by Correct Jue (*Zhengjiao*). The phase attains balanced qi, and this is called "Spreading Harmony" (*Fuhe*). This is what is meant by balanced qi: Metal does not conquer Wood, nor does it bring disaster to Earth. Thus, each transformative mandate aligns with its proper time, and this is called balanced qi, also known as "Yearly Convergence" (*Suihui*). *Ding* governs Wood, and *mao* is Wood—its qi assists it. In the *ding* year, the first month is *renyin*, and *ren* harmonizes with *ding* in stem virtue—this is called "Stem-Virtue Convergence" (*Gande Fu*). Thus, the yearly triumph prevails. The transformation of wind is three, following the generative number. This is the day of correct transformation (*Zhenghua*), meaning the mandate transforms in accord with its time, and no other mandate intrudes—thus, it is the day of correct transformation.

The year of *dingyou* shares the same phase, but it does not receive the year’s power. *You* is Metal, and in the first month, *renyin*, it is also called "Stem-Virtue Convergence." However, the triumph sign does not arrive, so it is not called a Yearly Convergence. The transformation of wind is three, following the generative number. In the year of *dingyou*, the mandate is even more pronounced.

In the year of *wuchen*, the central phase is Fire, governed by Grand Zhi (*Taizhi*). Fire-qi is in excess, and this is called "Blazing Radiance" (*Hexi*). When qi triumphs, the lung viscus is afflicted, and over time, the large intestine is also affected. Armored creatures (*jiachong*) suffer calamity. Autumn and winter are warm, while summer is scorching. However, its transformative governance is only half—why? Because above, it encounters the Water of the Heavenly Controller (*Sitian*), which restrains half of Fire’s power.

In the transformation of heat, seven follows the completion number—this is the standard measure of governance, with no exception. Such is the mandate. The years of *wuxu* all follow this pattern.

In the year of *jisi*, the central phase is Earth, governed by Minor Gong (*Shaogong*). Disaster befalls the five palaces, with the fifth palace being the Central Palace, corresponding to the *Kun* hexagram’s position. In humans, it governs the spleen; in the four seasons, it aligns with summer; among creatures, it rules the protected insects (*baochong*). When Earth is deficient, it is called "Humble Orchid" (*Beilan*). Thus, the transformative mandate of the four seasons’ qi is not upright, and Wood comes to triumph. Great winds arise frequently, and the people suffer from abdominal fullness, jaundice, and edema. The qi of rain and dampness fails to transform, and the protected insects perish prematurely. When the triumph runs deep, Metal comes to counterbalance. At the arrival of this counterbalance, white dust rises on all sides, and the force of stern killing arrives. Leaves wither and fall, and the people suffer afflictions of the liver viscus, while the furred creatures languish in distress. Once the counterbalance subsides, the spleen’s qi remains depleted. Only in the ninth month, *jiaxu*, when *ji* gains the power of *jia* and achieves its stem convergence, does it return to the Central Palace. The transformation of rain follows the number five, and the governance of *sihai* years aligns with this pattern.

In the year of *gengwu*, the central phase is Metal, governed by Grand Shang (*Taishang*). When Metal-qi is in excess, it is called "Firm Completion" (*Jiancheng*). When qi triumphs, the liver is afflicted. White dust rises on all sides, and the killing qi gathers like clouds. The generative qi fails to govern, while the consumptive qi prevails. Furred creatures suffer greatly, and grasses and trees bloom late. The people fall ill with blockages in the flanks and limbs, sinew contractions, blurred vision, and mood swings. Though its transformative governance brings calamity, it does not reach extreme severity—it attains only half its power. Why is this?

The above sees the presence of Lesser Yin Sovereign Fire governing, and the year *wu* is also Fire, thus Metal’s command is half diminished, and Wood’s calamity is likewise minor. The dryness transformation follows the completion number nine, as does the year *gengzi*.

The year *zi* is Water, and Metal-qi accords with it, so its calamity reaches full triumph. The emotional transformation follows the completion number nine. In the year *xinwei*, the central phase is Water, governed by Lesser Yu, with calamity in the first palace. The first palace is the *kan* position, corresponding in humans to the kidneys, and in the four seasons to winter. The creatures are scaled creatures. When Water-qi fails to flow, it is called "dried streams." Then Earth comes to triumph, and dampness prevails greatly. The long-qi is used in reverse, and its transformation is swift. Summer heat and rain arrive frequently, and the people suffer from abdominal fullness, heavy limbs, watery diarrhea, cold sores, flowing water that does not freeze, pain in the waist and thighs, discomfort in the popliteal fossa, thighs, and knees, vexation, foot weakness, reversal cold in the feet, pain in the soles, and in severe cases, swelling of the instep. When the visceral qi is not upright, the resurgence arises. Wood comes to rescue Water, and great winds arrive violently. Grasses are laid flat, and trees shed their leaves. Growth is not fresh, complexions change frequently, sinews and bones contract together, flesh becomes flaccid and paralyzed, vision is dim, objects appear sparkling, muscles twitch, and qi erupts. Pain arises in the diaphragm and heart. The Yellow qi is thus diminished, and the five grains fail to sprout. When the resurgence subsides, Water-qi is pacified. By the seventh month, *bingshen*, Water’s governance is the upright *yu*. The cold transformation follows the generative number one. The perverse transformation is called "when the seasonal command is not upright." The command of *xinchou* is thus.

In the year *renshen*, the central phase is Water, governed by Grand Jue. Wood-qi is in excess, and it is called "Burgeoning Growth." Then great winds uproot and break, and the qi punishes the Spleen viscus, eventually reaching the Stomach. As Wind-qi spreads, the Spleen Earth is afflicted. The people fall ill with diarrhea, reduced appetite, heavy limbs, vexation, rumbling intestines, and fullness in the flanks. The transformative qi governs alone. Insects and birds take flight, and grasses and trees are unsettled. In severe cases, they are shaken and fall. There is pain in the flanks and vomiting. The wind transformation follows the completion number eight. This is the measure of perverse transformation, when the upright command loses its season. In the year *renyin*, the qi is even more severe. It is also called a "yearly convergence," for *yin* Wood and *ren* Wood converge. In the year *guiyou*, the central phase is Fire, governed by Lesser Zhi, with calamity in the ninth palace. The ninth palace is the southern *li* position, corresponding in humans to the Heart, and in the four seasons to summer. Here, Fire-qi is insufficient, and it is called "Hidden Brightness." The Heart viscus is inherently weak, and the summer command is not upright. Feathered creatures perish prematurely. Then Water comes to triumph. When Water arrives, its triumph brings great cold. The long-qi is not upright, and things are scorched and decline. The cold is so severe that Yang-qi fails to transform, and flourishing beauty is broken. The people suffer from pain in the chest, fullness in the flanks and limbs, pain in the flanks, back, shoulders, and between the scapulae, and pain in the inner arms. Depression and darkness cloud the Heart. When the triumph reaches its depth, Fire has a child—Earth—who comes to its rescue. The mother then overcomes the triumph. Dust and gloom gather, and great rains arrive. Black qi is thus subdued. The people suffer from sudden blindness, abdominal fullness, inability to eat or drink, internal cold, rumbling intestines, diarrhea, cramping pain, atrophy, and numbness. Their feet cannot support their bodies. When the resurgence subsides, Fire-qi begins to balance. In the fifth month after, *wuwu*, *gui* meets its stem-branch Fire counterpart and returns to the upright *zhi*. The heat transformation follows the generative number two. The perverse transformation is called "losing the upright command." The year *guimao* is likewise.

In the year *jiaxu*, the central phase is Earth, governed by Grand Gong. Earth-qi is in excess, and it is called "Abundant Mound." Earth enacts the rain command. Then dust, summer heat, and dampness gather. The Great Void is filled with dust, darkness, clouds, and rain. When the seasonal qi is excessive, it harms the Kidneys, eventually reaching the Bladder. The transformative qi is in excess, while the visceral qi does not govern. The people fall ill with qi reversal, impotence, cold in the foot meridians, lack of strength, loss of essence, and scaled creatures suffer. When qi is abundant, Wind arises to triumph and shift. The people suffer from eye diseases, blockages, and jaundice. When the above triumphs, Heaven’s command is not followed. The rain transformation follows the number five. It is also called perverse transformation, when governance loses its season. The year *jiachen* is the opposite transformation of this command.

In the year *yihai*, the central phase is Metal, governed by Upright Shang. It is a balanced qi, and it is called "Judicious Balance." The so-called balanced qi refers to the third month, when *gengchen* arrives early, meeting the stem’s virtue. *Yi*, the yielding, meets *geng*, the firm, and the qi returns to its upright position. Fire has not yet attained its kingly phase, so it does not triumph but is first balanced. When Fire does not triumph, Water does not resurge. Moreover, *hai* is Water, and it also gains the year’s power, so Fire does not triumph. The emotional transformation follows the generative number four. The upright transformation is called "no other command," for it follows its own transformation in due time. In the year *yisi*, Fire comes to slightly triumph, for *si* is Fire and can assist the triumph. Then, during the mid-season qi of the second month, Sovereign Fire’s seasonal transformation is called "Fire comes to triumph." Metal-qi triumphs, and Lesser Shang follows Greater Zhi. The triumph does not last long and does not await Water’s resurgence. Instead, in the third month, *gengchen*, *yi* meets *geng*, and the qi is complete. Metal returns to Upright Shang, and the qi is balanced.

In the year *bingzi*, the central phase is Water, governed by Grand Yu. Water-qi is in excess, and it is called "Flowing Overflow." When Water is abundant, it overcomes the Controller of Heaven, and the transformative command is not followed. *Bing* is the Water phase, the stem’s firmness, and it is also Water. Greater Yang governs Heaven. When it is excessive, Water-qi confronts Fire, and the long command is not followed. This is the triumph of the visceral qi. The Heart viscus is afflicted, eventually reaching the Small Intestine. Feathered creatures suffer calamity, while scaled creatures thrive. The cold transformation follows the completion number six. It is also called perverse transformation, when summer loses its seasonal uprightness. The year *bingwu* differs only slightly. *Wu* is Fire, and Fire gains the year’s power. Though *bing* is the phase’s firmness, Water triumphs. It is said that Fire resides in the southern *wu* position, gaining the upright *li* qi’s assistance. Thus, the summer command is transformed, the Heart viscus is not afflicted, feathered creatures do not suffer calamity, and the heat transformation attains its upright transformation. There is no other perverse qi that arrives.

In the year *dingchou*, the central Wood phase governs with the upright *jiao* tone, for Wood’s virtue attains balanced qi—its name is "Spreading Harmony." What does this mean? It does not await Metal’s triumph but first achieves alignment with the celestial tally. At the onset of the initial qi, it encounters the first month *renyin*; though *ding* is Wood’s yielding phase and *chou* a yin year, *ren* is Wood’s firm phase, and its virtue aligns with *ding*. When *ding* meets *ren*, its qi is restored in full, so Metal does not triumph, Fire does not counter, and Wood’s virtue assumes the upright *jiao* tone, its generative qi prevailing. The seasonal command of Wood does not harm Earth, and the people enjoy well-being. Shelled creatures, furred creatures, and armored creatures each flourish in their season. The wind transformation follows the generative number three—this is the day of upright transformation. In accordance with the seasons, the governance does not lose its timely order.

In the year *dingwei*, the qi transformations and phase movements align with Heaven, following the governance of *dingchou*.

In the year *wuyin*, the central Fire phase governs with the excessive *zhi* tone, for Fire’s qi is in excess—its name is "Blazing Radiance." The phase movement precedes Heaven, arriving prematurely, hence it is called "preceding Heaven." Moreover, the phase aligns in virtue with Heaven, termed a "celestial tally." Above, Lesser Yang’s ministerial Fire presides over Heaven, so the phase and Heaven share Fire’s nature, and its qi is intensely abundant. Scorching heat spreads, the Metal viscus Lung is afflicted, and the people suffer from malaria, shortness of breath, coughing, wheezing, blood overflow, diarrhea, constipation, dryness, deafness, internal heat, shoulder and back heat, and in severe cases, chest pain, rib and limb fullness, pain in the chest, back, shoulders, and scapulae, pain in the inner arms, bodily heat, bone pain, and spreading damp-heat. The gathering qi does not prevail, while the growing qi alone flourishes, manifesting Fire’s triumph. The heat transformation follows the completion number seven—this is the day of perverse transformation, when governance loses its timely order.

In the year *wushen*, there is a slight difference: *shen* is Metal, which assists the Lung. Though the Lung suffers Fire’s punishment, its qi is somewhat steadfast, and the people’s illnesses are halved—hence the slight difference. The remaining commands follow this pattern.

In the year *jimao*, the central Earth phase governs with the diminished *gong* tone, for Earth’s qi is insufficient, bringing calamity to the fifth palace—the fifth palace is the Center. In humans, it corresponds to the Spleen. Its qi divides into the four qi, and its creatures are shelled—its name is "Humble Orchid." Wood then comes to punish: the Wood phase’s wind triumphs over Earth, and wind prevails greatly. The transformative qi loses its command, grasses and trees flourish luxuriantly, swaying violently, flowering but bearing no fruit. The people suffer from undigested diarrhea, cholera, heaviness, abdominal pain, strained sinews and bones, and aching muscles. The triumph is extreme. Metal’s child comes to counter, and when the counter arrives, the gathering governance is severe: grasses and trees wither and fade, sudden pain strikes the chest and abdomen, pulling downward to the lower abdomen, with frequent sighing. Insects consume sweet and yellow things. Qi invades the Spleen, grains rot, and people eat little and lose their meals. When the counter subsides, Earth’s qi is not yet upright. Later, in the ninth month *jiaxu*, Earth returns to the upright *gong* palace. The rain transformation follows the number five—this is the day of perverse transformation, when the command loses its upright order.

In the year *jiyou*, it differs from this year: *you* is Metal, which fears triumph, so Wood’s triumph is slight.

In the year *gengchen*, the central Metal phase governs with the excessive *shang* tone, for Metal’s qi is in surplus—its name is "Firm Completion." With Metal’s qi in surplus, the generative qi withers, and the gathering qi brings destruction: white dust rises on all sides, grasses and trees wither and fall, forests become desolate, and dryness parches the fields white. The people suffer in the Liver, furred creatures are distressed, and there is rib-side qi block, difficult urination, dribbling urine, blurred vision, and muscle spasms. The dryness transformation follows the completion number nine—this is the day of perverse transformation, when the spring command loses its governance.

The phase movement in *gengxu* follows this pattern.

In the year *xinsi*, the central Water phase governs with the diminished *yu* tone, for Water’s qi is insufficient, bringing calamity to the first palace—the first palace is the northern *kan* position. In humans, it corresponds to the Kidneys, and its creatures are scaled. Water’s decline is called "Dried Flow," meaning desiccation and exhaustion, for Earth’s phase triumphs over Water. Earth’s phase brings rain, hence it is called the "rain transformation’s triumph." When the triumph arrives, by the fourth qi, great rains pour ceaselessly, the Kidney viscus is endangered, and eventually the Bladder is afflicted. Scaled creatures are distressed, and Water’s peril is dire. Wood then comes to counter the triumph: great winds arise repeatedly, stirring dust high, breaking and toppling forests, and hurling sand and stones. Thus, Earth’s qi is depleted, the Spleen viscus is afflicted, and shelled creatures suffer calamity. When Wood’s counter subsides, Earth is not yet fully restored. In the seventh month *bingshen*, *xin* meets *bing* in alignment, and Water returns to the upright *yu* tone. Water’s blackness is complete, and the cold transformation follows the number one—this is the day of perverse transformation, when governance loses its timely order.

In the year *xinhai*, there is a slight difference. Why? *Hai* is Water, and though *hai* is a yin year, *hai* Water aligns with *xin* Water’s phase movement in a "yearly convergence," so Water attains balanced qi. Thus, Earth does not triumph, and Wood does not counter—hence it attains the upright *yu* tone. This is the day of upright transformation, when the cold transformation follows the generative number one.

In the year *renwu*, the central Wood phase governs with the excessive *jiao* tone, for Wood’s qi is in surplus—its name is "Arising Life." *Ren* is Wood’s phase movement, the firm phase of the movement. *Wu* is a yang year, and in yang years, excess prevails—hence the qi’s abundance is great. The generative qi’s command is excessive, the movement precedes Heaven, and the wind transformation flourishes. The transformative qi loses its command, and rain and dampness are deficient. The Spleen viscus is afflicted, eventually reaching the Stomach, and shelled creatures do not flourish. The wind transformation follows the completion number eight—this is the perverse qi losing its timely order.

The year *renzi* is likewise.

In the year *guiwei*, the central Fire phase governs with the upright *zhi* tone, for Fire attains balanced qi—its name is "Ascending Clarity." Why? The two Fires on the left and right serve as intervening qi to assist it. Moreover, in the fifth month *wuwu*, it first achieves alignment with the celestial tally. When *gui* meets *wu*, its qi is complete. Having first attained the tally’s power, Water does not triumph—hence it is called balanced qi, for Water does not triumph and Earth does not counter. Fire also does not bring calamity to the ninth palace—hence it is called the upright *zhi* tone.

The heat transformation follows its timely order, and the upright transformation is called "without other influences"—the heat transformation being two, following the generative number. The year *guichou* follows the same pattern as before.

In the year *jiashen*, the central Earth phase governs with the grand *gong* tone, for Earth’s qi is in excess—its name is "Abundant Mound." Earth enacts the rain mandate, and thus the transformative qi flourishes. When the visceral qi is untimely, perverse qi invades the Kidney viscus, eventually reaching the Bladder. Scaled creatures then languish; cold and chill reverse to warmth, while rain and dampness prevail. The people suffer from abdominal pain, reversal counterflow, dispiritedness, heaviness of body, vexation and oppression, and in severe cases, muscle atrophy, inability to lift the feet, frequent cramps, pain beneath the soles, fluid retention causing central fullness, poor digestion, and inability to raise the four limbs. The rain transformation being five marks the day of perverse transformation, for the visceral qi is not upright. The year *jiayin* differs from this. Why? *Yin* belongs to Wood, and Wood can restrain Earth—this is the balanced qi. Thus, the visceral qi is balanced, scaled creatures naturally flourish, and the Kidney qi is harmonized. This is called the day of upright transformation, hence it is free from other perverse influences.

In the year *yiyou*, the central Metal phase governs with the upright *shang* tone, for Metal attains balanced qi—its name is "Prudent Equilibrium." The seventh palace suffers no calamity; Fire’s triumph does not arrive, and Water’s retaliation does not come. Furred creatures flourish, and the Lung viscus’s qi is at peace. Why? Though *yi* is the yielding phase of Metal’s qi, and *you* is a yin year, *you* is the Metal position of the western direction, and Metal’s qi assists it—hence it attains balanced qi. The long qi also does not restrain the generative qi, and the killing qi is naturally upright. The cool transformation being four follows the generative number—this is called the day of upright transformation without other perverse influences. The year *yimao* differs from this. In that year, the Metal phase is in minor *shang*, for Metal’s qi is insufficient—its name is "Following Transformation." Fire then gains the second qi, and the sovereign Fire’s phase comes to prevail in its division, bringing sweltering heat. Furred creatures perish, and the Lung falls ill. Since Fire’s triumph is insufficient, Water has not yet acted in retaliation to balance its qi. Why? In the third month *gengchen*, *yi* meets *geng* and harmonizes with its celestial virtue. The Metal phase attains the upright *shang* tone, and its qi is thus balanced, ensuring the killing qi does not lose its mandate. The clear transformation being four follows the generative number—this is called the day of perverse transformation with other influences.

In the year *bingxu*, the central Water phase governs with the grand *yu* tone, for Water’s qi is in excess—its name is "Flowing Overflow." Water, strengthened by the firmness of *bingxu*, with *xu* bearing the Greater Yang above, aligns with cold. Its qi confronts Fire, and the long qi loses governance; scorching heat thus wanes. Sudden chills arise intermittently, and the visceral qi flourishes. Frost and hail appear, its mandate is cold clouds and biting chill, and feathered creatures forget their nature. The visceral illness becomes perilous, eventually reaching the Small Intestine. The people suffer from heart heat and vexation, heart dryness and palpitations, yin counterflow, cold in the upper, lower, and middle, delirium and forgetfulness, and heart pain. Cold qi arrives early. The cold transformation being one, six in the generative and completion numbers, and two transformations merging with the celestial mandate—this is called the day of perverse transformation losing its governance. The year *bingchen* follows the same pattern.

In the year *dinghai*, the central Wood phase governs with the upright *jiao* tone, for Wood attains balanced qi—its name is "Spreading Harmony." Wood’s qi does not harm the third palace. Why? Though *ding* is the yielding phase of Wood’s qi, and *hai* is a yin year, in the first month *renyin*, *ding* meets *ren* and harmonizes with its celestial virtue—hence it attains balanced qi. Thus, the phase achieves celestial harmony, and Wood’s qi is complete. Metal does not triumph, and Fire does not retaliate. Wood also does not harm Earth’s mandate, allowing each seasonal mandate to attain its proper transformation—hence it is called the day of upright transformation. The wind transformation being three follows the generative number. The upright *dingsi* year follows this same mandate.

In the year *wuzi*, the central Fire phase governs with the grand *zhi* tone, for Fire’s qi is in excess—its name is "Brilliant Scorch." Above, it joins virtue with the Lesser Yin sovereign Fire—this is called a "Celestial Tally." Fire enacts the summer heat mandate, and thus scorching heat prevails greatly. The summer mandate is excessive, its mutation is oppressive steam, and its manifestation is blazing brilliance. As such, the Heart’s qi is in excess, and perverse heat scorches the Lung viscus, eventually reaching the Large Intestine. Furred creatures do not thrive, the killing qi loses governance, and the stern killing lacks authority. The summer heat transformation follows the completion number. The year *wuwu* is called the "Grand Son’s Celestial Tally," a triple convergence. That is, *wu* Fire phase above joins the Lesser Yin sovereign Fire, and *wu* is the southern direction’s position—thus, the three Fire positions join virtue. Its transformation becomes even more severe, and this is called the day of perverse transformation where autumn loses its uprightness.

In the year *jichou*, the central Earth phase governs with the minor *gong* tone, for Earth’s qi is insufficient—it brings calamity to the fifth palace. The fifth palace is the central palace, corresponding in humans to the Spleen, in the hexagrams to *Kun*, in the governing qi to the fourth qi, and in creatures to shelled creatures. Earth being insufficient, its name is "Humble Supervision." Earth enacts the rain mandate, and the damp transformation is thus deficient. Wood then comes to restrain it, and Wood enacts the wind mandate—thus, the wind transformation prevails in triumph. When this triumph arrives, it comes early with the first qi. During the time of wind and Wood, transformation is upright, and the Spleen falls ill, eventually reaching the Stomach. Shelled creatures are severely afflicted, the fourth qi is again deficient, and Earth is in peril. Metal then arrives, bringing dryness in retaliation to triumph over Wood. Wood in turn declines, and the Liver falls ill, eventually reaching the Gallbladder. Earth then becomes tranquil, the Spleen’s illness is cured, shelled creatures are relieved, and by the ninth month *jiaxu*, *ji* meets *jia* to harmonize its celestial virtue. Earth returns to the upright *gong* tone’s position, called "Rain and Wind," where triumph and retaliation coincide. The measure of perverse transformation—perverse transformation is the name for mutual restraint and triumph. The rain transformation being five, the year *jiwei* follows this same upright pattern.

In the year *gengyin*, the central Metal phase governs with the upright *shang* tone, for Metal attains balanced qi—its name is "Prudent Equilibrium." *Yin* is yang, and *geng* governs excess, so why is it called balanced qi? Because above, it meets the Lesser Yang ministerial Fire as the Celestial Controller, and below, it is restrained by what it encounters—thus, the Celestial Controller punishes the phase, and the phase cannot be excessive. Hence, its excess is tempered to appear balanced. Its qi also harms the Liver, though this is but a minor calamity. Furred creatures are slightly afflicted, and the spring mandate is clear and dry.

The Dryness transformation being nine follows the completion number, and the perverse transformation is not severe.

In the year *gengshen*, Metal attains excess, following the Greater *shang* tone of Metal—its name is "Firm Completion," for *shen* Metal serves as its assistant. The Metal qi harms the Liver and, over time, affects the Gallbladder. The mandate of generative qi does not kill, yet Metal qi being excessive, the Dryness transformation follows its decree.

In the year *xinmao*, the central Water phase governs with the Lesser *yu* tone, and the Water qi is insufficient, bringing calamity to the first palace—the first palace being the *kan* position of the north. In humans, Water corresponds to the Kidneys. Water being insufficient, its name is "Dried Flow," meaning desiccation and exhaustion. Thus, the Earth qi arrives to triumph, punishing the Water, and above, the rain mandate is enacted—its name is the "Rain Transformation Triumph." The triumph reaches its peak in the fourth qi, for Earth attains its timely transformation and thus prevails. The Great Void is veiled in dust and haze, clouds churn in turmoil, and the rain mandate transforms repeatedly. The Kidney viscus falls ill, and over time, the Bladder is affected. Scaled creatures suffer grievously, the winter mandate turns warm, flowing waters do not freeze, and the peril of Water’s distress invites Wood’s restorative punishment. Wood, being Water’s child, enacts the Wind mandate—its name is the "Wind Transformation," where triumph and restoration coincide. Thus, the great wind restores its triumph over rain. Earth, corresponding to the Spleen, falls ill in turn, and shelled creatures suffer misfortune—the Earth qi is endangered. As such, the Earth qi begins to wane, and by the seventh month *bingshen*, Water regains its upright *yu* tone. The Cold transformation being one follows the generative number, and the perverse transformation is called "Loss of Upright Mandate." The year *xinyou* is likewise.

In the year *renchen*, the central Wood phase governs with the Greater *jue* tone, and the Wood qi is in surplus—its name is "Burgeoning Growth." Its qi is abundant, and Wood being excessive, the Wind mandate prevails. Winds arise in great force, stirring and snapping, howling and tearing, their power wreaking havoc. When the qi overreaches, it harms the Spleen and, over time, affects the Stomach. Shelled creatures fail to thrive, and the transformative qi does not fulfill its mandate. The Wind transformation being eight follows the completion number, and the perverse transformation is called "Loss of Upright Mandate." The mandate of *renxu* likewise follows this year’s decree.

In the year *guisi*, the central Fire phase governs with the upright *zhi* tone, and Fire attains balanced qi—its name is "Ascendant Peace." Though *si* is a yin year and *gui* is yielding, first, *si* is Fire and is also called a "Yearly Convergence"; second, Water has not attained its timely transformation; third, in the fifth month *wuwu*, *gui* meets *wu* in union, their stems harmonizing—thus, it attains balanced qi. Since Water does not arrive to triumph nor Fire to restore, the Fire mandate follows its season. The Heat transformation being two follows the generative number, and the upright transformation is called "Following the Season’s Upright Mandate."

In the year *guihai*, the central Fire phase governs with the Lesser *zhi* tone, and Fire is insufficient, bringing calamity to the ninth palace—the ninth palace being the *li* position of the south. In humans, it corresponds to the Heart, and creatures are feathered. Fire being insufficient, its name is "Concealed Brightness," for *hai* is Water, differing from *si*. Thus, Water gains the year’s power and arrives to enact triumph—sudden cold ensues. When triumph is questioned, the people suffer in the Heart and, over time, in the Small Intestine, while feathered creatures fall ill. When the triumph is extreme, Earth arrives to restore its triumph. Water, distressed by the triumph, causes the Kidneys to fall ill in turn, affecting scaled creatures. By the fifth month *wuwu*, Fire regains its upright *zhi* tone, its qi now balanced, and the perverse transformation is called "Loss of Governance Mandate."

*The Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi in the Plain Questions, Scroll Two* concludes.

*The Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi in the Plain Questions, Scroll Three*
*As Recorded by Master Qi Xuan*

---

[Textual variants noted in collation are incorporated into the translation below.]

When Wood is insufficient, its name is "Veiled Brilliance." In humans, it corresponds to the Liver, and creatures are hairy. Metal, gaining the year’s power, arrives to enact triumph—sudden winds arise. When triumph is questioned, the people suffer in the Liver and, over time, in the Gallbladder, while hairy creatures fall ill. When the triumph is extreme, Fire arrives to restore its triumph. Metal, distressed by the triumph, causes the Lungs to fall ill in turn, affecting feathered creatures. By the third month *bingchen*, Wood regains its upright *zhi* tone, its qi now balanced, and the perverse transformation is called "Loss of Governance Mandate."

When Earth is insufficient, its name is "Lowly Oversight." In humans, it corresponds to the Spleen, and creatures are naked. Wood, gaining the year’s power, arrives to enact triumph—sudden dampness ensues. When triumph is questioned, the people suffer in the Spleen and, over time, in the Stomach, while naked creatures fall ill. When the triumph is extreme, Metal arrives to restore its triumph. Wood, distressed by the triumph, causes the Liver to fall ill in turn, affecting hairy creatures. By the ninth month *renxu*, Earth regains its upright *gong* tone, its qi now balanced, and the perverse transformation is called "Forgetting the Mandate."

When Metal is insufficient, its name is "Hidden Clarity." In humans, it corresponds to the Lungs, and creatures are feathered. Fire, gaining the year’s power, arrives to enact triumph—sudden heat arises. When triumph is questioned, the people suffer in the Lungs and, over time, in the Large Intestine, while feathered creatures fall ill. When the triumph is extreme, Water arrives to restore its triumph. Fire, distressed by the triumph, causes the Heart to fall ill in turn, affecting winged creatures. By the ninth month *yihai*, Metal regains its upright *shang* tone, its qi now balanced, and the perverse transformation is called "Forgetting the Mandate."

When Water is insufficient, its name is "Concealed Brightness." In humans, it corresponds to the Kidneys, and creatures are scaled. Earth, gaining the year’s power, arrives to enact triumph—sudden cold ensues. When triumph is questioned, the people suffer in the Kidneys and, over time, in the Bladder, while scaled creatures fall ill. When the triumph is extreme, Wood arrives to restore its triumph. Earth, distressed by the triumph, causes the Spleen to fall ill in turn, affecting naked creatures. By the fifth month *wuwu*, Water regains its upright *yu* tone, its qi now balanced, and the perverse transformation is called "Loss of Governance Mandate."

**Heavenly Origin’s Fixed Transformations Record**

The term *sitian* (Controller of Heaven) means "upright"; it denotes serving the uprightness of Heaven. The *zuoyou* (Left and Right) follow the upright, subordinate to the Controller of Heaven, thus accompanying the Controller to serve Heaven’s uprightness. Their names are the *wenqi* (Interrogating Qi), for the root qi follows Heaven’s emptiness and periodically interrogates the transformations of its mandate. This is the interrogating transformation of the Controller of Heaven’s mandate, hence the name *wenqi*.

Thus, some harmonize with Heaven, while others do not; some transform in parallel with Heaven’s mandate, while others overpower it and refuse transformation. Some precede Heaven’s mandate, others follow it; some arrive early in interrogation, others late; some come early and depart early, others come late and depart late; some come early but depart late, others come late but depart early. Some fear Heaven’s mandate and do not arrive; some respond on the left but not the right, or on the right but not the left; some respond on both sides, others on neither. Some follow the Southern Regulator, others the Northern Regulator. Such is the non-uniformity of Heaven’s mandate. Though predetermined, it is also governed by the minutely detailed fixed records, for Heaven’s mandate must transform—if it does not, the reasons are expounded below.

The *tianyuan* (Heavenly Origin’s Six Qi) are *jueyin*, *shaoyin*, *taiyin*, *shaoyang*, *yangming*, and *taiyang*. *Jueyin* governs the *sihai* (巳亥) cycle; *shaoyin* the *ziwu* (子午) cycle; *taiyin* the *chouwei* (丑未) cycle; *shaoyang* the *yinshen* (寅申) cycle; *yangming* the *maoyou* (卯酉) cycle; and *taiyang* the *chenxu* (辰戌) cycle. These are the numerical cycles of yin and yang’s alternating fixed records, thus they end and begin anew.

*Jueyin* is Wood. Its mandate is wind; its nature, warmth; its virtue, harmony; its distress, uprooting and tearing; its triumph, breaking and falling; its retaliation, furious gales. Its transformation is three eights; its creatures, furred; its organ, the Liver. Its diseases are tremors, dizziness, and tendon spasms. Its color is green; its flavor, sour; its odor, rancid. It nourishes the sinews; its indicator, the eyes; its season, spring. Its star is Jupiter; its movement, the left flank. Its symbol is the Azure Dragon; its pulse, string-like and long. Its trigram is *Zhen* (震); its positions, *yin* (寅) and *mao* (卯). Its grain is green; its fruit, the plum; its livestock, the parrot. Its warnings are falling and ruin; its disasters strike the Third Palace. Its spirit is the *hun*; its fluid, tears. It governs *si* (巳) and *hai* (亥); its phase aligns with *ding* and *ren*.

*Shaoyin* is Sovereign Fire. Its mandate is heat; its nature, warmth; its virtue, benevolence; its distress, oppressive steam; its triumph, extreme heat; its retaliation, stifling sultriness. Its transformation is two sevens; its creatures, feathered; its organ, the Heart. Its diseases are fright and palpitations. Its color is red; its flavor, bitter; its odor, scorched. It nourishes the vessels; its indicator, the tongue; its season, summer. Its star is the Lesser Blaze, resembling Mars—red and small. Its movement is at the heart; its symbol, the Vermilion Bird; its pulse, surging and vast. Its trigram is *Li* (離); its positions, *si* (巳) and *wu* (午). Its grain is cinnabar; its fruit, the apricot; its livestock, the sheep. Its warnings are vexing heat; its disasters strike the Ninth Palace. Its spirit is the *shen*; its fluid, sweat. It governs *zi* (子) and *wu* (午); its phase aligns with *wu* and *gui*. It does not govern the phase qi, for Sovereign Fire is nominal and does not command the Five Phases.

*Taiyin* is Earth. Its mandate is rain; its nature, moistening; its virtue, gentleness; its distress, dusty obscurity; its triumph, ceaseless downpours; its retaliation, sleet and hail. Its transformation is five; its creatures, naked; its organ, the Spleen. Its diseases are fullness, belching, and jaundice. Its color is yellow; its flavor, sweet; its odor, fragrant. It nourishes the flesh; its indicator, the lips; its season, late summer. Its star is Saturn; its movement, at the navel; its symbol, the Curved Array. Its pulse is moderate; its trigram, *Kun* (坤); its positions, *chen* (辰), *xu* (戌), *chou* (丑), and *wei* (未). Its grain is millet; its fruit, the jujube; its livestock, the ox. Its warnings are dimness and dullness; its disasters strike the Fifth Palace. Its spirit is the *yi*; its fluid, drool. It governs *chou* (丑) and *wei* (未); its phase aligns with *jia* and *ji*.

*Shaoyang* is Ministerial Fire. Its mandate is summerheat; its nature, blazing; its virtue, fierce intensity; its distress, boiling and seething; its triumph, scorching stone; its retaliation, molten metal. Its transformation is two sevens; its creatures, winged; its organ, the Pericardium. Its diseases are madness and mania. Its color is red; its flavor, bitter; its odor, scorched. It nourishes the blood; its indicator, the tongue; its season, summer. Its star is Mars; its movement, *Laogong* (the center of the palm). Its symbol is the Vermilion Bird; its pulse, hook-like. Its trigram is *Li* (離); its positions, *si* (巳) and *wu* (午). Its grain is cinnabar; its fruit, the apricot; its livestock, the sheep. Its warnings are flipping and entanglement; its disasters strike the Ninth Palace. Its spirit is the *zhi*; its fluid, sweat. It governs *yin* (寅) and *shen* (申); its phase aligns with *wu* and *gui*.

*Yangming* is Metal. Its mandate is dryness; its nature, freezing; its virtue, clarity; its distress, stern killing; its triumph, withering and decay; its retaliation, flying ruin. Its transformation is four nines; its creatures, shelled; its organ, the Lungs. Its diseases are wheezing, coughing, and sneezing. Its color is white; its flavor, pungent; its odor, fishy. It nourishes the skin and hair; its indicator, the nose; its season, autumn. Its star is Venus; its movement, the right flank. Its symbol is the White Tiger; its pulse, floating. Its trigram is *Dui* (兌); its positions, *shen* (申) and *you* (酉). Its grain is white; its fruit, the peach; its livestock, the horse. Its warnings are frost and dew; its disasters strike the Seventh Palace. Its spirit is the *po*; its fluid, nasal mucus. It governs *mao* (卯) and *you* (酉); its phase aligns with *yi* and *geng*.

*Taiyang* is Water. Its mandate is cold; its nature, freezing; its virtue, biting chill; its distress, piercing cold; its triumph, dense frost; its retaliation, hail. Its transformation is six; its creatures, scaled; its organ, the Kidneys. Its diseases are wilting and reversal. Its color is black; its flavor, salty; its odor, putrid. It nourishes the bones; its indicator, the ears; its season, winter. Its star is Mercury; its movement, below the navel. Its symbol is the Dark Warrior; its pulse, stone-like. Its trigram is *Kan* (坎); its positions, *hai* (亥) and *zi* (子). Its grain is black; its fruit, the chestnut; its livestock, the hare. Its warnings are frost and snow; its disasters strike the First Palace. Its spirit is the *zhi*; its fluid, spittle. It governs *chen* (辰) and *xu* (戌); its phase aligns with *bing* and *xin*.

Why does *Jueyin* govern *si* (巳) and *hai* (亥)? It is called *Jueyin* Wood, and Wood is born in *hai*, thus it rightfully governs *hai* and corresponds in transformation to *si*. Though *mao* (卯) is the proper position for Wood, it is the domain where *Yangming* Metal undergoes transformation, following the source of generation to align with governance.

Why does *Shaoyin* govern *zi* (子) and *wu* (午)? It is called *Shaoyin* as the Sovereign Fire, occupying the honored position. Thus, it rightfully claims the southern *Li* position, governing *wu* in direct transformation and corresponding to *zi* in opposition.

Why does *Taiyin* govern *chou* (丑) and *wei* (未)? It is called *Taiyin* as Earth, which rules the Central Palace. Lodged in the *Kun* trigram, *Kun* resides in the southwest, occupying the *wei* position. Thus, it governs *wei* in direct transformation and corresponds to *chou* in opposition.

Why does *Shaoyang* govern *yin* (寅) and *shen* (申)? It is called *Shaoyang* as the position of Ministerial Fire, subordinate to Sovereign Fire. Though *wu* is its position, Sovereign Fire occupies it, for Fire is born in *yin*. Thus, it rightfully governs *yin* and corresponds in transformation to *shen*.

Why does *Yangming* govern *mao* (卯) and *you* (酉)? It is called *Yangming* as Metal, and *you* is the western position of Metal. Thus, it rightfully governs *you* and corresponds in transformation to *mao*.

Why does *Taiyang* govern *chen* (辰) and *xu* (戌)? It is called *Taiyang* as Water. Though Water has its position in *zi*, it is the domain where Sovereign Fire undergoes transformation. Water returns within Earth, for the Six *Wu* reside at the Celestial Gate—*xu* is this. The Six *Si* reside at the Terrestrial Door—*chen* is this. Thus, Water is subsumed by Earth’s function, governing *xu* in direct transformation and corresponding to *chen* in opposition.

What do the transformative commands signify? Why does Wind-Wood transform through three and eight? Why does Fire-Heat transform through two and seven? Why does Earth-Rain transform through five? Why does Dry-Metal transform through four and nine? Why does Cold-Water transform through one and six? These are the numbers of the Five Phases, each possessing generative and completion numbers. Thus, Water is one, Fire two, Wood three, Metal four, and Earth five—these are the generative numbers of the Five Phases. What, then, are the completion numbers? Each is its base number increased by five: Water six, Fire seven, Wood eight, Metal nine, and Earth ten. Earth has no completion number because Earth reigns over the four seasons and does not occupy a fixed direction. Moreover, numbers proceed to ten and then reverse, returning to five. Heaven has nine palaces and cannot reach ten; it turns back at nine.

How are direct and corresponding transformations clarified through root and branch? They arise from their root and are completed through their branch. What is the branch? What is the root? Direct transformation is the root; corresponding transformation is the branch. Thus, *Jueyin* directly transforms in *hai*, Wind transforms through three—this is the root, hence the generative number. It governs *si* in correspondence, Wind transforms through eight—this is the branch, hence the completion number. *Shaoyin* directly governs *wu*, Heat transforms through two—this is the root, hence the generative number. It governs *zi* in correspondence, Heat transforms through seven—this is the branch, hence the completion number. *Taiyin* directly governs *wei* and corresponds to *chou*, both transforming through Rain as five. Earth has no completion number, thus only the generative number. *Shaoyang* directly governs *yin*, Fire transforms through two—this is the root, hence the generative number. It governs *shen* in correspondence, Fire transforms through seven—this is the branch, hence the completion number. *Yangming* directly governs *you*, Dryness transforms through four—this is the root, hence the generative number. It governs *mao* in correspondence, Dryness transforms through nine—this is the branch, hence the completion number. *Taiyang* directly governs *xu*, Cold transforms through one—this is the root, hence the generative number. It governs *chen* in correspondence, Cold transforms through six—this is the branch, hence the completion number. All follow the root in generative numbers and the branch in completion numbers. Direct governance embodies the fullness of transformative command; corresponding governance embodies its emptiness.

What of left and right? They follow governance and are termed *intercalary qi*. For instance, if *Jueyin* governs Heaven, its left is *Shaoyin* and its right *Taiyang*. If *Shaoyin* governs Heaven, its left is *Taiyin* and its right *Jueyin*. If *Taiyin* governs Heaven, its left is *Shaoyang* and its right *Shaoyin*. If *Shaoyang* governs Heaven, its left is *Yangming* and its right *Taiyin*. If *Yangming* governs Heaven, its left is *Taiyang* and its right *Shaoyang*. If *Taiyang* governs Heaven, its left is *Jueyin* and its right *Yangming*. The preceding is left, the following is right. If the Northern Regulator governs Heaven, left lies in the west and right in the east. If the Southern Regulator governs Heaven, left lies in the east and right in the west. All Wood, Fire, Metal, and Water phases are governed by the Northern Regulator, while only Earth is governed by the Southern Regulator.

In all cases of governance, the *in-quarter* and the phase jointly rule the year, except for the left and right intercalary *qi*. The left governs the first three *qi*—the initial, first, and second—corresponding to Wood, Sovereign Fire, and Ministerial Fire. These three *qi* align with the left. The right governs the last three *qi*—the fourth, fifth, and final—corresponding to Earth, Metal, and Water. These three *qi* align with the right.

Why do intercalary *qi* sometimes arrive and sometimes not? For example, if *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire governs Heaven, its left is *Yangming*. *Yangming* is Metal, and Metal retreats from Fire, failing to arrive. The corresponding transformation of Ministerial Fire in Heaven is empty; only if Water phase appears may it arrive slightly. Otherwise, it does not arrive. In all other cases, it arrives.

If *Shaoyin* governs Heaven, its left is *Taiyin*. The left governs the first, second, and third *qi*, and *Taiyin* Earth fears the initial Wood *qi*, thus arriving late. Why? After entering the second *qi*, Wood *qi* retreats from its position, only then arriving—hence its lateness. This principle applies to all others. Moreover, the left intercalary *qi* governs first, while the right intercalary *qi* governs afterward, both harmonizing with Heaven’s governance.

When it arrives, the order of precedence follows the principles described below. If the intercalary *qi* prevails over Heaven, it arrives. If Heaven prevails over the intercalary *qi*, the intercalary *qi* does not arrive—though it may arrive at another time. This also follows the principle of direct correspondence in transformation: the left intercalary *qi* circulates within the *Yang* sequence, aligning with Heaven’s governance, and arrives when it encounters the correct cyclical sign.

How is this observed? For example, in a *zi* year when *Shaoyin* governs Heaven, the left presents *Taiyin*. *Taiyin* is Earth, which governs the fifth palace. When the cyclical sign *jiazi* enters the fifth palace, it arrives. Another example: in a *chou* year when *Taiyin* governs Heaven, the left presents *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire, which governs the ninth palace. When the cyclical sign *jiazi* shifts to *chou* and enters the *Li* palace, *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire arrives. These two examples illustrate the method; all others follow accordingly—examine them carefully and apply.

**Observing Celestial Signs in Accordance with Heavenly Principles**
Whenever the six *qi* descend, ascend, and assume their positions, their arrival is observed through the waxing and waning of *qi*, their compliance or rebellion, and the auspicious or inauspicious omens—all reflected in the changes of the five planets’ forms, the movements of the sun and moon, and celestial phenomena. These are all responses to the *qi* governing Heaven.

At times, *qi* arrives but the star is not seen; at others, the star appears before the *qi* arrives. Some stars deviate from their proper paths or positions, appearing too early or late, growing large when they should be small, or brightening when dim. Sometimes one star appears as two, or *qi* responds while the star does not, or the star fails to appear when expected. The sun and moon may lose their proper courses, brighten excessively, or darken. They may align with *qi* and celestial signs or diverge; stars may cluster, or a star may conjoin the moon while another *qi* disrupts them. They may share the moon’s path, trespass the moon’s horns, or two stars may clash while one diminishes. Two stars may radiate light at each other—all these portend fortune or misfortune, aligning below with above and manifesting clearly in the myriad transformations.

The afflictions of the people, the seasons, and future calamities or blessings are all described in this record.

For instance, when *Shaoyin* Sovereign Fire governs Heaven, it corresponds above to the *Genhuang* star. If this star appears bright and resplendent, it signifies Sovereign Fire’s presence in Heaven. If it does not appear at the expected time, why? Unless it is a year of excessive Water *qi*, its absence is inauspicious. If Water is not excessive that year, the star should appear in Heaven; if not, it is ominous. On Earth, it should appear during the *qi*’s active phase, after half the year has passed. If it fails to appear at either of these times, it is also inauspicious.

If it appears alongside the five planets, it signifies the ruler’s neglect of governance. If it appears near the Metal star (*Venus*), with *Venus* large and bright while *Genhuang* is dim and small, it portends rebellion by military ministers. *Genhuang* resembles *Yinghuo* (*Mars*) but is redder, smaller, and lacks *Mars*’s radiant glow—its natural form is small and faintly red.

If it appears near the Water star (*Mercury*) or Wood star (*Jupiter*), it signals impending rebellion in the ministerial ranks. If near Fire (*Mars*) or Earth (*Saturn*), it also indicates disloyalty. Thus, no star should rival *Genhuang* in brilliance—all such cases signify treason.

If two *Genhuang* stars appear, they are not to be confused with *Mars*. If they are similar in size and indistinguishable, they foretell the rise of an unborn ruler in this world.

If two *Taibai* (*Venus*) stars appear, identical in size and indistinguishable, especially if close together, one is *Venus* and the other the *Gejia* star. Their appearance heralds great warfare.
