When the *yun* transitions, face *si* and gaze forward. First, a yellow qi appears; once it fades, a red qi then flows from *wu* to *shen* and concludes. Its qi is deep, swift in movement, without shifting position, arriving in timely sequence—this is auspicious.

16. *Wuyin*: *Wu* Fire *yun* in excess, *yin* as a yang year. The counting number increases by fifteen—why? *Yin* belongs to *gen*, its number is eight; Fire in excess follows its completion number, seven. Seven and eight together make fifteen, thus adding fifteen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *si* and gaze forward. First, a yellow qi appears; once it fades, a red qi then flows from *wu* to *yin* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in timely sequence without shifting position—this is auspicious.

17. *Gengxu*: *Geng* Metal *yun* in excess, *xu* as a yang year. The counting number increases by fourteen—why? *Xu* belongs to Earth, its number is five; Metal in excess follows its completion number, nine. Nine and five together make fourteen, thus adding fourteen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *shen* and gaze forward. Only a white qi flows from *geng* to *xu* and concludes. Without other colors, arriving in timely sequence without encroaching on other positions—this is auspicious.

18. *Gengchen*: *Geng* Metal *yun* in excess, *chen* as a yang year. The counting number increases by fourteen—why? *Chen* belongs to Earth, its number is five; Metal in excess follows its completion number, nine. Five and nine together make fourteen, thus adding fourteen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *shen* and gaze forward. Only a white qi flows from *geng* to *chen* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in timely sequence without missing its position—this is auspicious.

19. *Renzi*: *Ren* Wood *yun* in excess, *zi* as a yang year. The counting number increases by nine—why? *Zi* belongs to *kan*, its number is one; Wood in excess follows its completion number, eight. Eight and one together make nine, thus adding nine *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *hai* and gaze forward—*ren* is inherently lodged in *hai*. First, a black qi appears; then a blue-green qi flows from *hai* to *zi* and concludes. Its color is profound, swift in movement, without straying to other positions—this is auspicious.

20. *Renwu*: *Ren* Wood *yun* in excess, *wu* as a yang year. The counting number increases by seventeen—why? *Wu* belongs to *li*, its number is nine; Wood in excess follows its completion number, eight. Eight and nine together make seventeen, thus adding seventeen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *hai* and gaze forward. First, a black qi appears; once it fades, a blue-green qi then flows from *ren* to *wu* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in timely sequence without shifting position—this is auspicious.

21. *Renxu*: *Ren* Wood *yun* in excess, *xu* as a yang year. The counting number increases by thirteen—why? *Xu* belongs to Earth, its number is five; Wood in excess follows its number, eight. Eight and five together make thirteen, thus adding thirteen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *hai* and gaze forward. First, a black qi appears; once it fades, a blue-green qi then flows from *ren* to *xu* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in timely sequence without shifting position—this is auspicious.

22. *Renchen*: *Ren* Wood *yun* in excess, *chen* as a yang year. The counting number increases by thirteen—why?

*Chen* belongs to Earth, its number is five; Wood *yun* in excess follows its number, eight. Eight and five together make thirteen, thus adding thirteen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *hai* and gaze forward. First, a black *qi* appears; once it fades, a blue-green *qi* then flows from *ren* to *chen* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in timely sequence without shifting position—this is auspicious.

23. *Renshen*: *Ren* Wood *yun* in excess, *shen* as a yang year. The counting number increases by ten—why? *Shen* belongs to *kun*, its number is two; Wood *yun* in excess follows its number, eight. Two and eight together make ten, thus adding ten *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *hai* and gaze forward. First, a black *qi* appears; once it fades, a blue-green *qi* then flows from *ren* to *shen* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in timely sequence without shifting position—this is auspicious.

24. *Renyin*: *Ren* Wood *yun* in excess, *yin* as a yang year. The counting number increases by sixteen—why? *Yin* belongs to *gen*, its number is eight; Wood *yun* in excess follows its number, eight. Eight and eight together make sixteen, thus adding sixteen *ke*. When the *yun* transitions, face *hai* and gaze forward. First, a black *qi* appears; once it fades, a blue-green *qi* then flows from *ren* to *yin* and concludes. Its color is deep, its movement swift, arriving in due time without encroaching on other positions—this is harmonious.

*Suwen Liuqi Xuanzhu Miyu*, Scroll Five, concludes.

*Suwen Liuqi Xuanzhu Miyu*, Scroll Six
As recorded by Qixuanzi.

**Heavenly Punishment: Excessive *Yun* Chapter**
**Heavenly Judgment: Six Methods of the *Yun* in Yang Years**

Over thirty years in a yang year, when the *yun* should be excessive but is restrained by the *si tian* (Controller of Heaven), it cannot reach full excess. Thus, it is neither excessive nor deficient, resulting in no disasters, no overcoming, and no retaliation—this is because it is not a yin year.

1. *Gengzi*: *Geng* Metal *yun* in excess, *zi* as a yang year. The counting number increases by five—why?
*Zi* belongs to *kan*, its number is one. *Geng* Metal *yun* in a yang year should be excessive, but with *shaoyin* Sovereign Fire as the *si tian* above, it restrains the Metal *yun* below. Fire suppresses Metal’s excess, preventing it from being excessive. Its number follows the generating cycle, thus adding only four. One and four together make five, hence adding five *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *shen* and gaze forward. *Geng* is lodged in *shen*, so only a white *qi* appears, flowing from *geng* to *zi* and concluding. At the end, a red *qi* from Heaven descends to restrain the Metal *qi*, preventing Metal from harming Wood. This is neither a yin year nor an excessive *yun*, hence called the *Heavenly Judgment Yun*.

2. *Gengwu*: *Geng* Metal *yun* should be excessive, *wu* as a yang year. The counting number increases by thirteen—why?
*Wu* belongs to *li*, its number is nine. *Geng* Metal *yun* should be excessive, but with *shaoyin* Sovereign Fire as the *si tian* above, it restrains the Metal *yun* below. Fire suppresses Metal’s excess, preventing it from being excessive. Its number follows the generating cycle, which is four. Four and nine together make thirteen, hence adding thirteen *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *shen* and gaze forward. Only a white *qi* appears, flowing from *geng* to *wu* and concluding. At the end, a red *qi* from Heaven descends to restrain the Metal *qi*, preventing it from being excessive. This is neither a yang nor yin year.

3. *Gengyin*: *Geng* Metal *yun* should be excessive, *yin* as a yang year. The counting number increases by twelve—why?
*Yin* belongs to *gen*, its number is eight. *Geng* Metal *yun* should be excessive, but with *shaoyang* Minister Fire as the *si tian* above, Fire suppresses Metal’s excess below, preventing it from being excessive. Its number follows the generating cycle, which is four. Four and eight together make twelve, hence adding twelve *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *shen* and gaze forward. Only a white *qi* appears, flowing from *geng* to *yin* and concluding. At the end, a red *qi* from Heaven descends to restrain the Metal *yun*, preventing it from being excessive and thus unable to harm Wood.

4. *Gengshen*: *Geng* Metal *yun* should be excessive, *shen* as a yang year. The counting number increases by six—why?
*Shen* belongs to *kun*, its number is two. *Geng* Metal *yun* should be excessive, but with *shaoyang* Minister Fire as the *si tian* above, it restrains the Metal *yun* below. Fire suppresses Metal’s excess, preventing it from being excessive. Following its generating number, which is four, four and two together make six, hence adding six *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *shen* and gaze forward. Only a white *qi* appears, rising straight from *geng* without flowing horizontally. *Geng* is lodged in *shen*, so the *qi* rises directly. Later, a red *qi* from Heaven descends to restrain it, preventing excess. This is not a yin year, and its *qi* cannot harm Wood.

5. *Wuxu*: *Wu* Fire *yun* should be excessive, *xu* as a yang year. The counting number increases by seven—why?
*Xu* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Wu* Fire *yun* should be excessive, but with *taiyang* Cold Water as the *si tian* above, it restrains the Fire *yun* below, preventing excess. Following its generating number, which is two, two and five together make seven, hence adding seven *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *si* and gaze forward. First, a yellow *qi* appears, then a red *qi* flows horizontally, from *wu* to *xu* and concludes. At the end, a black *qi* from Heaven descends to restrain the Fire *qi*, preventing excess.

6. *Wuchen*: *Wu* Fire *yun* should be excessive, *chen* as a yang year. The counting number increases by seven—why?
*Chen* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Wu* Fire *yun* should be excessive, but with *taiyang* Cold Water as the *si tian* above, Water suppresses Fire’s excess below, preventing it from being excessive. Following its generating number, which is two, two and five together make seven, hence adding seven *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *si* and gaze forward. First, a yellow *qi* appears, then a red *qi* flows from *wu* to *chen* and concludes. At the end, a black *qi* from Heaven descends to restrain the Fire *yun*, preventing it from harming Metal. Thus, it is neither excessive nor a yin year.

**Yin Deficiency: Balanced *Yun* Chapter**
**Seventeen Methods of the Insufficient *Yun* in Yin Years**

This pertains to yin years.

1. *Yichou*: *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, *chou* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by nine—why?
*Chou* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is four. Five and four together make nine, hence subtracting nine *ke*. The method for yin years is to decrease. This is an insufficient year.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chen*. *Yi* is lodged in *chen*, so first a green *qi* appears, which is *Yi*’s color. After it fades, a white *qi* flows horizontally from *yi* to *chou* and concludes. Its color is pale, its movement slow. Sometimes a red *qi* arrives simultaneously, or later, indicating Fire’s overcoming. Subsequently, a black *qi* arrives, indicating Water’s retaliation.

2. *Yiwei*: *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, *wei* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by nine—why?
*Wei* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is four. Four and five together make nine, hence subtracting nine *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, a green *qi* appears. After it fades, a white *qi* flows from *yi* to *wei* and concludes. If a red *qi* arrives simultaneously, the overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, the overcoming is mild. If the subsequent black *qi* is large, the retaliation is severe; if small, the retaliation is mild.

3. *Yihai*: *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, *hai* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by ten—why?
*Hai* belongs to *Qian*, its number is six. *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is four. Four and six together make ten, hence subtracting ten *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, a green *qi* appears. After it fades, a white *qi* flows from *yi* to *chen* and concludes. Its color is pale, its movement slow. If a red *qi* arrives simultaneously, the overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, the overcoming is mild. If the subsequent black *qi* is large, the retaliation is great; if small, the retaliation is slight.

4. *Yisi*: *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, *si* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by eight—why?
*Si* belongs to *Xun*, its number is four. *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is four. Four and four together make eight, hence subtracting eight *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, a green *qi* appears. After it fades, a white *qi* flows from *yi* to *si* and concludes. Its color is pale, its movement slow. If a red *qi* arrives simultaneously, the overcoming is deep; if it arrives later, the overcoming is mild. If the subsequent black *qi* is large, the retaliation is great; if small, the retaliation is slight.

5. *Dingchou*: *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient, *chou* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by eight—why?
*Chou* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is three. Three and five together make eight, hence subtracting eight *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. *Ding* is lodged in *wei*. First, a red *qi* appears. After it fades, a green *qi* flows from *ding* to *chou* and concludes. If a white *qi* arrives simultaneously, Metal’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, the overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a red *qi* arrives—if large, Fire’s retaliation is great; if small, Fire’s retaliation is slight, indicating an early return of the *yun*.

6. *Dingwei*: *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient, *wei* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by eight—why?
*Wei* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is three. Three and five together make eight, hence subtracting eight *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a red *qi* appears. After it fades, a green *qi* rises upward, not flowing horizontally to *wei*, for *ding* is lodged in *wei* and thus does not flow horizontally. If a white *qi* appears simultaneously, Metal’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, the overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a red *qi* arrives—if large, Fire’s retaliation is great; if small, Fire’s retaliation is slight.

7. *Dingyou*: *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient, *you* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by ten—why?
*You* belongs to *Dui*, its number is seven. Wood *yun* is insufficient, its number is three. Three and seven together make ten, hence subtracting ten *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a red *qi* appears. After it fades, a green *qi* flows horizontally from *ding* to *you* and concludes. Its color is faint, its movement slow. If a white *qi* arrives simultaneously, Metal’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, the overcoming is slight. Subsequently, a red *qi* arrives—if large, Fire’s retaliation is great; if small, Fire’s retaliation is slight.

8. *Jimao*: *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, *mao* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by eight—why?
*Mao* belongs to *Zhen*, its number is three. *Ji* Earth *yun*’s number is five, but Earth has no completion number, only five. Three and five together make eight, hence subtracting eight *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei*, for *ji* is also lodged in *wei*. First, a purple *qi* appears. After it fades, a yellow *qi* flows horizontally from itself to *mao* and concludes. If a green *qi* arrives simultaneously, Wood’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Wood’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a white *qi* arrives—if large, Metal’s retaliation is great; if small, Metal’s retaliation is slight.

9. *Jiyou*: *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, *you* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by twelve—why?
*You* belongs to *Dui*, its number is seven. *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, its number is five. Seven and five together make twelve, hence subtracting twelve *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a purple *qi* appears. After it fades, a yellow *qi* flows horizontally from itself to *you* and concludes. If a green *qi* arrives simultaneously, Wood’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Wood’s overcoming is slight. Subsequently, a white *qi* arrives—if large, Metal’s retaliation is great; if small, Metal’s retaliation is slight.

10. *Jisi*: *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, *si* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by nine—why?
*Si* belongs to *Xun*, its number is four. *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, its number is five. Four and five together make nine, hence subtracting nine *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a purple *qi* appears. After it fades, a yellow *qi* flows horizontally from itself to *si* and concludes. If a green *qi* arrives simultaneously, Wood’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Wood’s overcoming is slight. Subsequently, a white *qi* arrives—if large, Metal’s retaliation is great; if small, Metal’s retaliation is slight.

11. *Jihai*: *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, *hai* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by eleven—why?
*Hai* belongs to *Qian*, its number is six. *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient, its number is five. Five and six together make eleven, hence subtracting eleven *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a purple *qi* appears. After it fades, a yellow *qi* flows horizontally from itself to *hai* and concludes. If a green *qi* arrives simultaneously, Wood’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Wood’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a white *qi* arrives—if large, Metal’s retaliation is great; if small, Metal’s retaliation is slight.

12. *Xinmao*: *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient, *mao* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by four—why?
*Mao* belongs to *Zhen*, its number is three. Water *yun* is insufficient, following its generating number, which is one. One and three together make four, hence subtracting four *ke*.

When the *yun* transitions, face *xu*. Since *xin* is lodged in *xu*, a warm white color first appears, resembling brown. After it fades, a black *qi* flows horizontally from *xin* to *mao* and concludes. If a yellow *qi* arrives simultaneously, Earth’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Earth’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a green *qi* arrives—if large, Wood’s retaliation is great; if small, Wood’s retaliation is slight.

13. *Xinyou*: *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient, *you* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by eight—why?
*You* belongs to *Dui*, its number is seven. Water *yun* is insufficient, its number is one. One and seven together make eight, hence subtracting eight *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, a warm white color appears. After it fades, a black *qi* flows horizontally from *xin* to *you* and concludes. If a yellow *qi* arrives simultaneously, Earth’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Earth’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a green *qi* arrives—if large, Wood’s retaliation is great; if small, Wood’s retaliation is slight.

14. *Xinsi*: *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient, *si* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by five—why?
*Si* belongs to *Xun*, its number is four. *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient, its number is one. One and four together make five, hence subtracting five *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, a warm white color appears. After it fades, a black *qi* flows horizontally from *xin* to *si* and concludes. If a yellow *qi* arrives simultaneously, Earth’s overcoming is great; if it arrives later, Earth’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a green *qi* arrives—if large, Wood’s retaliation is great; if small, Wood’s retaliation is slight.

15. *Xinhai*: *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient, *hai* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by seven—why?
*Hai* belongs to *Qian*, its number is six. *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient, its number is one. One and six together make seven, hence subtracting seven *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, a warm white color appears. After it fades, a black *qi* flows horizontally from *xin* to *hai* and concludes. If a yellow *qi* arrives simultaneously, Earth’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Earth’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a green *qi* arrives—if large, Wood’s retaliation is great; if small, Wood’s retaliation is slight.

16. *Guichou*: *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient, *chou* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by seven—why?
*Chou* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient, its number is two. Two and five together make seven, hence subtracting seven *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chou* and gaze forward. Since *gui* is lodged in *chou*, a jade-green *qi* first appears. After it fades, a red *qi* rises straight upward to the heavens. For *guichou* alone, it does not flow horizontally. Its color is faint. If a black *qi* appears simultaneously, Water’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Water’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a yellow *qi* arrives—if large, Earth’s retaliation is great; if small, Earth’s retaliation is slight.

17. *Guiwei*: *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient, *wei* as a yin year. The counting number decreases by seven—why?
*Wei* belongs to Earth, its number is five. *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient, its number is two. Two and five together make seven, hence subtracting seven *ke*.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chou* and gaze forward. First, a jade-green *qi* appears. After it fades, a red *qi* flows horizontally from *gui* to *wei*. Its color is pale, and its movement is slow. If a black *qi* arrives simultaneously, Water’s overcoming is severe; if it arrives later, Water’s overcoming is mild. Subsequently, a yellow *qi* arrives—if large, Earth’s retaliation is great; if small, Earth’s retaliation is slight.

The methods of *pingqi* (balanced *qi*) *yun* total sixteen, but here are thirteen. Among the four-year conjunctions, three are removed as they coincide with *tianfu*, hence thirteen.

1. *Jiwei*: *Ji* Earth *yun* is yin and thus insufficient. *Wei* is a yin year, and above it meets *Taiyin* Earth as the *sitian* (celestial controller), harmonizing its virtue, hence called *tianfu*. The *fu* aligns with *Ji* Earth *yun*’s *qi*, making it balanced, thus called *pingqi*. The arriving *qi* matches the *sitian* on the same day. The counting number for *wei* as Earth is five; *ji* gains the balanced *qi* and adds five. One added to one is subtracted, so it is neither insufficient nor excessive.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei*. Since *ji* is lodged in *wei*, a purple *qi* first appears. After it fades, a yellow *qi* rises upward to the heavens, where it meets another yellow *qi* from the sky, thus harmonizing with celestial *qi*. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

2. *Jichou*: *Ji* Earth *yun* is insufficient. *Chou* is a yin year, and above it meets *Taiyin* Earth as the *sitian*, harmonizing its virtue, hence called *tianfu*. The counting number for *chou* is five; Earth *yun* adds five.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a purple *qi* appears. After it fades, a yellow *qi* flows horizontally from itself to *chou*, where it meets a yellow *qi* from the heavens. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

3. *Yiyou*: *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient. *You* is a yin year, and above it meets *Yangming* Metal as the *sitian*, also coinciding with the year’s conjunction. *You* is also Metal. The counting number for *you* is seven; Metal *yun* adds seven.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, a green *qi* appears. After it fades, a white *qi* flows horizontally from *yi* to *you*, where it meets a white *qi* from the heavens. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

4. *Yimao*: *Yi* Metal *yun* is insufficient. *Mao* is a yin year, and above it meets *Yangming* Metal as the *sitian*, called *tianfu* harmonizing virtue. The counting number for *mao* as *Zhen* is three; *yi* Metal *yun* adds seven.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, a green *qi* appears. After it fades, a white *qi* flows horizontally from *yi* to *mao*, where it meets a white *qi* from the heavens. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

5. *Dinghai*: *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient. *Hai* is a yin year, and above it meets *Jueyin* Wood as the *sitian*, harmonizing its virtue, hence called *tianfu*. The counting number for *hai* as *Qian* is six; *ding* Wood *yun* adds eight.

When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a red *qi* appears. After it fades, a green *qi* flows horizontally from *ding* to *hai*, where it meets a red *qi* from the heavens. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

6. *Ding-si*: *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient. *Si* is a yin year, and above it meets *Jueyin* Wood as the *sitian*, harmonizing its virtue, hence called *tianfu*. The counting number for *si* is four; *ding* Wood *yun* adds eight.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a red *qi* appears. After it fades, a green *qi* flows horizontally from *ding* to *si*. It meets a red *qi* from the heavens. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.
The above six are all *tianfu*, constituting balanced *qi*.

7. *Gui-si*: *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient. *Si* is a yin year, and below it meets *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire as the *zaiquan*, harmonizing its virtue below, hence called *tong sui hui*. The counting number for *si* is four; *gui* Fire *yun* adds seven.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chou* and gaze forward. First, a jade-green *qi* appears. After it fades, a red *qi* flows horizontally from *gui* to *si*, where it meets a red *qi* from the earth. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

8. *Gui-hai*: *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient. *Hai* is a yin year, and below it meets *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire as the *zaiquan*, harmonizing its virtue below, hence called *tong sui hui*. The counting number for *hai* is six; *gui* Fire *yun* adds seven.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chou* and gaze forward. First, a jade-green *qi* appears. After it fades, a red *qi* flows horizontally from *gui* to *hai*, where it meets a red *qi* from the earth. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

9. *Xin-chou*: *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient. *Chou* is a yin year, and below it meets *Taiyang* Cold Water as the *zaiquan*, harmonizing its virtue below, hence called *tong sui hui*. The counting number for *chou* is five; Water *yun* adds six.
When the *yun* transitions, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, a warm white *qi* appears, followed by a black *qi* flowing horizontally from *xin* to *chou*, where it meets a black *qi* from the earth. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

10. *Xin-wei*: *Xin* Water *yun* is insufficient. *Wei* is a yin year, and below it meets *Taiyang* Cold Water as the *zaiquan*, harmonizing its virtue below, hence called *tong sui hui*. The counting number for *wei* is five; *xin* Water *yun* adds six.
When the *yun* transitions, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, a warm white *qi* appears. After it fades, a black *qi* flows horizontally from *xin* to *wei*, where it meets a black *qi* from the earth. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

11. *Gui-mao*: *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient. *Mao* is a yin year, and below it meets *Shaoyin* Sovereign Fire as the *zaiquan*, harmonizing its virtue below, hence called *tong sui hui*. The counting number for *mao* is three; *gui* Fire *yun* adds seven.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chou* and gaze forward. First, a jade-green *qi* appears. After it fades, a red *qi* flows horizontally from *gui* to *mao*, where it meets a red *qi* from the earth. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

12. *Gui-you*: *Gui* Fire *yun* is insufficient. *You* is a yin year, and below it meets *Shaoyin* Sovereign Fire as the *zaiquan*, harmonizing its virtue below, hence called *tong sui hui*. The counting number for *you* is seven; *gui* Fire *yun* adds seven.
When the *yun* transitions, face *chou* and gaze forward. First, a jade-green *qi* appears. After it fades, a red *qi* flows horizontally from *gui* to *you*, where it meets a red *qi* from the earth. No other colors appear—inquire for auspiciousness.

13. *Ding-mao*: *Ding* Wood *yun* is insufficient. *Mao* is a yin year, and *mao* is also Wood, thus *mao* Wood converges, constituting a proper *sui hui*. The counting number for *mao* is three; *ding* Wood *yun* adds eight.
When the *yun* transitions, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, a red *qi* appears. After it fades, a green *qi* flows horizontally from *ding* to *mao*, where it is met by another green *qi* above *mao*, hence called *sui hui*.
There are four *sui hui*, of which this is one; the other three are thus equivalent to *tianfu*. These are the years *yi-you*, *ji-wei*, and *ji-chou*. Therefore, the sixteen instances of balanced *qi* actually occur across thirteen years.

*Plain Questions: Six Qi Mysterious Pearl Secret Sayings*, Scroll Six, concludes.

*Plain Questions: Six Qi Mysterious Pearl Secret Sayings*, Scroll Seven
Recorded by Qi Xuanzi.

**The *Yun* Encounters Overstepping and Connects with the Era: The Twenty Methods of *Tuo Lin***

*Tuo Lin* refers to years within the sixty *jiazi* cycle where the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches do not correspond—these are years of great misfortune. Yet not every such year results in *tuo lin*; it may occur once in over a hundred years, bringing widespread ruin where the people and agriculture fall into desolation.

The "twenty methods" account for forty years within the sixty-year cycle, from remote antiquity to the present, where *yun* and *qi* consistently correspond without *tuo*. There are twelve years of *shou zhi* (Stem-Guarding), where correspondence remains unbroken:
1. *Jia-yin*
2. *Yi-mao*
3. *Wu-wu*
4. *Ji-wei*
5. *Geng-shen*
6. *Xin-you*
7. *Bing-wu*
8. *Ding-wei*
9. *Ren-zi*
10. *Gui-chou*
11. *Wu-xu*
12. *Ji-si*

These twelve years of *shou zhi* maintain unbroken correspondence.

Next are twelve years of *tianfu* (Celestial Correspondence), where *yun* and *qi* also align:
1. *Wu-zi* (same as *shou zhi*)
2. *Wu-wu* (same as *shou zhi*)
3. *Wu-yin*
4. *Wu-shen*
5. *Bing-xu*
6. *Bing-chen*
7. *Ji-chou*
8. *Ji-wei* (same as *shou zhi*, conflicting with *shou zhi* year)
9. *Yi-mao* (same as *shou zhi*)
10. *Yi-you*
11. *Ding-si*
12. *Ding-hai*

Among these twelve *tianfu* years, three coincide with *shou zhi*, leaving nine distinct years.

Next are twelve years of *di he* (Earthly Harmony), where correspondence remains unbroken:
1. *Geng-zi*
2. *Geng-wu*
3. *Xin-chou*
4. *Xin-wei*
5. *Ren-yin*
6. *Ren-shen*
7. *Gui-you*
8. *Gui-wei*
9. *Jia-chen*
10. *Jia-xu*
11. *Gui-si*
12. *Gui-hai*

These twelve years of *di he* maintain unbroken correspondence.

Next are ten years of *zhi fu* (Direct Correspondence), where *yun* and *qi* also align:
1. *Ren-chen*
2. *Ren-xu*
3. *Bing-wu* (same as *shou zhi*)
4. *Bing-zi*
5. *Bing-yin*
6. *Bing-shen*
7. *Xin-mao*
8. *Xin-you* (same as *shou zhi*)
9. *Yi-wei* (same as *shou zhi* and *tianfu*)
10. *Ji-chou* (same as *tianfu*)

Among these ten years, five coincide with others. Within the above forty-six years, eight overlap, leaving thirty-eight distinct years. Additionally, *jia-zi* as the *yuan shou* (Origin Head) maintains correspondence, and *ding-mao* as the *sui hui* (Yearly Convergence) also remains unbroken—adding two more years. In total, forty years maintain unbroken correspondence, with only twenty years experiencing *tuo lin*:

1. *Yi-chou*: At the *yun* transition, face *chen* and gaze forward. Only green *qi* appears; white *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *chou*—this is *yi* not corresponding to *chou*, a year of great misfortune.
2. *Wu-chen*: The reckoning aligns with excess. At the *yun* transition, face *si* and gaze forward. First, yellow *qi* appears; red *qi* emerges but then recedes or remains unseen—this is *wu* not corresponding to *chen*, where the Heavenly Stem does not align with the Earthly Branch.
3. *Yi-hai*: The reckoning aligns with a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, green *qi* appears; white *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *hai*—this is *yi* not corresponding to *hai*.
4. *Ding-chou*: The reckoning aligns with a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, red *qi* appears; blue-green *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *chou*—this is *ding* not corresponding to *chou*.
5. *Ji-mao*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, purple *qi* appears; yellow *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *mao*—this is *ji* not corresponding to *mao*.
6. *Geng-chen*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, face *shen* and gaze forward. First, white *qi* appears but then recedes, failing to reach *chen*—this is *geng* not corresponding to *chen*.
7. *Xin-si*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, warm white *qi* appears; black *qi* emerges but then recedes—this is *xin* not corresponding to *si*.
8. *Ren-wu*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, face *hai* and gaze forward. First, black *qi* appears; blue-green *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *wu*—this is *ren* not corresponding to *wu*.
9. *Gui-wei*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *you* and gaze forward. First, jade-green *qi* appears; red *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *wei*—this is *gui* not corresponding to *wei*.
10. *Jia-shen*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, face *yin* and gaze forward. First, blue-green *qi* appears; yellow *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *shen*—this is *jia* not corresponding to *shen*.
11. *Geng-yin*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, face *shen* and gaze forward. First, white *qi* appears; its *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *yin*—this is *geng* not corresponding to *yin*.
12. *Xin-mao*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, warm white *qi* appears; black *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *mao*—this is *xin* not corresponding to *mao*.
13. *Jia-wu*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, face *yin* and gaze forward. First, blue-green *qi* appears; yellow *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *wu*—this is *jia* not corresponding to *wu*.
14. *Yi-wei*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, green *qi* appears; white *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *wei*—this is *yi* not corresponding to *wei*.
15. *Ding-you*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, red *qi* appears; blue-green *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *you*—this is *ding* not corresponding to *you*.
16. *Ji-hai*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, purple *qi* appears; yellow *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *hai*—this is *ji* not corresponding to *hai*.

17. *Yi-si*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *chen* and gaze forward. First, green *qi* appears; white *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *si*—this is *yi* not corresponding to *si*.

18. *Ji-you*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *wei* and gaze forward. First, purple *qi* appears; yellow *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *you*—this is *ji* not corresponding to *you*.

19. *Geng-xu*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, face *shen* and gaze forward. First, white *qi* appears but then recedes, failing to reach *xu*—this is *geng* not corresponding to *xu*.

20. *Xin-hai*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, face *xu* and gaze forward. First, warm white *qi* appears; black *qi* emerges but then recedes, failing to reach *hai*—this is *xin* not corresponding to *hai*.

The above are all cases of *tuo lin* ("detached correspondence"). This does not necessarily occur every year; it is only when the *qi* of the *yun* fails to arrive that the Heavenly Stem does not correspond to the Earthly Branch, all indicating inauspicious years.

**Chapter on Disasters and Transformations in the Cycle of *Yun***
**Twelve Methods of Punitive *Yun***

These methods apply to six yin years and six yang years.

1. *Ren-zi*: *Ren* Wood *yun*, *zi* yang year. When the *yun* transitions, the reckoning follows the preceding method. Beneath the Wood *yun*, it encounters *yang ming* Metal as the *zai quan*. Metal comes to punish Wood: white mists rise on all sides, bearing down upon the Wood *yun*. The punitive *qi* is weak and diminished, so the Earth’s power is lesser than Heaven’s decree.

2. *Ren-wu*: *Ren* Wood *yun*, *wu* yang year. When the *qi* and *yun* transition, the reckoning follows the preceding method. After the *qi* passes, below lies *yang ming* Metal. White *qi* is frequently seen in the mountains and valleys, repeatedly punishing the Wood *qi*. The Wood *qi* is faint and small, unable to overcome the victory, so the Earth prevails over the *yun*.

3. *Gui-chou*: Fire *yun* is insufficient. When the *yun* and *qi* transition, the reckoning follows the preceding method. Below, it encounters *tai yang* Cold Water as the *zai quan*. After the *yun* *qi* passes, black *qi* frequently rises, appearing dim and dark from afar. It punishes the Fire *yun* from above, leaving its *qi* insufficient and the transformation of heat bereft of its mandate.

4. *Gui-wei*: Fire *yun* is insufficient. When the *qi* and *yun* transition, the reckoning follows the preceding method. After the *yun* *qi* passes, Earth Water comes to punish. Black *qi* arises from the Earth, overpowering the Fire *yun* from above. Its *qi* is insufficient, and the decree of heat’s transformation weakens, losing half its force.

5. *Jia-yin*: Earth *yun*, which is excessive. When reckoning the *yun*, the later *qi* is unified. After the *yun* passes, below appears *jue yin* Wood as the *zai quan*. At times, green mists rise on all sides; from afar, forests appear as if veiled in smoke, yet remain verdant. Thus, the Earth’s *qi* frequently manifests, and the transformation of Earth—rain and dampness—must still lose its mandate.

6. *Jia-shen*: Opposite to *jia-yin* in transformation, it also encounters *jue yin* Wood as the *zai quan* below, punishing the Earth *yun*. The transformation of rain and dampness is the same as in *jia-yin*.

7. *Yi-mao*: Metal *yun* is insufficient. Its reckoning is diminished, and the *qi* conditions follow the preceding method. After the *yun* *qi* passes, below it encounters *shao yin* Sovereign Fire as the *zai quan*. Heat steams from the Earth, and red *qi* ascends, coming to punish the Metal *yun*. Thus, the decree of dryness and clarity is all deficient, instead giving rise to the transformation of heat—this is the mutation of the Earth’s *yun*.

8. *Yi-you*: Metal *yun* follows the preceding method. Below, it encounters *shao yin* Sovereign Fire as the *zai quan*, punishing the Metal *yun* from above. The decree of clarity and dryness is deficient, instead generating the decree of heat, just as in *yi-mao*.

9. *Bing-chen*: Water *yun*. Below, it encounters *tai yin* Earth as the *zai quan*. The *yun*’s decree and *qi* conditions follow the excessive pattern. Afterward, there is yellow, stagnant *qi*, and distant mists appear dim. Earth comes to restrain Water. Thus, the decree of cold is reversed to warmth, and winter brings light rain.

10. *Bing-xu*: Water *yun*. Below, it encounters *tai yin* Earth as the *zai quan*. When reckoning the *yun* *qi*, the method follows the preceding pattern. Earth *qi* lies below, punishing the cold transformation from above, just as in the decree of *bing-chen*.

11. *Yi-si*: *Yi* Metal *yun*. The method of observing the *qi* and *yun* is the same as before. After the *yun* passes, below it encounters *shao yang* Minister Fire as the *zai quan*. Heat moves upon the Earth, steaming the Earth’s *qi*. Flames illuminate the countryside. Thus, the Metal *yun* loses its proper decree and instead transforms into Fire.

12. *Yi-hai*: *Yi* Metal *yun*. The method of observation follows the preceding description. Below, it encounters Minister Fire, which overcomes the Metal *yun*, instead generating the decree of heat. In the six yang years, the victory is slight; in the six yin years, the victory is severe.

**Ten Methods of Intercalary Punitive *Yun***

1. *Yi-si*: Central Metal *yun*. The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, if white *qi* and red *qi* arrive together, this indicates the *qi* of Fire’s victory. If red *qi* arrives subsequently, this is the left intercalary *qi*—*shao yin* Sovereign Fire—secondarily punishing the insufficiency of Metal.

2. *Gui-si*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, if black *qi* and red *qi* arrive together, this indicates Water coming to prevail. If black *qi* arrives subsequently, this is *tai yang* Water as the right intercalary *qi*.

3. *Bing-zi*: The reckoning follows a yang year. The *qi* of a yang year has no distinct color. Only after the red *qi* of *bing-wu* has fully appeared, then black *qi* from *bing* to *zi* arrives. If yellow *qi* arrives instead, this is the *tian xu* ("Heavenly Void") of oppositional transformation, with *tai yin* Earth *qi* coming as the left intercalary *qi*. Though the intercalary *qi* is secondary, the *si tian* ("Controller of Heaven") also arrives—this is the intercalary *yun*. Where there is punishment, it will arrive.

4. *Jia-zi*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, yellow *qi* arrives from *jia* to *zi*. If green *qi* arrives subsequently, this is the left intercalary *qi*—*jue yin* Wood coming to punish the Wood *yun*. Earth is the southern ruler, so Wood is on the left.

5. *Yi-mao*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, white *qi* appears first, then red *qi* arrives together with it, indicating Fire coming to overcome Metal. If red *qi* arrives subsequently, this is the right intercalary *qi*—the *qi* of Minister Fire.

6. *Gui-mao*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, red *qi* appears first, with black *qi* arriving together with it, indicating Water coming to overcome Fire. If black *qi* arrives subsequently, this is the left intercalary *qi*—the *qi* of *tai yang* Water.

7. *Yi-chou*: The reckoning follows a yin year. At the *yun* transition, red *qi* appears first, arriving together with white *qi*, indicating Fire coming to overcome Metal. If red *qi* arrives subsequently, this is the left intercalary *qi*—Minister Fire coming to punish Metal.

8. Moreover, if there is a sovereign Fire as the right intercalary *qi*, when the left intercalary *qi* arrives, the right does not; when the right arrives, the left does not. Thus, an additional year is established, making the count eight.

9. *Ren-shen*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, as in a yin year, if white *qi* arrives later, this is the left intercalary *qi* of *yang ming*, punishing the Wood *yun*.

10. *Bing-shen*: The reckoning follows a yang year. At the *yun* transition, after black *qi* passes, if yellow *qi* appears as in a yin year, this is the right intercalary *qi*—*tai yin* Earth coming to punish the Water *yun*.

**Five Methods of Guest *Qi* Punishing the *Yun***

1. When the Wood *yun* is insufficient, Metal prevails. If a guest *qi* arrives subsequently, it becomes the residing *qi*—termed the "lesser intercalary *qi*." Observing the time, if the *qi* arrives obliquely, though its color is faint, it traverses the *yun* horizontally—this is the guest *qi*. If there is a prevailing *qi*, it does not arrive; if there is none, it does. This is the small white *qi* piercing through the Wood *yun*.

2. When the Fire *yun* is insufficient, Water prevails. If the *qi* arrives simultaneously, and *tai yang* comes to reside, this is black *qi* traversing the Fire *qi* horizontally.

3. When the Earth *yun* is insufficient, Wood *qi* arrives together, and *jue yin* comes to reside—this is green *qi* traversing the Earth *qi* horizontally.

4. When the Metal *yun* is insufficient, Fire *qi* arrives together, and Minister Fire comes to reside—this is red *qi* traversing the white *qi* horizontally. Sovereign Fire is likewise in *wu*.

5. When the Water *yun* is insufficient, yellow *qi* arrives together, and *tai yin* comes to reside—this is yellow *qi* piercing through the black *qi*.

**Six Methods of Heavenly Correspondence Overcoming the *Yun***

Among the balanced *qi*, there are six heavenly correspondences, which occur in yin years and differ from these six overcoming heavenly correspondences.

1. *Wu-zi*: The Fire *yun* is excessive. The reckoning follows a yang year, with red *qi* extending from *wu* to *zi*. Its *qi* is bright and distinct, and the heavens bear red *qi* in accord. Above, it joins with the virtue of *shao yin* Sovereign Fire. The term "overcoming heavenly correspondence" refers to self-overcoming, thus punishing Metal.

2. *Wu-wu*: Likewise, the Fire *yun* is excessive. The reckoning follows a yang year, with red *qi* extending from *wu* to *wu*. The heavens bear red *qi* in accord. When the *qi* converges, if the sky is free of clouds, it portends auspiciousness—hence the name "overcoming."

3. *Wu-yin*: The Fire *yun* is excessive. Above, it joins with *shao yang* Minister Fire to prevail together, unlike the benevolence of Sovereign Fire. When Fire is too abundant, all things wither and scorch; metal melts and stones liquefy; waves boil; insects perish; and the people suffer from panting and coughing.

4. *Wu-shen*: The Fire *yun* is excessive. Above, it joins with *shao yang* Minister Fire to prevail together. When the overcoming reaches its extreme, Metal loses its proper state and falls into distress, ultimately without Water to restore balance—this exemplifies self-overcoming. At its zenith, all things wither and scorch, and Venus diminishes.

5. *Bing-xu*: The Water *yun* is excessive. Above, it encounters *tai yang* Cold Water as the *si tian*. The heavenly and earthly *qi* converge. Thus, summer turns cold, and winter becomes biting. Cold mists arise repeatedly; yang light fails to govern. When extreme, Earth does not restore balance—this exemplifies overcoming. Mars loses its color, and feathered creatures perish.

6. *Bing-chen*: The Water *yun* is excessive. Above, it joins with *tai yang* Cold Water in command. The two *qi* unite in virtue, and guest *qi* assists. Hail arrives suddenly; cold winds assail; earthly *qi* chills; heavenly *qi* congeals; human *qi* contracts. The biting cold intensifies; Earth does not restore balance. Red *qi* and crimson clouds vanish entirely.

**Four Methods of the Supreme Heavenly Correspondence *Yun***

This is the triple convergence of heaven, earth, and *yun*.

1. *Wu-wu*: Above, *shao yin* Sovereign Fire governs as *si tian*; in the center, the Fire *yun* is excessive. The year *wu* belongs to the south, the position of *li* Fire—hence the name "Supreme Heavenly Correspondence" of the triple convergence. The reckoning adds sixteen: *wu* is *li*, its number nine; the excessive Fire *yun* is seven. Seven and nine together make sixteen. At the *yun* transition, facing *wu*, one sees radiant red *qi*. The heavens bear red *qi* in accord—this *yun* must give birth to noble persons.

2. *Yi-you*: Above, *yang ming* Metal governs as *si tian*; in the center, the Metal *yun* is insufficient. The heavenly correspondence is balanced. *You* belongs to the west, *dui*, corresponding to Metal—hence the name "triple convergence." The reckoning marks the year as seven; the *yun* adds seven. At the *yun* transition, facing *chen*, white *qi* extends from *yi* to *you*. The heavens bear white *qi* in accord. Those born in this *yun* are destined to become renowned generals.

3. *Ji-wei*: Above, *tai yin* Earth governs as *si tian*; in the center, the Earth *yun* is insufficient. The heavenly correspondence is balanced. *Wei* is *kun* Earth; the reckoning adds five. At the *yun* transition, from oneself to *wei*, radiant yellow *qi* appears. The heavens bear yellow *qi* in accord—this *yun* gives birth to future chancellors.

4. *Ji-chou*: Above, *tai yin* Earth governs as *si tian*; in the center, the Earth *yun* is insufficient. The heavenly correspondence is balanced. *Chou* is the central palace of Earth—hence the name "triple convergence." The reckoning adds five. At the *yun* transition, from oneself to *chou*, radiant yellow *qi* appears. The heavens bear yellow *qi* in accord—this *yun* gives birth to prime ministers.

These four Supreme Heavenly Correspondences govern the birth of noble persons.

**Four Methods of the Same Heavenly Correspondence**

When *shao yin* governs as *si tian* in *zi* and *wu*, the *wu* year is the same heavenly correspondence—first;

When *Yangming* governs as *si tian* in *mao* and *you*, the *you* year is the same heavenly correspondence—second. When *Taiyin* governs as *si tian* in *chou* and *wei*, both *chou* and *wei* are the same heavenly correspondence—fourth. The observation of *yun-qi* follows the method: the four-year convergence in the preceding balanced *qi* has already clarified this correspondence.

**Twelve Methods of the Same Yearly Convergence**

1. *Geng-zi* Metal *yun*: Below, *Yangming* Metal is *zai quan*; the earth emits white *qi* to assist the Metal *yun*’s triumph.
2. *Geng-wu* Metal *yun*: Below, *Yangming* Metal is *zai quan*; the earth emits white *qi* to assist the Metal *yun*’s triumph.
3. *Gui-chou* Water *yun*: Below, *Taiyang* Water is *zai quan*; the earth releases black *qi* to assist the Water *yun*’s triumph.
4. *Gui-wei* Water *yun*: Below, *Taiyang* Water is *zai quan*; the earth releases black *qi* to assist the Water *yun*’s triumph.
5. *Ren-yin* Wood *yun*: Below, *Jueyin* Wood is *zai quan*; the earth emits verdant mist to assist the Wood *yun*’s triumph.
6. *Ren-shen* Wood *yun*: Below, *Jueyin* Wood is *zai quan*; the earth emits verdant mist to assist the Wood *yun*’s triumph.
7. *Gui-mao* Fire *yun*: Below, *Shaoyin* Sovereign Fire is *zai quan*; the earth emits red *qi* to assist the Fire *yun*’s triumph.
8. *Gui-you* Fire *yun*: Below, *Shaoyin* Sovereign Fire is *zai quan*; the earth emits red *qi* to assist the Fire *yun*’s triumph.
9. *Jia-chen* Earth *yun*: Below, *Taiyin* Earth is *zai quan*; the earth emits yellow mist to assist the Earth *yun*’s triumph.
10. *Jia-xu* Earth *yun*: Below, *Taiyin* Earth is *zai quan*; the earth emits yellow mist to assist the Earth *yun*’s triumph.
11. *Gui-si* Fire *yun*: Below, *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire is *zai quan*; the earth steams red *qi*, illuminating the outskirts at night to assist the Fire *yun*’s triumph.
12. *Gui-hai* Fire *yun*: Below, *Shaoyang* Ministerial Fire is *zai quan*; the earth steams red *qi*, lighting the wilds at night, with fires visible beyond the suburbs to assist the Fire *yun*’s triumph.

**Five Methods of Heavenly Depression**

1. In a Wood *yun* year, if Metal governs as *si tian* above, the heavenly constraint overpowers the *yun*, which fails to prevail. In the following yin year, after *si tian* retreats but before the Wood *yun* transitions, the suppressed Wood *qi* transforms into verdant *qi*, bringing calamity to the world and causing sudden deaths among the people.
2. In a Fire *yun* year, if Water governs as *si tian* above, the heavenly constraint overpowers the *yun*, which fails to prevail. In the following yin year, with the *yun-qi* transition delayed and *si tian* already retreated, the suppressed Fire *qi* bursts forth, afflicting the world and the people with restlessness, fright, red urine, sores, ulcers, and rashes.
3. In an Earth *yun* year, if *Jueyin* Wood governs as *si tian* above, the heavenly constraint overpowers the *yun*, which fails to prevail. In the following yin year, after *si tian* retreats but before the *yun-qi* transitions, the suppressed Earth *qi* scatters, causing the people to suffer from swelling, jaundice, abdominal distension, edema, diarrhea, and limb weakness.
4. In a Metal *yun* year, if Sovereign or Ministerial Fire governs as *si tian* above, the heavenly constraint overpowers the *yun*, which fails to prevail. In the following yin year, after *si tian* retreats but before the *yun-qi* transitions, the suppressed Metal *qi* disperses, afflicting the people with limb fullness, blockage, distension, muscle spasms, strangury, urinary difficulty, dryness in the upper burner, blurred vision, irritability, pallor, sorrow, and melancholy.
5. In a Water *yun* year, if *Taiyin* Earth governs as *si tian* above, the heavenly constraint overpowers the *yun*, which fails to prevail. After *si tian* retreats but before the *yun-qi* transitions, the suppressed Water *qi* scatters, causing the people to suffer from atrophy, cold limbs, impotence, incontinence, limb blockage, joint pain, and lower abdominal fullness.

**Five Methods of Heavenly Destruction**

1. If the Wood *yun* is excessive, arriving early with surplus *qi*, and *Yangming* Metal governs as *si tian* above without having retreated, the heavenly Metal constrains it. Wood does not submit, transforming into thunderous sounds—this is called *Heavenly Destruction*. The people suffer from convulsions and spasms; plants flourish prematurely, but frost returns to kill them, causing restlessness, blockage, thirst, and delirium.
2. If the Fire *yun* is excessive, arriving early with surplus *qi*, and *Taiyang* Water governs as *si tian* above without having retreated, the heavenly Water constrains it. Fire does not submit, transforming into scorching heat, while hail falls—this is called *Heavenly Destruction*. The people suffer sudden deaths, alternating chills and fever, abdominal fullness, dry throat, and esophageal obstruction.
3. If the Earth *yun* is excessive, arriving early with surplus *qi*, and *Jueyin* Wood governs as *si tian* above without having retreated, the heavenly Wood constrains it. Earth does not submit, transforming into dense fog and dust, followed by gentle rain and then violent winds—this is called *Heavenly Destruction*. The people suffer from limb swelling, dampness, jaundice, edema, and loss of appetite.
4. If the Metal *yun* is excessive, arriving early with surplus *qi*, and Sovereign or Ministerial Fire governs as *si tian* above, the heavenly constraint prevails. Metal does not submit, transforming into rustling winds, tiger roars, and ape cries—this is called *Heavenly Destruction*. The people suffer from restlessness, tooth decay, throat dryness, thirst, brittle hair, wheezing, and coughing.
5. If the Water *yun* is excessive, arriving early with surplus *qi*, and *Taiyin* Earth governs as *si tian* above without having retreated, the heavenly constraint prevails. Water does not submit, transforming into sleet and unrelenting gloom—this is called *Heavenly Destruction*. The people suffer from bone atrophy, leg soreness, impotence, incontinence, limb blockage, joint pain, and lower abdominal fullness.

**Chapter on Disasters, Omens, and Cyclical Patterns**

**Era of Great Peace**
In years when the Five *Yun* are excessive, observe as before: if, beside the *yun*’s proper position, five-colored hues like rainbows appear, flanked by "ears," and if solar "ears" also manifest, persisting long after the *yun* has passed without dissipating, a single sighting heralds thirty years of Great Peace.

**Era of Ascending Peace**
The Era of Ascending Peace corresponds to the *yun* of the imperial house attaining kingship—fire for fire, water for water. In years of excessive *yun*, hues beside the *yun*’s proper position resemble rainbows, lingering without fading. Their appearance brings prosperity, joyful livelihoods, flourishing imperial governance, and an aura slightly lesser than the Era of Great Peace.

**Era of Heavenly Warfare**
The Era of Heavenly Warfare arises within the Five *Yun*, regardless of excess or deficiency. After the *yun* passes, a white *qi* like silk appears, followed by clouds clinging to it—these clouds, too, are white, resembling wolves or tigers. Their sighting foretells major warfare the following year.

**Era of Heavenly Aridity**
The Era of Heavenly Aridity occurs in years of excessive Metal *yun*, or when Wood is deficient and Metal prevails, or when the Metal *yun* aligns with a Heavenly Correspondence, invariably in years dominated by dry Metal transformations. It may also appear in years when Earth fails to restrain. After the *yun* passes, white *qi* scatters into red, intermingling as red and white. Its sighting portends severe drought.

**Era of Heavenly Moisture**
The Era of Heavenly Moisture often appears in years of excessive Earth *yun*, or when Water is deficient and Earth prevails, or in years when Earth aligns with a Heavenly Correspondence. In years of excessive Earth, yellow *qi* manifests; in years when Earth overcomes Water, yellow and black *qi* intermingle. If the *qi* appears as fine, greenish-black strands like horsehair, its sighting signals flooding disasters.

**Era of Usurpation**
The Era of Usurpation is determined by the *yun* of the imperial house attaining kingship. After the *yun* passes, a distinct white *qi* encroaches upon it. Within this white *qi*, small red specks like sparks appear, followed by clouds resembling snakes or insects. This foretells rebellion against the sovereign.

**Era of the Illustrious Sovereign**
The Era of the Illustrious Sovereign appears in years when the imperial house’s *yun* is excessive. The *yun* is vast and luminous, accompanied by purple *qi*. Alternatively, it may resemble a purple canopy, a purple figure, or a five-colored dragon. Its sighting heralds the flourishing of imperial governance.

**Era of the Sage**
The Sage is born of Heaven and Earth, emerging once every thousand years. In years of Grand Heavenly Correspondence, Heavenly Correspondence, or when the *yun* aligns with Heaven, a red *qi* illuminates the sky, and celestial brilliance suffuses the mountains and valleys. From the caves and grottoes of these peaks, a Sage is born.

**Era of the Worthy**
The Worthy appears once every five hundred years, not born of Heaven and Earth. In years of Heavenly Correspondence or when the *yun*’s governance is harmonious, after the *yun*’s *qi* passes, white *qi* surges upward in specific regions, towering and resplendent. Where this *qi* descends, many Worthies are born.

**Era of Heavenly Locusts**
In years when the *yun* clash without harmony, regardless of excess or deficiency, yellow masses appear within the *yun* and do not disperse. If locusts appear but the masses remain intact, no disaster occurs. If the masses scatter like fragmented stars, the infestation will be severe, affecting the regions where they disperse.

**Era of Famine**
In years when the Five *Yun* clash and overcome one another, after the *yun* passes, clouds—yellow, black, or obscuring the *yun*—appear, resembling ghosts, geese, ducks, or overturned boats. Their sighting foretells crop failure.

**Era of Heavenly Pestilence**
Heavenly Pestilence may arise in any *yun*, its *qi* arriving even when the *yun* is unseen. Minor disasters manifest as epidemics with yellow *qi*. Major disasters occur when the yellow *qi* is encircled by halos of purple and red, varying in size, scattering like tiny lightning bolts or writhing earthworms. The intermingling of purple, red, and yellow *qi* within the yellow portends mass death.

**Era of Bountiful Harvests**
The Era of Bountiful Harvests occurs in years of deficient *yun* where the *qi* is faint yet unexpectedly profound, or when the overcoming *qi* does not merge. In years of excessive *yun*, all five colors intermingle with yellow *qi*. After the *qi* passes, clouds resembling people, phoenixes, or cranes appear, heralding abundant harvests.

**Era of Auspicious Omens**
The Era of Auspicious Omens may appear in years of excessive or deficient *yun*. Beyond the *yun*’s proper position, hues of purple or red manifest, resembling lingzhi mushrooms or mountains with trees. Their sighting brings Great Peace, national prosperity, and a content, abundant populace.

**Era of True Correspondence**
The Era of True Correspondence heralds the emergence of a sagely and enlightened sovereign, answering to the future Son of Heaven. It appears within excessive *yun*, its five colors unfixed—wood responding to wood, fire to fire. The *qi* is vast, flanked by subsidiary hues of the same color, accompanied by several smaller *qi* streams. Each stream represents an emperor, while the smaller *qi* signify descendants.

*End of Volume Seven of the* Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi *from the* Plain Questions.

**Plain Questions: Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi**
**Volume Eight**
*Recorded by Master Qi Yuan*

**The Southern Regulator’s Twelve Celestial Governances**

When the Southern Regulator governs Heaven, it proceeds from the *gan* in sequence to the *zhi*, then applies the *zhi*’s numerical value to the generative and consummate numbers.

1. **Jiazi Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, the *zheng* tone presides. The sovereign fire resides in Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in harmony.
   From *jia* to *zi*, it advances eleven positions. *Zi* corresponds to *kan*, its number one; fire’s consummate number is seven. At the celestial hour, it arrives precisely eight *ke* before the celestial count.
   Eleven days later, fire begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. Five days into its rule, *Tai Gong* arrives in harmony. Crimson *qi* ascends, heat prevails in Heaven, azure mists appear at dusk, and yellow clouds arise at dawn—these are the attendant hues following the Regulator’s color.

2. **Jiawu Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, *Tai Zheng* presides. The sovereign fire resides in Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in harmony.
   From *jia* to *wu*, it advances five positions. *Wu* corresponds to *li*, its number nine; fire’s generative number is two. Nine and two combine to make eleven.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives eleven *ke* before the celestial count. Five days later, fire begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. Five days into its rule, *Tai Gong* and *Tai Zheng* rise in harmony. Crimson *qi* appears above, azure mists manifest at dusk, and yellow *qi* emerges at dawn—this is the celestial Dao in harmonious accord, an auspicious sign.

3. **Jichou Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, the *zheng gong* tone presides. Grand Yin earth resides in Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in harmony.
   From *ji* to *chou*, it shifts seven positions to the left. *Chou* corresponds to earth, its number five; earth’s consummate number is also five. Two fives combine to make ten.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives ten *ke* after the celestial count. Seven days later, earth begins its governance of Heaven. *Shao Gong* harmonizes with the *zheng gong* above, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. Yellow *qi* ascends, dampness prevails in Heaven, and crimson *qi* with red clouds frequently appear at dawn and dusk—these are the proper hues of the left and right attendants.

4. **Jiwei Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, the *zheng gong* tone presides. Grand Yin earth governs Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in harmony.
   *Ji* originally resides in *wei*, requiring no leftward shift. *Wei* corresponds to earth, its number five; the phase earth’s number is also five. Two fives combine to make ten.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives ten *ke* after the celestial count. On that day, earth governs Heaven and immediately enacts the celestial mandate. Eighteen days into its rule, *Shao Gong* converges with *Zheng Gong*. Yellow *qi* ascends, dampness prevails in Heaven, and crimson *qi* aligns with the celestial mandate at dawn and dusk.

5. **Jiaxu Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, *Tai Yu* presides. Grand Yang cold water governs Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in harmony.
   From *jia* to *xu*, it shifts nine positions to the left. *Xu* corresponds to earth, its number five; the phase earth’s number is also five. Two fives combine to make ten.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives ten *ke* before the celestial count. Nine days later, water begins its governance of Heaven. *Tai Gong* imposes punishment on *Tai Yu*, but *Yu* remains unharmed, and the *qi* does not harmonize. Black *qi* ascends, cold prevails in Heaven, yellow *qi* appears at dawn, and yellow mists arise at dusk, eventually turning violet before shifting to black—this is the sign of harmonious transformation.

6. **Jiachen Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, *Tai Yu* presides. Grand Yang cold water governs Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves to the left.
   From *jia* to *chen*, it shifts three positions to the left. *Chen* corresponds to earth, its number five; the phase earth’s number is also five. Two fives combine to make ten.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives ten *ke* before the celestial count. Three days later, water begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. Five days into its rule, *Tai Gong* imposes punishment on *Tai Li*, but *Yu* remains unharmed. Black *qi* ascends, cold prevails in Heaven, and yellow *qi* rises, each imposing its mandate upon Heaven.

7. **Jihai Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, the *zheng jue* tone presides. Reverting Yin wood governs Heaven, and celestial *qi* shifts to the left.
   From *ji* to *hai*, it shifts five positions to the left. *Hai* corresponds to *qian*, its number six; the earth phase’s number is five. Five and six combine to make eleven.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives eleven *ke* after the celestial count. Five days later, wood begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. Eighteen days into its rule, *Shao Gong* submits to *Zheng Jue*. Azure *qi* ascends, wind prevails in Heaven, black *qi* rises in the east at dawn, and at dusk, red mists intermingle with emerald—these are the shared hues of Heaven and its Regulator.

8. **Jisi Year (Earth Phase)**
   The Southern Regulator governs Heaven. The celestial face turns north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east. Above, the *zheng jue* tone presides. Reverting Yin wood governs Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves to the left.
   From *ji* to *si*, it shifts eleven positions to the left. *Ji* corresponds to *xun*, its number four; the earth phase’s number is five. Four and five combine to make nine.
   At the celestial hour, it arrives nine *ke* after the celestial count. Eleven days later, wood begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. Eighteen days into its rule, *Shao Gong* submits to *Zheng Jue*. Azure *qi* ascends, wind prevails in Heaven, black *qi* appears in the east at dawn, and red *qi* manifests in the west at dusk—these are the signs of the two attendants following the Regulator.

*End of Volume Eight of the* Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi *from the* Plain Questions.

---

9. In the *jia-shen* year of earth phase governance, the Southern Regulator presides over Heaven. Heaven faces north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east; above, *Tai Zhi* governs. Lesser Yang ministerial fire rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves to the left, shifting seven positions from *jia* to *shen*. *Shen* corresponds to *kun*, its number two; the earth phase’s number is five. Two and five combine to make seven. At the celestial hour, it arrives seven *ke* before the celestial count. Seven days later, ministerial fire begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. Five days thereafter, *Tai Gong* harmonizes with *Tai Zhi*. Crimson *qi* ascends, heat prevails in Heaven, white mist appears at dawn, and yellow *qi* arises at dusk—these are the signs of the two attendants following the Regulator.

10. In the *jia-yin* year of earth phase governance, the Southern Regulator presides over Heaven. Heaven faces north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east; above, *Tai Zhi* governs. Lesser Yang ministerial fire rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves to the left. *Jia* wood resides in *yin*, with no further movement. *Yin* corresponds to *gen*, its number eight; the earth phase’s number is five. Eight and five combine to make thirteen. At the celestial hour, it arrives thirteen *ke* before the celestial count. On that very day, ministerial fire governs Heaven and enacts the celestial mandate. Five days later, *Tai Gong* harmonizes with *Tai Zhi*. Crimson *qi* ascends, heat prevails in Heaven, white *qi* manifests in the east, and yellow clouds rise in the west, aligning with the transformations below in accordance with Heaven.

11. In the *ji-you* year of earth phase governance, the Southern Regulator presides over Heaven. Heaven faces north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east; above, the *Zheng Shang* governs. Yang Brightness metal rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in sequence, shifting three positions from *ji* to *you*. *You* corresponds to *dui*, its number seven; the earth phase’s number is five. Seven and five combine to make twelve. At the celestial hour, it arrives twelve *ke* after the celestial count. Three days later, metal begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. Eighteen days thereafter, *Shao Gong* harmonizes with *Zheng Shang*. White *qi* ascends, dryness prevails in Heaven, crimson clouds appear at dawn, and black *qi* arises at dusk—these are the signs of the two attendants jointly following the Regulator.

12. In the *ji-mao* year of earth phase governance, the Southern Regulator presides over Heaven. Heaven faces north, with the left aligned to the west and the right to the east; above, *Zheng Shang* governs. Yang Brightness metal rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves in sequence, shifting nine positions from *ji* to *mao*. *Mao* corresponds to *zhen*, its number three; the earth phase’s number is five. Three and five combine to make eight. At the celestial hour, it arrives eight *ke* after the celestial count. Nine days later, metal begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. White *qi* ascends, dryness prevails in Heaven, red *qi* appears at dawn, and black clouds gather at dusk—these are the signs of Heaven’s compliance.

*Record of the Northern Regulator’s Rightward Revolution*
The Northern Regulator’s Governance of Heaven: Forty-Eight

---

Following the Northern Regulator’s Governance of Heaven in Reverse Revolution, from *gan* to *zhi* the celestial *qi* shifts rightward in reverse sequence, incremented by the generative and consummate numbers.

1. *Yi-chou* Metal Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Zheng Gong* governs. Great Yin earth rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting four positions from *yi* to *chou*. *Chou* corresponds to earth, its number five; metal being insufficient, it follows the generative number four. Four and five combine to make nine. At the celestial hour, it arrives nine *ke* after the celestial count. Four days later, earth begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. After seventeen days, Lesser Shang harmonizes with *Zheng Gong*. Yellow *qi* ascends, dampness prevails in Heaven; red *qi* appears in the east, red hues in the west—these are the signs of the two regulators’ compliance.

2. *Yi-wei* Metal Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Zheng Gong* governs. Great Yin earth rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting ten positions from *yi* to *wei*. *Wei* corresponds to earth, its number five; metal being insufficient, it follows the generative number four. Five and four combine to make nine. At the celestial hour, it arrives nine *ke* after the celestial count. Ten days later, earth begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the transformation of the celestial mandate. After seventeen days, Lesser Shang harmonizes with *Shang Gong*. Yellow *qi* ascends, dampness prevails in Heaven; red *qi* appears in the east and west at dawn and dusk—these are the signs of the two regulators’ compliance.

3. *Bing-yin* Water Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Tai Zheng* governs. Lesser Yang ministerial fire rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting four positions from *bing* to *yin*. *Yin* corresponds to *gen*, its number eight; water being excessive, it follows the consummate number six. Eight and six combine to make fourteen. At the celestial hour, it arrives fourteen *ke* before the celestial count. Four days later, fire begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. After six days, Greater Yu punishes *Tai Zheng*. Red *qi* ascends, heat prevails in Heaven, and cold follows; red *qi* manifests in the east, yellow clouds appear at dusk—these are the signs of the two regulators’ compliance.

4. *Bing-shen* Water Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Tai Zheng* governs. Lesser Yang ministerial fire rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting ten positions from *bing* to *shen*. *Shen* corresponds to *kun*, its number two; water being excessive, it follows the consummate number six. Two and six combine to make eight. At the celestial hour, it arrives eight *ke* before the celestial count. Ten days later, fire begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. After six days, Greater Yu punishes *Tai Zheng*. Red *qi* ascends, heat prevails in Heaven, and cold repeatedly overcomes it.

5. *Ding-mao* Wood Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Zheng Shang* governs. Yang Brightness metal rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting five positions from *ding* to *mao*. *Mao* corresponds to *zhen*, its number three; the wood phase being insufficient, it follows the generative number three. Two and three combine to make six. At the celestial hour, it arrives six *ke* after the celestial count. Five days later, metal begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. After sixteen days, Lesser Jue submits to *Zheng Shang*. White *qi* ascends, dryness prevails in Heaven; black clouds appear in the east, red *qi* arises in the west—these are the colors of the two regulators.

6. *Ding-you* Wood Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Zheng Shang* governs. Yang Brightness metal rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting eleven positions from *ding* to *you*. *You* corresponds to *dui*, its number seven; the wood phase being insufficient, it follows the generative number three. Three and seven combine to make ten. At the celestial hour, it arrives ten *ke* after the celestial count. Eleven days later, metal begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. After sixteen days, Lesser Jue submits to *Zheng Shang*. White *qi* ascends, dryness prevails in Heaven; black *qi* appears at dawn, red clouds rise at dusk—these are the signs of the two regulators’ compliance.

7. *Wu-xu* Fire Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Tai Yu* governs. Greater Yang cold water rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting eight positions from *wu* to *xu*. *Xu* corresponds to earth, its number five; the fire phase being excessive, it follows the consummate number seven. Five and seven combine to make twelve. At the celestial hour, it arrives twelve *ke* before the celestial count. Eight days later, water begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. After seven days, Greater Zheng submits to *Tai Yu*. Black *qi* ascends, cold prevails in Heaven; green mist arises in the east, white *qi* manifests in the west—these are the signs of the two regulators’ compliance.

8. *Wu-chen* Fire Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Tai Yu* governs. Greater Yang cold water rules Heaven, and celestial *qi* revolves rightward, shifting two positions from *wu* to *chen*. *Chen* corresponds to earth, its number five; the fire phase being excessive, it follows the consummate number seven. Seven and five combine to make twelve. At the celestial hour, it arrives twelve *ke* before the celestial count. Two days later, water begins its governance of Heaven, initiating the celestial mandate. After seven days, Greater Zheng submits to *Tai Yu*. Black *qi* ascends, cold prevails in Heaven; green *qi* appears in the east, white haze in the west—these are the signs of the two regulators’ compliance.

9. *Geng-wu* Metal Phase
   The Northern Regulator governs Heaven; the celestial face turns south, with the left aligned to the east and the right to the west; above, *Tai Zheng* governs.
