**Earth Harmonizes with Phase and Dominant Revolutions: Twelve Methods of Phase Harmonizing with Subterranean Springs**

1. *Gengzi* below appears *yimao*: *Yi* is the Metal phase. Earth sees *yangming* transforming in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is Metal, above harmonizing with the phase as Metal. Thus, the transformation of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. White dust rises on all sides, pungent entities flourish, sour entities diminish. After half the year, dryness prevails and wind recedes.

2. *Gengwu* below appears *yiyou*: *Yi* is the Metal phase. Earth sees *yangming* transforming in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is Metal, above harmonizing with the phase as Metal. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Gazing afar at mountains and valleys, white *qi* appears like silk. The proper mandate is firm, further harmonizing with the phase’s mandate. Dryness prevails, pungent transformation arises, and the Wood phase’s *qi* is diminished.

3. *Xinchou* below appears *chenchen*: *Bing* and *xin* are the Water phase. Earth sees *taiyang* transforming in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is Water, above harmonizing with the phase as Water. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Black *qi* appears in the distance, salty entities arise, bitter entities diminish. Cold transformation follows the mandate, and sunlight is obscured.

4. *Xinwei* below appears *bingxu*: *Bing* and *xin* are the Water phase. Earth sees *taiyang* properly transforming in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is Water, above harmonizing with the phase as Water. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Gazing afar to the horizon, darkness prevails. Earth’s *qi* ascends in dominance. Salty transformation prevails over bitter, cold prevails over heat. Its mandate further surpasses the proper transformation of the *chen* year’s phase harmonization.

5. *Renyin* below appears *dingsi*: *Ding* and *ren* are the Wood phase. Earth sees *jueyin* transforming in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is Wood, above harmonizing with the phase as Wood. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Beneath the blue dust, sour entities flourish, sweet entities diminish. Wind transformation follows the mandate.

6. *Renshen* below appears *dinghai*: *Ding* and *ren* are the Wood phase. Earth sees *jueyin* properly transforming in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is Wood, above harmonizing with the phase as Wood. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Thus, the Earth emits blue dust, and mountains generate azure *qi*. Sour entities restrain sweet, and the mandate brings destruction. The proper transformation of the phase harmonizes, further prevailing over *ji*.

7. *Guiyou* below appears *wuzi*: *Wu* and *gui* are the Fire phase. Earth sees *shaoyin* Sovereign Fire transforming in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is Sovereign Fire, above harmonizing with the phase as Fire. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. The Earth emits red *qi*, arising afar in the wilds. Bitter entities flourish, pungent entities turn bitter. The later mandate brings warmth, and winter sees flowing water.

8. *Guimao* below appears *wuwu*: *Wu* and *gui* are the Fire phase. Earth sees *shaoyin* Sovereign Fire properly transforming in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is Sovereign Fire, above harmonizing with the phase as Fire. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. The Earth steams with hot *qi*, and mountain valleys wither. Red *qi* frequently appears, blazing beyond the outskirts. Bitter entities prevail over pungent, red blossoms flourish. The later mandate brings winter warmth. The proper transformation of the phase harmonizes, differing from *zi*.

9. *Jiaxu* below appears *jichou*: *Jia* and *ji* are the Earth phase. Earth sees *taiyin* transforming in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is Earth, above harmonizing with the phase as Earth. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Yellow dust rises on all sides, and the Earth’s *qi* becomes moist. Sweet entities flourish, salty entities diminish. The later mandate brings dust and mist.

10. *Jiachen* below appears *jichou*: *Jia* and *ji* are the Earth phase. Earth sees *taiyin* properly transforming in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is Earth, above harmonizing with the phase as Earth. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Gazing afar at mountains and valleys, yellow *qi* rises from below. The great void is obscured by dust, clouds and entities are disturbed. Rain brings obscurity, sweet entities and yellow blossoms all flourish. The later rain brings dampness. The proper transformation of the phase harmonizes, differing from *chou*.

---

11. *Guisi* below appears *wushen*: *Wu* and *gui* are the Fire phase. Earth sees *shaoyang* in oppositional transformation in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire, above harmonizing with the phase as Fire. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Heat steams the earth warm, and hot springs emerge from the ground. Bitter entities transform, while pungent entities diminish; the winter mandate becomes warm instead.

12. *Guihai* below appears *wuyin*: *Wu* and *gui* are the Fire phase. Earth sees *shaoyang* in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire, above harmonizing with the phase as Fire. Thus, the *qi* of the subterranean springs harmonizes with the phase’s virtue. Heat steams the earth’s *qi*, and scorching brightness is seen day and night. In the outskirts and wilds, crimson *qi* arises afar. Bitter overcomes pungent; the proper transformation of the phase harmonizes, differing from *shen*.

**Twelve Methods of Phase Dominance over Subterranean Springs**

1. *Wuzi* below appears *guimao*: *Wu* and *gui* are the Fire phase, Earth sees [Yangming] in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is Metal, above seeing the Fire phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Metal; beneath crimson *qi*, pungent entities transform into bitter. After half a year, the dry mandate instead generates heat. In oppositional transformation, Earth is depleted, and the phase’s dominance is extreme.

2. *Wuwu* below appears *guiyou*: *Wu* and *gui* are the Fire phase, Earth sees *Yangming* in the subterranean springs, above seeing the Fire phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Metal; beneath crimson *qi*, pungent entities decline. After half a year, dryness intermingles with heat. In proper transformation, Earth is replete, and the phase’s dominance is halved.

3. *Jichou* below appears *jiachen*: *Jia* and *ji* are the Earth phase, Earth sees *Taiyang* in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is Water, above seeing the Earth phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Water; beneath yellow *qi*, salty entities transform into sweet. After half a year, the cold mandate instead transforms. In oppositional transformation, Earth is depleted, and the phase’s dominance is extreme.

4. *Jiwei* below appears *jiaxu*: *Jia* and *ji* are the Earth phase, Earth sees *Taiyang* in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is Water, above seeing the Earth phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Water; beneath yellow *qi*, salty entities transform into sweet. After half a year, cold intermingles with dampness, and dust and mist arise at times. In proper transformation, Earth is replete, and the phase’s dominance is halved.

5. *Gengyin* below appears *yisi*: *Yi* and *geng* are the Metal phase, Earth sees *Jueyin* in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is Wood, above seeing the Metal phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Wood; beneath white *qi*, sour entities transform into pungent. After half a year, the wind mandate instead becomes dry. In oppositional transformation, Earth is depleted, and the phase’s dominance is extreme.

6. *Gengshen* below appears *yihai*: *Yi* and *geng* are the Metal phase, Earth sees *Jueyin* in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is Wood, above seeing the Metal phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Wood; beneath white *qi*, sour entities transform into pungent. After half a year, wind intermingles with dryness. In proper transformation, Earth is replete, and the phase’s dominance is halved.

7. *Xinyou* below appears *bingzi*: *Bing* and *xin* are the Water phase, Earth sees *Shaoyin* in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is sovereign fire, above seeing the Water phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Fire; beneath black *qi*, bitter entities transform into salty. After half a year, warmth intermingles with cold. In oppositional transformation, Earth is depleted, and the phase’s dominance is extreme.

8. *Xinmao* below appears *bingwu*: *Bing* and *xin* are the Water phase, Earth sees *Shaoyin* in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is sovereign fire, above seeing the Water phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Fire; beneath black *qi*, bitter entities transform into salty. After half a year, warmth intermingles with cold. In proper transformation, Earth is replete, and the phase’s dominance is halved.

9. *Renxu* below appears *dingchou*: *Ding* and *ren* are the Wood phase, Earth sees *Taiyin* in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is Earth, above seeing the Wood phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Earth; beneath blue-green *qi*, sweet entities transform into sour. After half a year, rain intermingles with wind. In oppositional transformation, Earth is depleted, and the phase’s dominance is extreme.

10. *Renchen* below appears *dingwei*: *Ding* and *ren* are the Wood phase, Earth sees *Taiyin* in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is Earth, above seeing the Wood phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Earth; beneath blue-green *qi*, sweet entities transform into sour. After half a year, rain intermingles with wind. In proper transformation, Earth is replete, and the phase’s dominance is halved.

11. *Xinsi* below appears *bingshen*: *Bing* and *xin* are the Water phase, Earth sees *Shaoyang* in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire, above seeing the Water phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Fire; beneath black *qi*, bitter entities transform into salty. After half a year, heat instead transforms into cold. In oppositional transformation, Earth is depleted, and the phase’s dominance is extreme.

12. *Xinhai* below appears *bingyin*: *Bing* and *xin* are the Water phase, Earth sees *Shaoyang* in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire, above seeing the Water phase. The phase dominates Earth’s Fire; beneath black *qi*, bitter entities become salty. After half a year, heat intermingles with cold. In proper transformation, Earth is replete, and the phase’s dominance is halved.

*The Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi in the Plain Questions, Scroll Thirteen, Concluded*

**The Mysterious Pearl of the Six Qi in the Plain Questions, Scroll Fourteen**
*Recorded by Master Qixuan*

**Victory and Correspondence: The Twelve Methods of the Directing Qi in the Subterranean Springs**

1. *Jihai* below appears *jiayin*: *Shaoyang* ministerial fire resides in the subterranean springs. *Jia* is lodged in *yin*, called the Directing Qi—*qi* meaning convergence. The earthly transformation is natural, without mutual restraint or conquest.

2. *Yisi* below appears *gengshen*: *Shaoyang* ministerial fire resides in the subterranean springs. *Geng* is originally in *shen*; the Directing Qi is the convergence of stem and branch virtue. Earthly fire cannot overcome the annual phase—this is one fire unable to conquer two metals.

3. *Dingyou* below appears *renzi*: *Shaoyin* sovereign fire resides in the subterranean springs. *Ren* is originally in *zi*; stem and branch converge in virtue, earthly transformation follows its own mandate, without mutual restraint or conquest.

4. *Xinmao* below appears *bingwu*: *Shaoyin* sovereign fire resides in the subterranean springs. *Bing* dwells in the south, *wu* is its abode; the earthly transformation’s mandate remains constant, seasonal change does not shift, and the intervening phase is unobstructed.

5. *Renchen* below appears *dingwei*: *Taiyin* earth resides in the subterranean springs. *Ding* is lodged in *wei*; stem and branch share the same domain, the qi’s mandate is self-correcting, without encroaching conquest.

6. *Jiachen* below appears *jiwei*: *Taiyin* earth resides in the subterranean springs. *Ji* also dwells in *wei*; stem and branch share the same region, called the Directing Qi, and the earthly mandate responds to the seasonal signs.

7. *Wuxu* below appears *guichou*: *Taiyin* earth resides in the subterranean springs. *Gui* is originally in *chou*; stem and branch converge, the earthly mandate transforms with singular focus, without intervening restraint.

8. *Gengzi* below appears *yimao*: *Yangming* metal resides in the subterranean springs. *Yi* returns to the east; stem and branch converge in virtue, the earthly transformation responds with clarity, and the qi’s mandate is without flaw.

9. *Bingzi* below appears *xinyou*: *Yangming* metal resides in the subterranean springs. *Xin* turns toward the west; stem and branch share the same position, the earthly transformation adheres to its mandate, without intervening restraint.

10. *Wushen* below appears *guihai*: *Jueyin* wood resides in the subterranean springs. *Gui* arrives in the north; stem and branch converge in position, the earthly transformation follows the seasonal mandate, without deviation from the primordial.

11. *Guiwei* below appears *wuxu*: *Taiyang* water resides in the subterranean springs. *Wu* reaches the celestial interval, as if returning to its dwelling; the earthly transformation is singular and refined, without other conquest.

12. *Jiayin* below appears *jisi*: *Jueyin* wood resides in the subterranean springs. *Ji* returns to the earthly gate, as if going home; the earthly transformation follows the seasonal mandate, responding to the signs without flaw.

**The Twelve Methods of Earthly Victory in the Subterranean Springs**

1. *Renzi* below appears *dingmao*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Yangming* residing in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is metal; the earth conquers the phase, white *qi* ascends, phase transformation does not respond, and in the land of oppositional transformation, its victory is slight.

2. *Renwu* below appears *dingyou*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Yangming* residing in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is metal; the earth conquers the phase, white *qi* ascends, dryness arises and wind is extinguished, and in the land of proper transformation, its victory is mighty.

3. *Guichou* below appears *wuchen*: *Wu-Gui* fire phase, with *Taiyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is water; the earth conquers the phase, black *qi* descends, the fire mandate is halved, and in the land of oppositional transformation, its victory is faint.

4. *Guiwei* below appears *wuxu*: *Wu-Gui* fire phase, with *Taiyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is water; the earth conquers the phase, black *qi* descends, the fire phase is extinguished, and in the land of proper transformation, its victory is formidable.

5. *Jiayin* below appears *jisi*: *Jia-Ji* earth phase, with *Jueyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is wood; the earth conquers the phase, green *qi* ascends, earthly dampness weakens, and in the land of oppositional transformation, its victory is insubstantial.

6. *Jiashen* below appears *jihai*: *Jia-Ji* earth phase, with *Jueyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is wood; the earth conquers the phase, green mist arises on all sides, rain and dampness are entirely depleted, and in the land of proper transformation, its victory is resolute.

7. *Yiyou* below appears *gengzi*: *Yi-Geng* metal phase, with *Shaoyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is sovereign fire; the earth conquers the phase, red *qi* descends, clarity and dryness lose their transformation, and in the land of oppositional transformation, its victory is minimal.

8. *Yimao* below appears *gengwu*: *Yi-Geng* metal phase, with *Shaoyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is sovereign fire; the earth conquers the phase, red *qi* descends, dry metal is entirely lost, and in the land of proper transformation, its victory is extreme.

9. *Bingxu* below appears *xinchou*: *Bing-Xin* water phase, with *Taiyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is earth; the earth conquers the phase, yellow *qi* ascends, the cold phase is extinguished, and in the land of oppositional transformation, its victory is light.

10. *Bingchen* below appears *xinwei*: *Bing-Xin* water phase, with *Taiyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is earth; the earth conquers the phase, yellow *qi* rises, the water phase loses its coldness, and in the land of proper transformation, its victory is severe.

11. *Yisi* below appears *gengshen*: *Yi-Geng* metal phase, with *Shaoyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire; the earth conquers the phase, red *qi* descends, the dry mandate is insufficient, and in the land of oppositional transformation, its victory is faint.

12. *Yihai* below appears *gengyin*: *Yi-Geng* metal phase, with *Shaoyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire; the earth conquers the phase, red *qi* descends, clarity and dryness are not enacted, and in the land of proper transformation, its victory is extreme.

**Disasters, Stagnation, Reversal, and Harmony: The Five Methods of Earthly Stagnation in the Subterranean Springs**

1. *Jueyin* wood resides in the subterranean springs; *si* and *hai* are directly opposed, following the same principle. If metal phase appears above, the metal phase conquers below, wood *qi* does not arise, and green mist lingers as wood *qi* remains long concealed within the earth.

In the following year, when the water phase prevails, the wood *qi* remains concealed, and its pent-up fury erupts from the earth, bringing disaster to the people. The afflictions strike suddenly: loss of speech, paralysis, atrophy of the sinews, emaciation, and cold limbs. The green mist and dampness recede, sweet and yellow *qi* fail to transform, great winds arise repeatedly, the heavens grow dim with dust, and clouds and rain cease.

2. When both sovereign and ministerial fire reside in the subterranean springs, *zi* and *wu*, *yin* and *shen* stand in direct opposition, following the same principle. If the water phase appears above, the water phase conquers below, and the fiery *qi* of the earth—red *qi*—remains concealed, unable to emerge, lying hidden deep within the earth for years. In the following year, when the wood phase arrives, the fire *qi* remains suppressed, and its pent-up fury begins to break forth, bringing disaster to the people. This manifests as madness, convulsions, sighing, depression, restlessness, and oppressive heat, with urine like blood. All things wither and dry, and mountains and rivers grow parched.

3. When *Taiyin* earth resides in the subterranean springs, *chou* and *wei* stand in direct opposition, following the same principle of transformation. If the wood phase appears above, the wood phase conquers below, and the earth *qi* remains concealed within the earth, its yellow *qi*—its true color—unable to emerge for a long time. In the following year, when the fire phase arrives, the earth *qi* remains suppressed, and its pent-up fury begins to vent. Once released, it brings pestilence to the people: jaundice, swelling, dampness, distension, abdominal fullness, swollen feet, diarrhea, and turbid stools. Mountains and marshes grow dim and obscured, all things lose their freshness, and rain falls in murky confusion.

4. When *Yangming* metal resides in the subterranean springs, *mao* and *you* stand in direct opposition, following the same principle of transformation. If the fire phase appears above, the fire phase conquers below, and the white *qi* does not appear, the fire *qi* lying concealed within the earth, unable to ascend. In the following year, when the earth phase arrives, the metal *qi* remains suppressed, and its pent-up fury at last breaks forth from the earth, bringing disaster to the people. The afflictions include wheezing, coughing, grief, chills and fever with shivering, coughing of blood, and withered hair. Grasses and trees wither, the killing force of autumn arises in spring, and the forests resound with eerie sounds.

5. When *Taiyang* water resides in the subterranean springs, *chen* and *xu* stand in direct opposition, following the same principle of transformation. If the earth phase appears above, the earth phase suppresses it, and the black *qi* remains long concealed, unable to manifest. In the following year, when the metal phase arrives, the water *qi* remains suppressed, and its pent-up fury begins to erupt from the earth, bringing disaster to the people. The afflictions include numbness, cold limbs, atrophy of the bones, chills in the channels, incontinence, and weakness in the waist and knees. All flowering plants wither, and the sunlight loses its brilliance.

**The Twelve Methods of Reversed Transformation in the Subterranean Springs**

1. *Bingzi* below appears *xinmao*: *Bing-Xin* water phase, with *Yangming* residing in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is metal; metal generates water. The child occupies the upper position, the father the lower—though they are in harmony, this is called "reversed transformation." Reversed transformation is also inauspicious. In the land of oppositional transformation, the earth’s transformation is not singular.

2. *Bingwu* below appears *xinyou*: *Bing-Xin* water phase, with *Yangming* residing in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is metal; metal generates water. Water occupies the upper position, metal the lower—the child oversteps the father’s position, which is reversed and thus inauspicious. In the land of proper transformation, the disasters are minor.

3. *Dingchou* below appears *renchen*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Taiyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is water; water generates wood. The child wood occupies the upper position, the father water the lower—the child oversteps the father’s position, which is inauspicious. This is reversed transformation. In the land of oppositional transformation, the earth’s mandate is not firm.

4. *Dingwei* below appears *renxu*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Taiyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is water; water generates wood. The child wood occupies the upper position, the father water the lower—the child oversteps the father’s position, which is inauspicious. This is reversed transformation. In the land of proper transformation, the earth’s mandate is firm.

5. *Wuyin* below appears *guisi*: *Wu-Gui* fire phase, with *Jueyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is wood; wood generates fire. The child fire occupies the upper position, the father wood the lower—the child oversteps the father’s

**Twelve Methods of Proper Transformation in the Subterranean Springs**

1. *Jiazi* below appears *Jimao*: *Jia-Ji* earth phase, with *Yangming* residing in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is metal; earth generates metal. The father earth descends to the position of the child metal. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. Though the land of oppositional transformation is weak, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens—auspicious.

2. *Jiawu* below appears *Jiyou*: *Jia-Ji* earth phase, with *Yangming* residing in the subterranean springs. *Yangming* is metal; earth generates metal. The father earth descends to the position of the child metal. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. With the mandate of proper transformation firm, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens, producing auspicious omens.

3. *Yichou* below appears *Gengchen*: *Yi-Geng* metal phase, with *Taiyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is water; metal generates water. The father metal descends to the position of the child water. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. Though the land of oppositional transformation is weak, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens—auspicious.

4. *Yiwei* below appears *Gengxu*: *Yi-Geng* metal phase, with *Taiyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyang* is water; metal generates water. The father metal descends to the position of the child water. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. With the mandate of proper transformation firm, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens, and the waters and marshes yield auspicious signs.

5. *Bingyin* below appears *Xinsi*: *Bing-Xin* water phase, with *Jueyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is wood; water generates wood. The father water descends to the position of the child wood. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. Though the land of oppositional transformation is weak, the earth’s qi supports the phase—likewise auspicious.

6. *Bingshen* below appears *Xinhai*: *Bing-Xin* water phase, with *Jueyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Jueyin* is wood; water generates wood. The father water descends to the position of the child wood. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. With the mandate of proper transformation firm, the earth’s qi supports the phase, giving rise to *lingzhi* mushrooms, auspicious grain, and repeated appearances of blue-green mists.

7. *Dingyou* below appears *Renzi*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Shaoyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is sovereign fire; wood generates fire. The father wood descends to the position of the child fire. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. Though the land of oppositional transformation is weak, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens, also producing warm springs and sweet waters.

8. *Dingmao* below appears *Renwu*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Shaoyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyin* is sovereign fire; wood generates fire. The father wood descends to the position of the child fire. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. With the mandate of proper transformation firm, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens, giving rise to red herbs—consumption prolongs life.

9. *Wuxu* below appears *Guichou*: *Wu-Gui* fire phase, with *Taiyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is earth; fire generates earth. The father fire descends to the position of the child earth. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. Though the land of oppositional transformation is weak, the earth’s qi supports the phase, and turbid waters return to clarity.

10. *Wuchen* below appears *Guiwei*: *Wu-Gui* fire phase, with *Taiyin* residing in the subterranean springs. *Taiyin* is earth; fire generates earth. The father fire descends to the position of the child earth. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. With the mandate of proper transformation firm, the earth’s qi supports the phase, and the land produces toads bearing yellow *zhi* mushrooms on their backs—consumption brings auspicious signs, bestowing earthly transcendence.

11. *Dingsi* below appears *Renshen*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Shaoyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire; wood generates fire. The father wood descends to the position of the child fire. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. Though the land of oppositional transformation is weak, the earth’s qi supports the phase, yielding abundant harvests.

12. *Dinghai* below appears *Renyin*: *Ding-Ren* wood phase, with *Shaoyang* residing in the subterranean springs. *Shaoyang* is ministerial fire; wood generates fire. The father wood descends to the position of the child fire. The father occupying the child’s position is proper. With the mandate of proper transformation firm, the earth’s qi ascends to support the heavens, producing the auspicious sign of abundant harvests.

**Twelve Methods of Auxiliary Transformation in the Subterranean Springs**

1. *Jueyin* in oppositional transformation, not meeting a metal phase: the sour-transforming mandate instead draws upon the bitter. The form of the bitter flavor becomes plump and abundant. The auxiliary of oppositional transformation relies solely upon this.

2. *Jueyin* in proper transformation, not meeting a metal phase: the sour-transforming mandate instead draws upon the bitter. The abundance of the bitter flavor is further supplemented by the salty. The auxiliary of proper transformation relies upon these two.

3. *Shaoyin* in oppositional transformation, not meeting a water phase: the bitter-transforming mandate instead draws upon the sweet. The sweet transformation becomes plump and abundant, without further supplementation. The auxiliary of oppositional transformation relies solely upon this.

4. *Shaoyin* in proper transformation, not meeting a water phase: the bitter-transforming mandate instead draws upon the sweet. The sweet things become plump and abundant, further supplemented by the sour. The auxiliary of proper transformation relies upon these two.

5. *Taiyin* in oppositional transformation, not meeting a wood phase: the sweet-transforming mandate instead draws upon the acrid. The acrid things become plump and abundant, without further supplementation. The auxiliary of oppositional transformation relies solely upon this.

6. *Taiyin* in proper transformation, not meeting a wood phase: the sweet-transforming mandate instead draws upon the acrid. The acrid transformation becomes plump and abundant, further supplemented by the bitter. The auxiliary of proper transformation relies upon these two.

7. *Yangming* in oppositional transformation, not meeting a fire phase: the acrid-transforming mandate instead draws upon the salty. The salty things become plump and abundant, without further supplementation. The auxiliary of oppositional transformation relies solely upon this.

8. *Yangming* in proper transformation, not meeting a fire phase: the acrid-transforming mandate instead draws upon the salty. The salty transformation becomes plump and abundant, further supplemented by the sweet. The auxiliary of proper transformation relies upon these two.

9. *Taiyang* in oppositional transformation, not meeting an earth phase: the salty-transforming mandate instead draws upon the sour. The sour transformation becomes plump and abundant, without further supplementation by the acrid. The auxiliary of oppositional transformation relies solely upon this.

10. *Taiyang* in proper transformation, not meeting an earth phase: the salty-transforming mandate instead draws upon the sour. The sour transformation becomes plump and abundant, further supplemented by the acrid. The auxiliary of proper transformation relies upon these two.

11. *Shaoyang* in oppositional transformation, not meeting a water phase: the bitter-transforming mandate instead draws upon the sweet. The sweet transformation becomes plump and abundant, without further supplementation by the sour. The auxiliary of oppositional transformation relies solely upon this.

12. *Shaoyang* in proper transformation, not meeting a water phase: the bitter-transforming mandate instead draws upon the sweet. The sweet transformation becomes plump and abundant, further supplemented by the sour. The auxiliary of proper transformation relies upon these two.

*Plain Questions: Six Qi Mysterious Pearl Secret Teachings*, Scroll Fourteen, concludes.

*Plain Questions: Six Qi Mysterious Pearl Secret Teachings*, Scroll Fifteen
*Recorded by Master Qixuan*

**Treatise on Terrestrial Intervals and Material Records, Scroll One**
**Thirty-Six Methods of Interval Transformation in the Spring-Qi**

1. Beneath *jiazi*, *jimao* appears: Yangming resides in the spring-qi. Oppositional transformation bears intervals; when harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left. As for the intervals of the land: first, the flavors of beings are interrupted; thereafter, the commands of qi are interrupted. For example, when Yangming resides in the spring-qi: if the celestial north is upright, the terrestrial south is upright; if the celestial south is upright, the terrestrial north is upright. Thus, in upholding the celestial upright, the land manifests *jimao*; if the celestial south is upright, the left reveals Taiyang. Following an odd sequence, Taiyang’s interval comes first—first interrupting the generation of salty flavors and black vegetation, then interrupting the command of cold. Following an even sequence, the right interval comes first: Shaoyang’s right interval first interrupts bitter flavors and red blossoms, then proceeds to the command of heat. This single interval is here presented as an example; all others follow accordingly.

2. Beneath *bingzi*, *xinmao* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Yangming in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

3. Beneath *wuzi*, *guimao* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Yangming in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When disharmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "major interval," which is to say, both left and right intervals occur. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, then the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, then the left.

4. Beneath *gengzi*, *yimao* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Yangming in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

5. Beneath *renzi*, *dingmao* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Yangming in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When the yearly qi cannot overcome the land, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

6. Beneath *yichou*, *gengchen* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Taiyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

7. Beneath *dingchou*, *renchen* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Taiyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

8. Beneath *jichou*, *jiachen* appears: *Jia* and *ji* govern the earth qi. The land reveals Taiyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When disharmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "major interval," which is to say, both left and right intervals occur. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, then the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, then the left.

9. Beneath *xinchou*, *bingchen* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Taiyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

10. Beneath *guichou*, *wuchen* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Taiyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When the yearly qi cannot overcome the land, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

11. Beneath *jiayin*, *jisi* appears: *Jia* and *ji* govern the earth qi. The land reveals Jueyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When the yearly qi cannot overcome the land, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

12. Beneath *bingyin*, *xinsi* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Jueyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

13. Beneath *wuyin*, *guisi* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Jueyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

14. Beneath *gengyin*, *yisi* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Jueyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When disharmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "major interval," which is to say, both left and right intervals occur. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, then the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, then the left.

15. Beneath *renyin*, *dingsi* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Jueyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

16. Beneath *yiyou*, *gengzi* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Shaoyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When the yearly qi cannot overcome the land, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

17. Beneath *dingyou*, *renzi* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Shaoyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval.

A single interval.

If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

18. Beneath *jiyou*, *jiazi* appears: *Jia* and *ji* govern the earth qi. The land reveals Shaoyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

19. Beneath *xinyou*, *bingzi* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Shaoyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When disharmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "major interval," which is to say, both left and right intervals occur. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, followed by the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, followed by the left.

20. Beneath *guiyou*, *wuzi* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Shaoyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

21. Beneath *jiaxu*, *jichou* appears: *Jia* and *ji* govern the earth qi. The land reveals Taiyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

22. Beneath *bingxu*, *xinchou* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Taiyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When the yearly qi cannot overcome the land, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

23. Beneath *wuxu*, *guichou* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Taiyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

24. Beneath *gengxu*, *yichou* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Taiyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

25. Beneath *renxu*, *dingchou* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Taiyin in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When disharmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "major interval," which is to say, both left and right intervals occur. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, followed by the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, followed by the left.

26. Beneath *yisi*, *gengshen* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Shaoyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When the yearly qi cannot overcome the land, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

27. Beneath *dingsi*, *renshen* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Shaoyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

28. Beneath *jisi*, *jiashen* appears: *Jia* and *ji* govern the earth qi. The land reveals Shaoyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

29. Beneath *xinsi*, *bingshen* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Shaoyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When disharmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "major interval," which is to say, both left and right intervals occur. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, followed by the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, followed by the left.

30. Beneath *guisi*, *wushen* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Shaoyang in the spring-qi; oppositional transformation bears intervals. When harmonious with the yearly qi, it is termed a "minor interval," which is to say, a single interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

Next are the six minor intervals of yearly qi punishment:

1. Beneath *wuwu*, *guiyou* appears: *Wu* and *gui* govern the fire qi. The land reveals Yangming in its proper transformation in the spring-qi. Proper transformation originally bears no intervals; thus, when the fire qi is excessive, it overcomes the metal of the governing land below, resulting in a minor interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

2. Beneath *gengshen*, *yihai* appears: *Yi* and *geng* govern the metal qi. The land reveals Jueyin in its proper transformation in the spring-qi. Proper transformation originally bears no intervals; thus, when the metal qi is excessive, it punishes the wood of Jueyin below, and wood succumbs to metal’s conquest, resulting in a minor interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

3. Beneath *renchen*, *dingwei* appears: *Ding* and *ren* govern the wood qi. The land reveals Taiyin earth in the spring-qi. The land’s proper transformation originally bears no intervals; thus, when the wood qi is excessive, it overcomes the earth of the governing land below, resulting in a minor interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

4. Beneath *xinhai*, *bingyin* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Shaoyang ministerial fire in the spring-qi. The land’s proper transformation originally bears no intervals; thus, when the yearly water qi overcomes the fire of the governing land below, it results in a minor interval. If the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

5. Beneath *xinmao*, *bingwu* appears: *Bing* and *xin* govern the water qi. The land reveals Shaoyin sovereign fire in the spring-qi. The land’s proper transformation originally bears no intervals; thus, in a year governed by the water qi, it overcomes the fire of the governing land below, resulting in a minor interval.

When the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

6. Beneath *jiwei*, *jiaxu* appears: *Jia* and *ji* govern the earth qi. The land reveals Taiyang cold-water in the spring-qi. The land’s proper transformation originally bears no intervals; thus, in a year governed by the earth qi, it overcomes the water of the governing land below, resulting in a minor interval. When the terrestrial sequence follows an odd number, the left interval precedes, not the right; if it follows an even number, the right interval precedes, not the left.

**Ten Principles of Earth Intervals in the Spring-Qi**

1. When Shaoyin resides in the spring-qi and encounters its proper transformation, yet no wood qi governs the center, neither left nor right intervals arise to disrupt the transformation. Shaoyin alone conducts its bitter transformation, and thus bitter substances grow increasingly lush. As fire moves through the land, it attains its qi, and since fire generates earth, earth becomes the interval. Sweet substances thus proliferate, and yellow blossoms flourish. Because wood does not arrive to create an interval, earth itself becomes the interval.

2. When Yangming governs the land in the spring-qi and its proper transformation proceeds without intervals—neither above nor below, left nor right, does fire interfere with the central qi, nor do they mutually restrain or overcome—then the land’s metal transforms of itself. White substances grow abundant, and pungent flavors intensify. Thus, the qi of the governing land is exceedingly fine, and earth arrives to create an interval. Sweet substances’ flavors also lengthen, and yellow substances deepen in hue. This occurs as earth qi encroaches upon the mandate of metal.

3. When Shaoyang ministerial fire governs the land in the spring-qi and its proper transformation proceeds without intervals, and when no water qi governs the year, the land attains its own mandate. Bitter flavors thus abound, red blossoms grow vivid, and cinnabar valleys bear fruit. During the time of its proper flourishing, earth arrives to create an interval. Sweet substances vie in lushness, and yellow blossoms compete in growth. This arises as earth rides the beauty of fire to arrive.

4. When Taiyang cold-water governs the land in its proper transformation, with no intervals on left or right, and no earth qi governs the year, the land attains its own mandate. Salty substances’ flavors thus lengthen, and the qi of transformation becomes singular in its command. When its proper mandate is in effect, sweet earth arrives to create an interval. Though it creates an interval, it does not restrain; rather, water remains self-contained. Sweet transformation and sweet-flavored substances form a distinct transformation, self-styled as the earth interval.

5. When Shaoyin conducts a counter-transformation in the spring-qi, the land’s qi becomes depleted. During the time when interval substances have yet to transform, or when interval qi arrives exceedingly late, the transformation of sweet earth arises anew, competing in flavor with the interval substances. Sweetness emerges to supplement the decline of bitterness, and thus within bitterness, sweetness is reborn.

6. When Yangming conducts a counter-transformation in the land, the land’s qi becomes depleted. Pungent substances’ flavors grow thin, and interval transformation arrives late, failing to produce its interval flavor. Sweet earth arrives to nourish the deficiency of metal, and within pungent substances, sweetness may intermingle. This is the interval transformation of sweet earth aiding metal’s flavor.

7. When Shaoyang ministerial fire conducts a counter-transformation in the land, the land possesses an interval transformation. If flavors are not singular, and interval substances seek to arise, earth qi acts first. If within flavors sweetness emerges internally, it prevents saltiness from arising. The nature of this interval sweet earth is swift in transformation and abundant in arrival to meet the interval.

8. When Taiyang conducts a counter-transformation in the spring-qi, the land’s qi becomes depleted. Salty substances’ flavors grow thin, while sweet substances dominate. Thus, within salty substances, a reversal occurs, and sweetness may supplement their saltiness, lengthening their flavor. This is the establishment of sweetness overcoming and returning flavor through restraint.

9. When Taiyin conducts a counter-transformation in the land, the land’s qi becomes depleted and receives intervals from others. If wood arrives to restrain sweetness, sweet flavors ought to decline. Sweet substances, yellow blossoms, and aged grains all grow thin in qi. Their sweet flavors also fear wood and decline, corresponding to the year’s depletion and diminution. Yet the flavor shifts into salty substances, and their flavors ought not to diminish.

10. When Taiyin governs its proper transformation in the spring-qi, and neither left nor right intervals arrive, nor does wood qi govern the year, sweetness rules with singular authority. Thus, within all flavors, sweetness intermingles, distinct from other flavors. Within the spring-qi, only earth intervals abound, for the land’s earth is aided by the great earth.

*Plain Questions: Six Qi Mysterious Pearl Secret Sayings, Scroll Fifteen* concludes.
*Plain Questions: Six Qi Mysterious Pearl Secret Sayings, Scroll Sixteen*
Recorded by Qixuanzi.

**Record of the Correspondences of the Five Phases**

Grasses and trees, wind, Jupiter, furred creatures, thunder and lightning—all correspond to wood. These pertain to the eastern category, governed by Jueyin, presiding over the four seasons as spring, transforming in the initial qi. In the Eight Trigrams, it is Zhen; in the Nine Palaces, it is the Third Palace; its celestial image is Jupiter. The celestial transformation issues as wind, as harmony and warmth. The transformation of creatures produces furred beings, with the *shizi* and qilin as their chiefs. The earth’s production yields sour flavor and blue-green color. The earth’s transformations, celestial stellar images, and wind’s seasonal correspondences—auspicious signs respond to timely omens, inauspicious signs to baleful portents, and propitious signs to felicitous auguries. These eastern categories all correspond to their wood.

When the wind-wood spring mandate brings warmth and harmony, wind spreads and engenders life. The great void is veiled in dust, and mighty winds uproot and shatter. From afar, the qi appears as a blue-green haze; the four qi radiate azure mist and luminous hues. Fragrant blossoms flourish, their transformations sour, their growth lush and exuberant, grasses and trees burgeoning in glory.

When the celestial correct mandate exceeds its measure, wind rules alone, and rain’s nourishment is deficient. Earth then follows its mandate, and wood qi does not punish. If earth does not comply but instead transforms into rain, the rain is suppressed by great winds, and thus rain and wind contend for dominance.

If the mandate aligns with celestial virtue, Jupiter shines brightly, blue-green mists frequently manifest, and azure qi is seen from afar. Furred creatures transform, rare beasts appear as auspicious omens, the earth yields lingzhi, forests grow wondrous trees, and the wilds bear famed herbs—all harmonizing with wood’s virtue.

In the eastern correctness, spring holds no killing mandate. Harmonious qi unfolds repeatedly, flowers and plants bloom charmingly, thunder arises in mid-spring, lightning strikes in season, and rainbows appear in timely response. Following this brings myriad transformations to flourishing glory; opposing it brings calamity and disaster.

When the celestial stems are jia or yi, and the trigrams are Zhen or Xun, if Jupiter deviates from its course, the year brings great famine, and the people suffer many illnesses. If Jupiter appears small, the people face disaster; if it appears large, the ruler is sagely and the state is secure, the people enjoy fortune, and blessings converge.

When Jupiter is lustrous and bright, its body white and tranquil, moving along the central path, its nature is upright. If it moves correctly, the ruler’s heart is upright; if it moves perversely, the ruler’s heart is perverse. If it moves leisurely, it brings double fortune; if it is too slow or swift, losing its position, all is in vain.

A blue-green hue brings peace to the people; yellow brings abundant harvests; black brings great lamentation; red with agitation heralds the rise of armies. If it is large with rays and horns, the ruler is blessed with sons. If it is white and small, the state has a powerful minister deserving execution. If it is blue-green and black, suddenly large then small, encircled by a red halo, a great black wind arrives.

When Jupiter’s movement is regular in its retrogression and progression, it surely brings fortune; if it loses regularity, it surely brings disaster. If Jupiter skips a station and advances, this is called "excess," and there will be war, with princes and lords unsettled. If it retreats from a station, this is called "deficiency," and generals will die and armies be defeated.

When Jupiter is eclipsed by the moon, the state will know much weeping, or a great minister or empress will pass. When it conjoins with Mars, treacherous ministers will be executed. When it approaches or conjoins with Venus, great battles will ensue.

Moreover, when metal and wood stars conjoin, if metal is south of wood, the southern lands will suffer military defeat; if metal is north of wood, the northern lands will suffer defeat—this applies likewise to east and west.

If Jupiter lacks light and moves erratically, the state has lost governance and faces sorrow. If it retrogrades and encroaches upon a state, or lingers and encircles it, the ruler is without the Dao.

Jia and yi are the virtues of wood; wind and thunder are the mandates of wood. Spring winds sigh softly, summer winds flutter and soar, autumn winds are desolate and rustling, and winter winds are whistling and biting—these are the regular patterns of the four seasons. Following them brings peace to all transformations; opposing them brings illness to all people.

If spring winds flutter and soar, the world suffers pestilence; if spring winds are desolate and rustling, the world knows plunder and conflict; if spring winds are whistling and biting, there is famine and loss of livelihood—these are failures of spring wind governance.

If summer winds sigh softly, the state’s governance is unstable; if summer winds are whistling and biting, many people die violently; if summer winds are desolate and rustling, great armies will mobilize—these are failures of summer wind governance.

If autumn winds sigh softly, the coming year will not be bountiful; if autumn winds flutter and soar, the people suffer from madness and illness; if autumn winds are whistling and biting, the state harbors treacherous ministers—these are failures of autumn wind governance.

If winter winds sigh softly, pestilence arises in winter; if winter winds flutter and soar, drought and floods are uneven; if winter winds are desolate and rustling, the five grains will not ripen—these are failures of winter wind governance.

Thunder is the intent and qi of wood. The thunder trigram Zhen corresponds to the eastern mao position. Lightning precedes thunder. If thunder first resounds in the east, the five grains will be abundant. If it first resounds in the south, there will be minor drought. If it first resounds in the west, corpses will lie exposed, and cattle and horses will die of pestilence. If it first resounds in the north, all rivers will overflow.

Winter thunder in the upper reaches is an omen of a fallen state. Where thunder strikes, corpses lie exposed in the wilds. When thunder and lightning are divined together, on the *baku* days there will be illness.

Thunder portends great battles; when great winds arise, the state issues urgent decrees. The *baku* days are: in spring, *jisi* and *dingchou*; in summer, *jiazi* and *renxu*; in autumn, *jihai* and *dingwei*; in winter, *jiawu* and *renchen*.

If on a *wuzi* day in winter there is no rain but lightning strikes, and lightning flashes without thunder, it portends war and chaos in the world. If thunder rumbles without clouds, great disaster befalls the people.

If thunder and lightning strike the imperial palace, ministers plot rebellion, and within five years, armies will clash and blood will flow. If they strike a ancestral temple, it is called "heaven’s warning," and the ruler acts without the Dao. A second strike foretells the state’s territory being diminished and seized within eight years.

If thunder and lightning strike the mansion of a noble, a flattering minister holds power, and within six years, the state’s land will be reduced. If they strike the carriages and cavalry of a noble’s retinue, the ruler is bewitched by women and neglects governance.

A single clap of thunder that ceases portends the ruler issuing severe decrees. If thunder crashes like a thunderbolt and dragons appear, a worthy scholar will emerge in the state. When thunder and rain are accompanied by gale-force winds that uproot trees and destroy houses, petty men occupy high positions while worthy scholars flee. If thunder and lightning strike with great slaughter, the ruler heeds slander and executes the loyal and good.

If thunder remains silent until summer, the ruler trembles without martial authority and retreats before powerful ministers. When thunder roars in late autumn, it is called the "heavenly hound’s cry," and the barbarians mobilize for war. If thunder sounds before spring, the people will suffer from pestilence.

Plants and trees are the earth’s manifestations. When lingzhi mushrooms or extraordinary trees grow in ancestral temples, it signifies the ruler’s devotion to sacrifices and the world’s great peace. If lingzhi or extraordinary trees grow in suburban altars, it portends abundant harvests and universal peace. When lingzhi grows in palace halls, the imperial house will flourish. Trees with interlocking branches are auspicious omens for the state. If extraordinary trees grow in the ruler’s palace, the state will receive blessings. When a tree dies and revives, the state will change its governance.

If mulberry trees wither in summer, the five grains will not ripen. When trees bleed upon being felled, the lord will face misfortune. If trees spontaneously grow on tombs, the state has lost its governance. When trees in the altars of soil and grain die, the ruler will lose territory. If a great tree in the suburban altars dies, it is the same omen.

If trees shed leaves out of season, it is as if they were felled by metal, and within two years, violent armies will invade from abroad. When trees uproot themselves, the state will descend into chaos. If trees bloom a second time, the ruler will face disaster. Frost in summer causes trees to wither and leaves to scatter seventy paces away, foretelling great warfare and people abandoning their homeland. If trees grow in summer but wither before ripening, the people will suffer calamity.

When bamboo and cypress wither in summer, the feudal lords will lose their positions. If trees "weep"—growing damp without rain—their bark turning red, it signals military defeat. Bamboo growing without nodes indicates the state has lost its governance. When bamboo sprouts two stalks from the same root, a powerful minister schemes for the throne. If bamboo leaves wither and suddenly revive, a powerful minister seizes control.

When withered trees revive in winter, it is called "yin and yang exchanging places," and the state will perish within two years. If trees bloom in winter, those who should live will die; winter blossoms foretell the outbreak of war. Except for plum blossoms, winter-sweet, and flowers that bloom in all four seasons, all other winter blooms are inauspicious. If trees bear fruit twice, the dead will return to life. When trees bear fruit in both spring and winter, the ruler will face misfortune. If they bear fruit again in autumn and winter, neighboring states will invade.

When jujube trees bear fruit twice, summer will bring hail. If plum trees bear fruit twice, spring will bring frost. When bamboo bears fruit twice, the people will suffer famine for three years. If trees suddenly cry out, their lord will die. When trees spontaneously grow in roadways, the ruler has lost the Dao. If trees grow atop houses, a sage will emerge in that land. When trees grow in unnatural forms, the people will be displaced.

If trees suddenly emit sounds like metal, the land will split apart. When trees sprout strange branches, the state will collapse. If plants and trees resemble human shapes, the state will face great peril. When grasses and trees wither on their own, the state will attain great peace.

When purslane grows abundantly, many will die of illness. If sweet flags proliferate, great floods will come. When *lian* grass spreads, famine will surely follow. If *hanhua* blooms in excess, there will be plunder and strife. When creatures resembling trees—such as those transforming into qilin, giving birth to Confucius, appearing as silkworms, or manifesting as *xieyu* or *bijiān* beasts—emerge, they are auspicious omens of a sagely king.

When white foxes arrive, governance will extend far. If a unicorn appears, the world will know great peace. When a white elephant arrives, the ruler will be overthrown in his domain. If a white deer appears, the ruler’s affairs will proceed swiftly. When a six-legged beast arrives, the state will be well-ordered without chaos. If a three-eyed beast appears, even commoners will be consulted in governance. When red bears emerge, power will rest with ministers.

If a dragon-horse arrives bearing tribute, the state will submit to its rule. When a patterned fox appears, benevolence will extend to widows and orphans. If a nine-tailed fox appears, the kingly Way will flourish. When a tiger has two mouths, a new lord will rise, and great ministers will rebel and harm him. If tigers devour one another, there will be great famine within three years.

When tigers and wolves enter the state, commanderies and cities will face misfortune. If wolves chase people, barbarians will invade and slaughter the land. When wild beasts and crows gather in the state, cities will face warfare. If wild beasts enter water without cause, the state will perish. When beasts howl in groups within cities, the cities will be emptied. If wild beasts hang themselves in the marketplace, the region will suffer great floods.

When wild beasts—large or small—enter cities, capital districts, or roads in great numbers, great harm will befall the land. If wild beasts give birth to offspring resembling humans, the era will change rulers. If they bear young resembling livestock, cities will be emptied. If wild beasts give birth to chaotic offspring, the ruler’s state will perish. If they bear winged young like birds, the world will face warfare.

When wild beasts give birth to offspring without ears or noses, cities will face rebellion. If they bear young without eyes, cities will face misfortune. If they bear serpent-like offspring, cities will suffer fires. If wild beasts give birth to many-legged young, cities will face civilian disasters. If they bear tailless offspring, the ruler will have no heir. The same applies to domestic animals.

If wild beasts give birth within city walls, the region will suffer drought and great disaster. When wolves and deer cry out ominously in cities, the people will die that year. If foxes enter homes and rooftops in great numbers, there will be sudden deaths, and the ruler will perish through licentiousness. When wild beasts carry withered wood into city streets, the ruler’s state will collapse.

If livestock suddenly speak, their words will foretell good or ill. When moles emerge, evil people will rise. If foxes howl in courtyards, misfortune will surely follow. When gibbons enter cities, water disasters will strike. If otters enter cities, great floods will come. When white hares arrive on their own, it is an auspicious omen for the king.

If hares climb city walls, cities will be emptied. If hares enter palaces without cause and give birth, the state will face misfortune. When hares traverse the royal palace, the ruler will perish. If purple hares appear, there will be abundant harvests. A three-legged hare foretells a great plague across the land.

If oxen and horses suddenly change in appearance, the ruler will face misfortune. When a household’s horse changes color, its master will face misfortune. If a cow gives birth to a horse, the ruler will fail to preserve the ancestral temples.

If oxen or horses suddenly speak, the good or ill they foretell will come to pass. If a cow gives birth to a calf with a southern-facing head, it foretells the division of military lands. If a cow is born with six legs and upper teeth, the ruler of the age will become a bandit. If a cow gives birth to a calf with a head and tail resembling a fish, great warfare will arise. If a cow gives birth to a calf with a human face and animal body, the people of the land will suffer illness. If a cow mates with a horse, the age will fall into chaos.

If a horse suddenly grows horns, the state will perish, or the Son of Heaven will personally lead a campaign against the barbarians. If a horse’s tail transforms to resemble that of an ox, it is called "changing garments," and petty men will govern major affairs. If a horse is born with four ears, the state will be divided into four. If a horse gives birth to a lamb, the people will be at peace—this also applies to cows.

If a sheep has four eyes, it is called "dual radiance," and the land will be torn by fourfold strife. If a dog gives birth to a piglet, the times will be greatly peaceful. If a pig gives birth to a puppy, the times will be unstable. If dogs and pigs mate, the consorts and concubines of feudal lords will plot harm. If a dog’s fur suddenly changes color—if a black dog turns white or a white dog turns black—the master of the household will face punishment. If dogs or pigs emerge from the earth, commanderies and cities will suffer great disasters. If large gatherings of dogs and pigs occur in the streets, a major rebellion will soon arise.

If a dog wails mournfully at a person, there will be a great funeral. If dogs lead one another into water or onto rooftops, there will be a great funeral. If a dog suddenly plays near a well, there will be a terrifying event. If a dog urinates or defecates in a well, ancestral hall, or on bedding, it foretells great fame. If a dog eats its own offspring, there will be imprisonment. If a dog suddenly dies, it is a sign of great misfortune. If a dog gives birth to headless pups, the household will face great misfortune. If a dog is born without hind legs, it is an omen of misfortune for the household.

If a rat gives birth three times in a single day, it foretells famine. If rats build nests in trees, there will be a great flood. If rats gather in the marketplace and wail loudly, the feudal lords will rebel. If rats dance in the central courtyard or on the roads, the household will be ruined. If one hears rat sounds underground, the household will be ruined. If rats eat their own young, the city will be emptied. If rats carry their young away and do not return, there will be a fire. If rats move their young to new burrows, heavy rain will come. If rats gather on high walls, there will be a great flood. If a rat’s head is severed on the road, the age will be marked by warfare and slaughter.

If rats give birth to multiple-headed offspring, the land will be plagued by plunder. If rat pups are born without feet, it foretells a year of misfortune. If rats gather and carry away objects, there will be great famine. If rats damage crops, the state’s punishments and laws will be unjust. The Fire Star, summer’s fire, feathered insects, and winged insects all correspond to fire. The southern regions of bing and ding, governed by the virtue of fire, enact their mandate in summer, aligning with the sovereign and ministerial fires, and above with the Fire Star and the Sparkling Deluder, while below, insects correspond to feathers and wings.

If the Fire Star appears large and radiant, it brings joy, and the people will be healthy and harmonious. If it is small and red, it portends anger, and the people will suffer disasters and illness. If the Fire Star approaches the Woman constellation, pregnant women will face misfortune, and many mothers will die in childbirth. If the Fire Star nears the Southern Dipper, the ruler will face disaster. If the Fire Star approaches the sun and the moon turns red, there will be a great drought.

If the Fire Star grows large and develops rays, encircled by a green halo, it foretells scorching winds and heat-induced illnesses. If the Fire Star deviates from its course and wanders far, the people will suffer disasters and bloodshed. If the Fire Star’s rays are small and flanked by minor red stars, it foretells fires that damage homes and harm many people. If the Fire Star appears yellow and large, the land will be struck by plague. If the Fire Star turns white, armies will invade the imperial palace. If the Fire Star turns green, there will be many dry winds and droughts. If the Fire Star suddenly dims, a great flood will follow drought.

If the celestial fire of bing and ding burns ancestral temples due to the ruler’s lack of reverence, indulgence, or failure to uphold winter’s mandate, and if heavenly fire burns palaces, altars, and state temples, there will be great calamity, for the ruler lacks proper governance within. If the ruler lacks proper governance within and fails to act with integrity toward ministers, it will result in fire disasters. If heavenly fire burns palaces, temples, and residences, the ruler has lost virtuous conduct. If the ruler heeds the words of pregnant women, his harem will diminish.

If heavenly fire burns the gates of commanderies and cities, external rebellions will erupt. If heavenly fire burns the stables, war will begin. If heavenly fire burns many homes, the state’s laws will be flawed. If heavenly fire burns crops in the fields, the local lord has lost governance. If heavenly fire burns mountains and valleys, the chief minister is unjust. If heavenly fire burns all things, the ruler’s heart lacks compassion. If heavenly fire burns oxen, the state’s soldiers will harbor resentment.

If heavenly fire burns rivers and plains, military officials will be in subordinate positions. If heavenly fire burns tents in military camps, the army will be defeated. If heavenly fire burns trees and the trees wail, treacherous people will rise. If heavenly fire burns prisons, the imprisoned noble will be wronged. If heavenly fire burns streets, the people will be displaced. If heavenly fire burns the main hall, it means the ruler does not heed remonstrance.

If flames erupt at night but no fire is visible, the ruler is benighted. If fire arises and extinguishes on its own, the land will be consumed by mutual destruction. If fire burns city walls, great floods will sweep through. If the earth suddenly produces fire with a radiant glow, the state will perish. If fire emerges from the ground in a military camp, the army will be defeated and the general will die. If palaces and halls are scorched by fire without cause, blood will flow in the imperial palace.

If fire emerges from water, bandits will rise, and warfare will be inauspicious. If a phoenix appears even once, the land will enjoy a hundred years of great peace. If paired-wing birds arrive, virtue will extend to the hidden and obscure. If a white turtledove comes, the ruler will not abandon the old for the new. If a white swallow nests, the ruler possesses filial virtue. If a star falls and becomes a crow, a great army will arrive.

If a literary crow dwells in the wild, within three years there will be mourning and drought. If storks and magpies share a nest, it is a sign of decline and loss, as worthy men are overthrown. If magpies nest in trees, many people will die that year. If a crow has three heads, many people will die of illness. If a crow has four feet, the harvest will fail. If a crow has two heads and four feet, the land will be torn by war.

If a crow-like bird with deep red legs and a black body appears, there will be a fire. If a bird as large as a magpie with a black body, fleshy wings, a head like a swallow, and long tail feathers—called a "water demon"—appears, there will be a flood.

If wild geese soar and linger above the palace halls for two or three days, the commanderies and towns will rebel. If a crow caws at the ruler’s gate in a human voice, that ruler will perish. If multicolored flying crows circle the imperial chambers with strange cries, the sovereign will be unsettled. If flocks of crows take human form in flight, the ruler will fall and the people lose their livelihoods. If many crows descend to drink from a household’s well, that home will be emptied. If crows in flight assume the shapes of the six domestic animals, the world will be in chaos. If flocks of crows fly in the form of dragons, the emperor will flee the capital. If flocks of crows fly in the form of bees or flies, there will be a fire. If a wagtail bears young resembling hawks, there will be great winds, and the land will split into three. If a turtledove has one head and three bodies, the earth will quake and suffer damage.

If flocks of crows gather upon the water, women will hold power, and the kingly Way will be severed. If flocks of crows spiral as if in combat, blood will flow in that land. If locusts devour the grass, governance will fall to women. If locusts emerge and fly, then suddenly die on their own, within three years there will be great warfare. If bees are born within the state’s halls, it is inauspicious. If mole crickets swarm and gather at the court, a renowned general will emerge. If locusts have red heads and black bodies, or black heads and red bodies, governance will be harsh and oppressive, and bandits will rise in the wilds. If monstrous insects appear, the people will suffer violence.

In the second year of *Jianwu* during the Han, a strange insect emerged in Hebei, as large as a wild goose, with hair on its head tied like a black coin knot; when it alighted on grass, it could not fly, and transformed into green mud—thus the people of the realm suffered. If shrikes appear as omens, the ruler will face disaster. If creatures with many colors, as large as crows, with heads like cats and long, flat bodies appear—if shrikes gather in numbers, there will be flooding in the middle of the year. If shrikes cry out, there will be mourning and misfortune. If shrikes nest upon the roof and call incessantly, within sixty days disaster will strike.
