If flocks of crows cry repeatedly at night, the capital will be alarmed. If flocks of crows perch upon the roofs of homes, there will be a fire. If crows mate with domestic parrots, the state will be plagued by licentiousness.

If large crows damage the sprouts and ears of the five grains, the regional lord will fail to govern. If sparrows nest in wells, rebels will overthrow the ruler. If sparrows nest in trees, there will be a great flood. If sparrows and swallows contend, neighboring states will fall into chaos. If sparrows and owls fly together, ministers will rebel against the ruler. If flocks of sparrows attack crows, there will be drought and flood. If sparrows vanish, the year’s harvest will fail. If pheasants nest in trees, a great flood will come. If a pheasant enters a home, there will be sorrow. If pheasants sport in the ruler’s hall, the ruler will face disaster. If pheasants cry in flocks, the land will be divided. If pheasants come to mate with domestic parrots, then depart and return, there will be war.

If female parrots cry out at midnight, the realm will be rife with treachery. If a male parrot enters a well, there will be imprisonment. If parrots and crows clash, the ruler will kill. If parrots suddenly die in great numbers, the ruler will be weakened and resources depleted. If parrots cry at dusk, women will hold power. If parrots chase wild crows and fly high away, the local people will scatter. If parrots do not cry at sunrise, the ruler will lack sagacity. If parrots do not lay eggs but instead hatch strange insects, petty men will gain office. If parrots do not leave their nests by noon, the state’s decrees will be untimely. If a female parrot transforms into a male, a woman will later usurp power and disrupt governance.

In the second year of *Xianqing* during the Tang, a female parrot transformed into a male, and later Empress Wu became ruler. If a female parrot grows a crest, ministers will not submit. During the *Xingyuan* era of Emperor Yuan of Jin, a female parrot in Hengyang grew a crest; eighty days later, Huan Xuan established a state, and eighty days after that, he fell. If a parrot’s eggs hatch into bees, the five grains will not ripen. If a parrot’s eggs hatch into mice, there will be plunder and robbery. If parrots and wild crows enter a home, great disaster will strike. If ducks do not enter water, there will be severe drought. If ducks take flight, petty men will rise to high positions. If geese lay eggs resembling running beasts, ministers will be disloyal. If geese have two heads, two rulers will arise. If geese and ducks bear animal tails, the people will suffer calamity.

If a great crow with a hundred heads cries in a flock, the realm will be torn by war and the ruler will spawn many heirs. If a great crow devours wild beasts, a treacherous hero will emerge. If giant mosquitoes like bees come to harm people, the people will face disaster. If strange insects like cicadas, noisy and hooked, appear, petty men will gain influence. If a great crow perches upon the imperial hall and remains still without sound, it is auspicious; if it cries, it is inauspicious. If a great crow perches in a tree and flocks of crows attend it, the state will prosper and the people flourish.

The Central Palace, the Star of Stability, the earth, and the protective insects all correspond to earth. The Star of Stability in the Central Palace is the radiance of earth; when observed in proper motion, all is auspicious, but if it flows in reverse or loses its course, all portends misfortune. When the Star of Stability aligns with earth’s fortune, it corresponds above to the Supreme Yin’s celestial governance, and all omens of disaster or fortune are judged by its conjunction with Saturn.

If the Star of Stability is large and bright, the people will be at peace; if small and dim, the ruler and people will face disaster. If it is large with rays, horns, and a brilliant glow, surrounded by red qi, the realm will suffer pestilence. If it appears alongside a yellow haze in the sky, yellow winds will rise, followed by great plague. If the Star of Stability is small and retreats in reverse, with white qi encroaching upon it, there will be severe drought and the people will suffer. If the Star of Stability is large and yellow, with five ranks of small yellow stars attending it, there will be great abundance and the people will be at peace.

If the Star of Stability flows but does not move, the region it passes over will face disaster. If it moves in reverse and retreats greatly, with rays and horns, there will be military conflict and the people will suffer. Among the five planets, the Star of Stability moves most slowly, taking two and a half years to traverse one palace—this is its regular course. If it moves swiftly out of turn, both military and people will face disaster, and all transformations will be unsettled. If the Star of Stability suddenly turns green, there will be great winds, and the five grains will fail. If it suddenly vanishes, there will first be drought, then rain—either the rain will be uneven, or there will first be rain, then great floods.

If the Star of Stability turns black, there will be prolonged heavy rains. If it is not near the sun but suddenly vanishes, the ruler will perish. If the Star of Stability is small and encircled by a halo, many people will die in disasters.

The Star of Stability shifts and drifts to left or right—this portends civil strife and military chaos. If beneath the Star of Stability appears a crimson qi stretching over ten feet long, it signifies that scheming ministers will seize power.

When the Star of Stability first emerges and appears large, with a white qi extending over fifty feet above it, it foretells slaughter and bloodshed across a thousand li. If the Star of Stability is large and moves in its regular course, with a purple qi trailing behind, it signifies that the emperor’s son will ascend the throne.

If the Star of Stability trespasses against the Southern Dipper, the ruler will face disaster. Should the Star of Stability enter the Celestial River and dim, lingering without movement, people will resort to cannibalism. If the Star of Stability trespasses against the Northern Dipper, the throne will change hands within twelve years.

When a retinue of stars attends the Star of Stability below, the realm will turn toward enlightenment. If a star falls and turns to earth, there will be great famine and bloodshed; if it falls and turns to sand and stone, war will erupt and the state will perish.

When the earth trembles violently, the ruler will lose his throne within a thousand days. If the earth quakes across a thousand li, construction projects will surge, and that year will be inauspicious. All earth tremors are ominous. If the earth quakes and damages city walls, houses, and people, it is called "loss," and warfare will spread across the four seas.

If the earth splits open a zhang wide, the five grains will suffer. If the earth splits beneath the ruler’s gate, ministers will rise from within. If the earth splits in the marketplace, the state will face misfortune. If the earth bleeds, bloodshed will follow. If the earth turns red as cinnabar, turmoil will erupt immediately. If the earth produces crow eggs, the people will fall ill. If the earth splits open a li wide, the general will perish and the state will fall.

When mountains collapse and break, turning into valleys filled with water, the realm will be overrun with refugees. If the earth suddenly rises in the middle of a road, the realm will enjoy great prosperity. If the earth sinks on its own, that state will perish.

In the eighth year of Emperor An of Jin’s *Yuanxing* reign, during the third lunar month of spring, the earth in Shanyin sank four chi deep with a sound like thunder—later, war erupted in fulfillment of the omen. If the earth rises in a city or market, the state will prosper; if it rises within a city’s walls, the structures will decay and collapse. If the earth rises in the marketplace, the state will benefit.

If the earth rises within the altars of soil and grain, the king’s power will grow. If the land produces stones, spring and summer will bring prosperity. If the earth sinks into the ruler’s chambers, ministers will plot rebellion. If the earth collapses on its own, forming springs or producing strange objects, the people will suffer from floods and great disasters.

If sounds arise from tombs, the ruler will face turmoil. If tombs shift on their own, natural disasters will strike and the state will fall. If tombs sink, the people will flee. If trees atop tombs wither, plagues will spread among the people.

If the earth trembles in a military encampment, battle will ensue. If flies and insects appear in a wild encampment, the army will be defeated and the general will die. If pits form in the encampment, the general will perish. If the earth splits in a military camp, it is auspicious to relocate. If the earth sinks or splits within ancestral temples, the state will perish.

If dragons emerge from earth fissures, the ruler will be exiled. If fire arises from earth fissures, the army will be destroyed. If the earth does not freeze in winter, the state will undergo political change. If the earth suddenly produces "soil coins," the people will scatter. If holes appear beneath a household’s rooms, the family will be ruined. If holes appear beneath the imperial gates, the state will fall.

If the earth grows fur in the morning, floods will come. If it grows fur at dusk, rebellion will arise. If the earth produces flesh-like masses, the army and people will suffer disasters. If countless flying insects emerge from earthen holes, plagues will kill many. If black qi rises from earthen holes, the state will harbor secret plots. If white qi emerges and scatters into mist, rebellion will follow.

If a light drizzle falls in winter fog—called "heaven weeping over corpses"—the people will lose their ruler. If snakes emerge from earth fissures, rebellion will come. If humans emerge from earth fissures, disasters will strike. If fish emerge from earth fissures, floods will come. If metal objects emerge from earth fissures, great war will follow. If rats appear from earth fissures, the state will face famine and chaos.

If the earth produces a human face, the wrongly punished will appear. If it produces a human eye, turmoil will follow. If it produces earthen horses, war will erupt. If it produces earthen humans, the feudal lords will rebel. If it produces earthen beasts, the northern tribes will invade. If it produces earthen oxen, discarding them brings good fortune.

If human voices arise from the earth, people will die in disasters. If dog sounds arise from the earth, the state will face trouble. If the cries of flying birds arise from the earth, the people will suffer. If bell sounds arise from the earth, high ministers will face disaster. If thunder sounds arise from the earth, plagues will spread.

If a person grows an extra head atop their own, war will come. If the dead revive in great numbers, famine and rebellion will follow. During the reign of Sun Hao of Wu, the Jiao family revived after seven months in the earth—soon after, the state fell.

If a person is born speaking, the state will face slanderous traitors. If a person is born invisible, royal affairs will grow urgent and the people will flee. If a person is born with dragon or snake features, the state will be invaded. If a virgin gives birth, a son brings good fortune while a daughter brings misfortune. If a person is born with rat features, their land will be seized. If a person is born with wild beast features, barbarian tribes will rise within a year. If a person is born with ox or horse features, war will come. If a person is born with dog or pig features, the ruler will lose the Dao.

If a person is born with a fish’s head, great floods will come. If a person is born with four eyes, the state will decline. If a person is born with eyes on their abdomen, grain will become expensive. If a person is born with a sealed mouth, famine will strike. If a person is born without a head or limbs, the ruler will neglect court affairs. If a person is born without ears or a nose, the ruler will be blind to remonstrance.

If a person is born with many feet, refugees will scatter. If a person is born with hands like feet, treacherous ministers will arise. If a person is born with one head and two bodies, the ruler will lose authority. If a person is born without feet, war and mourning will bring chaos, and the state’s foundations will weaken.

If a person is born with wings and flies away, severe drought will come. If a person is born resembling a yaksha, a cunning hero will rise. If a person is born with ox horns, beasts will fight. If a person is born with flying bird features, refugees will flee within two years. If a person is born without two arms, the state will lose its advisors. If a person is born with one arm, the state will lose loyal worthies. If a person is born with one foot, the state will lose wise counsel.

If a person is born with ten children, feudal lords will vie for power. If a person is born with three sons, great peace will come. If a person is born with three daughters, the state will grow licentious and lose governance. If a person is born as a flesh-like mass, famine will strike. If a person is born without genitals, the state will lack court rituals.

If a person is born with red hair like cinnabar, drought will come, and the family line will end. If a person is born with reversed ribs, a cunning hero will rise. If a person is born without hair, a disastrous year will follow. If a person is born with eyebrows extending past their feet, the state will enjoy longevity. If a person is born with hair covering their face, the state will face many troubles.

If a person is born with a face on their back, disloyal ministers will arise. If a person is born with four feet, the realm will boil over. If a person is born with hair like a monkey’s, the realm will face turmoil. If a person is born with a donkey’s head, upright ministers will not assist. If a person is born with a tail, the people will suffer disasters.

If a person is born with two mouths, the harvest will fail. If a person is born with two pillars and three nostrils on their nose, the state will enjoy good fortune. If a person is born with two pupils in one eye, it is an omen of supreme auspiciousness. If a person is born with seven pupils, the realm will face many troubles. If a person is born with four breasts, the realm will see conquests.

If a person is born with three eyes, the realm will prosper. If a person is born with a dog’s head, the ruler’s heart will be unrighteous. If a person is born with a sheep’s head, the ruler will grow licentious and lose governance. If a person is born with a boar’s head, lewd women will seize power. If a person is born with a monkey’s head, foreign ministers will be disloyal.

If a person is born without nine orifices, the realm will be blocked, and the ruler will be blind. If a person is born with their face on their back, the state will face misfortune. If a person is born with three heads, the state will face conflict. If a person is born with a donkey’s lips, rebellious ministers will arise. If a person is born with a crow’s egg, the state will not promote worthies.

If fog rises from the earth, it corresponds to the virtue of soil. If red qi appears in fog, a great plague will come. If fog transforms into yellow clouds, a severe plague will spread. If thick fog first turns purple then black, darkening the day like night, secret plots will arise within. If fog transforms into green clouds, later becoming purple qi, a sage emperor dwells among the people.

If a great fog persists for seven days without dispersing, the ruler will grow blind to governance.

If fog arises and transforms into rain, lingering without clearing, the ruler heeds the words of a wanton woman. If yellow clouds obscure the sun and later black fog emerges, great rain will follow. If green qi encroaches upon the sun, scattering into yellow qi, wind and rain will come. In evening divination, if red qi later shifts to black clouds, and yellow mingles within, prolonged rain will ensue. If white qi embraces the sun and black clouds cover it, hail will form within the clouds.

The Star of Venus, metal and stone, mountains and valleys, and armored insects all correspond to the Metal phase. The west, governed by the Metal virtue of Geng and Xin, aligns above with Venus, above with the Yang Brightness Controller of Heaven, in the middle with the excessive Metal phase of the year’s qi, and below with the Yang Brightness in the Springs. If Venus appears high and small, it portends great peace. If Venus appears large and radiant, war will arise. If Venus deviates from its course, approaching the south means war in the south; approaching the north means war in the north. If Venus traverses the constellations, its form tapering above and broadening below, advancing and retreating in proper measure, the realm will prosper. If Venus should remain visible when it ought to be hidden, ministers will disobey. If Venus hides when it should not, military affairs will falter. If Venus appears in daylight, great battles will follow. If Venus and the moon eclipse one another at an unusual time, generals will be executed. If Venus enters the moon and its stellar hue remains distinct, ministers plot against the ruler. If Venus emerges in the east while the moon is not yet full, and the star lies south of the moon, it bodes well; if north, armies will be defeated.

When Venus appears in the west at the moon’s first crescent, if the star lies north of the moon in the yin position, the state’s armies will be strong; if south, the central kingdom’s armies will prevail. If Venus and the moon draw near, with three fingers’ space between them, armies will be strong; two fingers’ space portends city distress; one finger’s space means cities will fall and generals flee. If Venus lies north of Saturn, lands will be lost and the state perish. If Venus appears in the east, visible even after sunrise, war will come. If Venus is large at first appearance but later diminishes, armies will weaken. If Venus is small at first but later grows, armies will strengthen. If Venus and Mars converge, one in the east and one in the west, kings and lords will suffer. If Venus sinks into the Milky Way, small and dim, a million will be slain, and blood will flow for a thousand li.

When stars fall as metal or iron, the realm will face war. If cauldrons boil in the wild, emerging from the earth, within three years a state will be usurped. In the third year of the Green Dragon reign of the Wei, Cheng Xiu built palaces, seized Jing’an in the west, and erected a bronze basin to catch dew; the sound of trees breaking echoed for a thousand li as the Metal heavens wept. Thus, the city of Ba flowed away—this was Metal losing its nature. If bells toll on their own, within three years war and chaos will arise. In the tenth year of Emperor An of Jin’s Yongxing reign, Mount Huo collapsed, revealing six bells; later, the throne passed to Liu Yu, Duke of Song.

If stone drums sound on their own, the state will be unsettled. In the time of the Three Hao, stone drums tolled, and the next year Sun En rebelled. If metal drums sound on their own, war will arise. If swords ring on their own, it is inauspicious. If a sword’s blade weeps blood, victory in battle will follow. If the ruler’s sword unsheathes itself, accompanied by blood and sound, war and wounds will come. If the blades of halberds and spears ring, war will arise. If a mirror fails to reflect one’s head, harm will befall. If gold in the state treasury suddenly leaps, the land’s ruler will change. If gold, jade, and treasures in the market suddenly become cheap, the noble will suffer losses.

If cauldrons in a military camp ring, the general will achieve merit. If stone statues weep, the world will fall into chaos. If stone statues emerge in the wild or mountains, a commoner will become ruler. In the second year of Sun Quan’s Wufeng reign, fifth month, in Yangxian County beneath Black Mountain, a stone statue over ten feet tall stood upright—this fulfilled the *Book of Changes* prophecy of Jing Fang that a commoner would become emperor. If stones form the shapes of birds or beasts, lords will rise. If stones resemble flying crows, the ruler’s female relatives and close ministers will conspire. If stones take the form of children, the ruler’s line will end. If stones appear on roads, the state will lose its ruler. If stones appear in stone quarries, the three armies will plot rebellion. If stones grow hair-like strands, within five years war will be plotted. If stones pile atop one another, within five years conspiracies will form. If stones emerge from water, close ministers and women will collude.

If mountains emit purple qi like lingzhi mushrooms, a sagely and enlightened ruler will appear. If mountains produce vessels or chariots, a sagely ruler will arise. When the sage-king Shun ascended the throne, mountains yielded chariots, white essence offered tribute, the Old Man Star appeared, waters flowed freely, the sea stilled its waves, irrigation came in season, the sun and moon shone brightly, and the sage’s virtue reached all without obstruction. If mountains produce auspicious qi, it heralds great peace. When auspicious qi appears, worthies emerge in the wilds, and noble men fill the court.

If mountains wail like men day and night for no reason, war and mourning will come. In the year a state is to perish, stones weep and ghosts wail, and blood rains from the sky. If mountains collapse without cause, the state will divide, and the ruler’s virtue will wane. If mountains collapse in spring, the state will be invaded; in summer, great floods will come; in autumn, great armies will arise; in winter, famine will strike. If mountains split apart, ruler and ministers will contend. If mountains roar like thunder, bandits will come within half a year. If mountains collapse and divide, war will come to that land. If mountains produce strange things unseen by men—with form, substance, or sound—their towns will face great floods and famine.

If mountains tremble at unusual times, the realm will be at war. If mountains suddenly glow, it bodes ill for ministers. If mountains turn red as blood, lords will not aid, and father and son will be estranged. If mountains transform into human shapes, the state will be hollowed. If water in mountain caves flows with the sound of jade, a sagely ruler will ascend the throne. (This jade-like sound is the "jade tone.") If mountains emit green or black qi, their waters will harm people and creatures. If mountains display white qi like silk or jade, it is an auspicious sign. If mountains reveal five-colored clouds and radiance, the king will bring peace, and the people will live in joy.

If tortoises grow green fur, it heralds great peace. If a tortoise’s eyes are white as pearls, an enlightened ruler will appear. If a tortoise resembles conjoined jade, a sagely ruler will emerge.

When crabs emerge in great numbers, it portends fierce winds. When conches sound, it portends fierce winds. When clams emit light, it portends overcast rain. When dried conches cry out on their own, it portends disaster and chaos. When turtles and snakes mate, and many are seen, it portends the state’s collapse and governance’s failure. When conches and clams gather in the capital, rebel armies will rise in turmoil. When flying birds eat clams, it portends famine. When turtles speak in human words, it portends ministers’ rebellion. When turtles and soft-shelled turtles devour fish, it portends famine. A three-legged turtle portends great peace. A three-tailed turtle portends bumper harvests. A nine-tailed turtle portends the state’s prosperity. A four-eyed turtle portends chaos under heaven. When conches and clams are excessively numerous, it portends the people’s suffering. When conches and clams frantically roam on the water’s surface, it portends military upheaval. A white soft-shelled turtle portends foreign ministers’ rebellion. A three-legged soft-shelled turtle portends the rise of feudal lords to kingship. A crab with four shells portends war. When turtles and soft-shelled turtles roam in markets, it portends military upheaval. When a turtle grows horns, it portends plunder and violence. When a soft-shelled turtle grows horns, petty men will seize power.

When frost arrives in accordance with the seasons, the state will possess majesty. If frost lingers at noon and returns after seeing the sun, it signifies ministers executing punishments without regard for the ruler. If frost melts before sunrise, it signifies the ruler failing to administer punishments. If frost persists after seeing the sun, it signifies the ruler’s unyielding authority, impervious to challenge. If frost appears without stars visible, it signifies ministers executing the ruler’s punishments. If frost does not kill living things, it signifies ministers usurping the ruler’s authority. If frost emits sound, it portends armies invading. If frost in the third lunar month kills grass and trees, there will be war and famine. If frost does not fall in late autumn, state governance will falter.

The rivers, seas, streams, wells, scaled creatures, Chen Star (Mercury), and hailstones correspond to the Water phase in the north. The Chen Star, embodying the Water virtue, aligns above with the Celestial Cold Water (Taiyang), harmonizes in the middle with the Water phase’s movement, and corresponds below with the Terrestrial Taiyang. When the Chen Star appears unusually yet shines in proper measure, the people will live in great peace. When the Chen Star appears large and radiant, it portends severe cold and snow. When it appears small and dim, it portends the people’s suffering. When it appears bright yet without sharp rays, clear and luminous, it portends civilized virtue and sagely power. When black qi coils beneath the Chen Star, it portends great floods. When the Chen Star appears small and yellow, it portends a warm winter without cold. When the Chen Star deviates from its course, moves erratically, or wanders, it portends disastrous years.

The Ren and Gui stems embody the Water virtue. When the Yellow River yields the *Hetu* (River Diagram) and the Luo River yields the *Luoshu* (Luo River Writing), when sweet springs flow and sweet dew descends, these all portend the auspicious signs of an enlightened ruler. The Yellow Emperor was born at Shouqiu, and at his birth, sweet springs flowed—a response to the auspicious omen, signifying the virtue of an enlightened ruler. When the sea remains calm without waves, it reflects the virtue of an enlightened ruler. When the Yellow River runs clear, it corresponds to great peace. It clears in alignment with enlightened times, not merely once every three thousand years. When water fails to moisten what lies below, punishments will be unjust. When all rivers flow toward their source, the ruler holds governance firmly.

When water transforms like blood, it will kill people in that land. In the second year of Chen Taijian, the Yangtze River turned to blood, reaching Jinling—later, war erupted, and the last ruler’s state fell. When islands in water grow long, the corresponding region will prosper. When the Earth Star (Saturn) falls and becomes water, it portends war, loss, floods, droughts, and famine. When springs flow without rain, the state will suffer great floods. When springs surge without rain, the people will face chaos. In the fifth year of Yong’an during the reign of Sun Hao of Wu, on the *renwu* day of the eighth month, the Yangtze River swelled and rose—two years later, great armies arose.

When water suddenly reverses its flow, women will confuse and disrupt governance. When flowing water halts, the land will face famine. When stagnant water suddenly flows, war will erupt across the land. When flowing water abruptly changes course, the state will alter its policies. When water in a capital or city suddenly dries up or shifts location, the city’s people will flee. When pond water suddenly overflows, the ruler will perish. When clear water suddenly turns turbid, the heavens will descend into chaos. When water flows through court and market, it portends military upheaval and governance’s collapse. When water freezes in late spring, the state will lose its governance. When water freezes in summer, the year will not yield harvests. When water freezes in autumn, the year will bring chaos. When water does not freeze in winter, the people will fall ill. When water suddenly cries out, the people will suffer. When water produces a metallic sound, the people will be displaced from their lands. When water suddenly emerges from rock crevices, ministers will plot to seize power. When well water overflows, people will flee in disaster. When well water suddenly turns turbid, the land will face plunder and violence. When sounds emerge from wells, it portends war. When black clouds rise from wells, great floods will come. When wells emit qi in summer, yin and yang will lose balance, and the people will fall ill. When thunder arises from wells, droughts and floods will strike unevenly.

When dragon eggs appear in rivers, great floods will come. When water suddenly emerges in a household’s courtyard, great wealth will follow. When ponds and marshes suddenly dry up, the city will decline and face misfortune. When the Yellow River runs dry, it is called "yin reversed," and within five years, people will flee. When the sea tide does not advance, the ruler’s Dao will falter. When the Yellow River surges like mountain peaks, it is called "threatening suppression," and within five years, ministers will rebel. When the sea tide does not recede for long, the state will face chaotic governance. When the sea surges like mountains, the world will be restless and unpeaceful. When rivers suddenly transform, within six years, the state will change rulers. When lakes resemble sea tides, ministers will rebel. When high mounds transform into marshes, their lands will be diminished.

When flowing water carries metal, it portends great peace. When flowing water carries written characters, it portends great peace. When flowing water carries brocade and embroidery, it portends the people’s suffering. When flowing water carries strange wood, an enlightened ruler will appear. When flowing water carries strange beasts, the world will descend into chaos. Hail, snow, and all such phenomena are transformations of water.

When hail falls in summer, it signifies untimely storage of ice. During winter, when the Dipper points to the northern region and the sun aligns with the Xu constellation, the state should store ice, offering it to ancestral temples. If this is not done according to the season, hail will strike in summer. When hail falls upon people, the ruler should heed their grievances. When hail kills birds, the ruler listens to slander. When hail strips tree bark and breaks branches, the ruler will enforce cruel punishments, and the people will harm themselves.

When hail destroys the five grains, and the hailstones bear what seem to be eyes, this is Heaven’s warning of punishment—it is the people’s transgression. When hail falls like pearls, the ruler intends harm upon the people. When hail falls like goose eggs, the ruler is arrogant and negligent. When hail falls like crows’ beaks, Heaven warns against slanderous ministers.

Whenever the Greater Yang governs the heavens, cold encroaches upon the summer mandate. If the summer mandate serves Heaven and fails to enact scorching heat, hail will not fall. If the ruler and minister—both associated with Fire—do not serve Heaven and instead enforce scorching decrees, hail will descend. This is called Heaven’s reprimand through the transformation of Fire.

When winter brings extreme cold yet no snow falls, the ruler lacks governance. When winter brings rain but no snow, yin and yang have reversed their mandates. When snowflakes are large in the air but small upon reaching the ground, punishments are misapplied. When snow accumulates in human shapes, the people face disaster. When snow accumulates in the form of flying birds, the state harbors slanderous ministers. When snow accumulates in the shapes of wolves and tigers, the yin lands will prevail in war. When snow blankets objects but not mountains, the state fails to embrace great worthies.

When snow falls but rises before reaching the ground, only to descend again, the ruler intends to wrong the innocent. When snow falls warm, the ruler will be absolved of guilt.

Scaled creatures take the form of water, manifesting its transformations. When dragons appear, it heralds great peace. When fish are born with two heads, war will follow. When a yellow dragon appears, it is an auspicious sign for the ruler. When Emperor Shun assumed the throne, a yellow dragon bore a jade ring in its presence, revealing a sage and enlightened ruler.

When dragons gather in a state, strife will arise. During the reign of Duke Zhao of Lu, dragons appeared, and Zichan said: "Cultivate virtue, and no harm will come." When a dragon drinks from the water within a military camp, the state will be weakened. When a dragon appears in a river, the ruler will face disaster. When a dragon enters a human dwelling or emerges from a pond, it signifies ministers plotting against their sovereign.

When snakes gather on roads or in cities, or when they swarm markets, it bodes ill for the state. When snakes appear in the main hall during winter, it is inauspicious—do not kill them. When snakes mate in the marketplace, the state will perish. When snakes appear in the market during winter, great ministers plot treason. When snakes enter wells, the people will suffer illness. When snakes are born with two heads, war will come. When a snake is born with one horn, it heralds a feudal lord. When a snake is born with two feet, the people will face disaster. When a snake is born with two tails, bandits and raiders will multiply. When a snake is born with four feet, plunder and violence will erupt.

When people mistakenly call a snake a dragon, the state will be unstable. When a snake is born with a rat’s head, the state will be weakened. When a snake is born with a crow’s beak, it foretells ominous filth. When a snake is born with a human head, the people will suffer death. When a snake is born with crow’s wings, a treacherous hero will rise.

When fish are born with beast-like heads, the state will be unstable. When fish are born with human heads, disease will spread. When fish are born with crow’s beaks, disaster will follow upon sight. When paired fish appear in great numbers, benevolence will extend across the land. When carp grow horns, feudal lords will govern. When Heaven rains fish, there will be war and mourning. When fish traverse human roads, the world will descend into chaos. When the sea punishes great fish, driving them onto land, a high minister will pass. When whales emerge from the sea, the ruler will perish. When fish grow crow’s wings, the world will fall into disorder. When fish are born with four eyes, disaster will strike. When fish appear in great numbers, the harvest will fail. When fish are cheap in the market, famine will follow. When fish grow crow’s tails, the state will undergo change. When *tui*-fish appear, young children will face disaster. When fish resemble women’s faces, licentiousness and chaos will reign.

When rivers and lakes run dry of fish, violent warfare will erupt. During the reigns of King Wu of Chu and King Liu Tan of Wu, a fish from the sea was used as a basin, and in that year, fish vanished from rivers and lakes—turmoil ensued. When fish leap from the water and do not return, sudden war will come. When fish are born with three mouths, it bodes ill for the state. When fish are born eyeless, the state’s governance will falter. When fish are born with human hands, plunder and violence will arise. When fish leap from the water, the people will face disaster. When fish are born with human feet, petty men will serve as ministers. When fish are born tailless, the world will descend into chaos, and people will scatter. When fish gather in broken schools, war will erupt.

The above five categories of anomalous transformations are not mere aberrations—they have existed since ancient times, arising in accordance with the movements of Heaven and Earth’s qi, yielding responses: misfortune answers misfortune, and fortune answers fortune.

**Record of the Origins of Transformation and Endowment**

There is a thing formless yet complete, emerging from the primordial void, where not a single speck of dust yet settled. At the beginning of the wondrous Dao of the Great Beginning, existence arose from non-existence. Before Heaven and Earth took shape, the Great Beginning coalesced into the Supreme Ultimate. The Supreme Ultimate divided, giving birth to Heaven and Earth: the pure qi ascended to form Heaven, while the turbid qi descended to form Earth. The yin essence of Earth became the moon, and the yang essence of Heaven became the sun. The union of sun and moon generated the five planets in the heavens. As Earth first opened, it bore a child named the Five Phases, which shared a kind with the five planets, while the Six Qi formed a single [pattern].

Thus, Earth gave rise to springs and sources as water. The Kan position of the moon lies in the north, so water was born first—its number is one. Next, the yang qi of Heaven became fire. The Li position of the sun resides in the south, so fire was born next—its number is two. Then, water’s veins nourished life, giving rise to grasses and trees. The Kan position in the north generates the Zhen, and Zhen generates wood in the east—thus, wood’s number is three. Next, the primordial transformation gave rise to mountains and peaks, which produced gold and jade. Thus, the Kun position generates the Dui, and Dui generates metal in the west—hence, metal’s number is four. Then, the four directions took form, giving rise to the central soil—thus, soil’s number is five, and it resides in the center.

Among the Five Phases, soil is revered, for it is the Kun soil. This is not the child of fire but the primordial division when turbid qi descended to form Earth—it is the Kun origin. The Kun origin began with the wondrous Dao of the Great Beginning, hence the reverence for Kun soil. The child born of fire is the central soil, not the Kun origin. Thus, Kun and the central soil must occupy two distinct positions.

On Earth, these took form as the Five Phases; in Heaven, they became the Six Qi. The commands of Heaven manifest as wind, which is the Jueyin wood—the first qi.

The east wind harmonizes to become warmth—this is the Shaoyin sovereign fire, hence the second qi. Within warmth arises heat to become summerheat—this is the Shaoyang ministerial fire, hence the third qi. Within summerheat, steaming and nurturing produce dampness—this is the Taiyin soil, hence the fourth qi. Amidst rain and dampness, transformation yields clarity—this is the Yangming metal, hence the fifth qi. Within clarity, cold arises to become chill—this is the Taiyang water, hence the sixth qi. Within cold, wind is born, completing the cycle to return to the beginning. From this point onward, it continues endlessly like a ring without end, cycling without cease.

Thus, Heaven generates Jupiter, and Earth generates wood; when Earth generates wood, Heaven generates wind, and the union of *ding* and *ren* gives rise to furred creatures. Heaven generates Mars, and Earth generates fire; when Earth generates fire, Heaven generates heat, and the union of *wu* and *gui* gives rise to feathered creatures—here, the sovereign and ministerial fires are as one. Heaven generates Saturn, and Earth generates soil; Kun soil first gives rise to *si* fire, for at this time fire generates soil. When Earth generates soil, Heaven generates dampness, which transforms into rain and dew. The union of *jia* and *ji* gives rise to naked creatures.

Heaven generates Venus, and Earth generates metal; when Earth generates metal, Heaven generates emotion. Why does metal transform into dryness? When *xin* is wedded to *bing* as husband, *geng* and *ren* await *xin*’s return; when *xin* returns, it bears fire and metal returns—thus metal transforms into dryness, for this is the husband’s command. This clear transformation is metal’s inherent nature. The union of *yi* and *geng* gives rise to scaled creatures.

Heaven generates Mercury, and Earth generates water; when Earth generates water, Heaven generates cold, and the union of *bing* and *xin* gives rise to scaled creatures.

Heaven generates the qi of birth, and Earth generates spring; when Earth generates sourness, Heaven generates *jue*, and the flow of wood’s movement gives rise to green—the image of the Azure Dragon, paired with the east. Heaven generates the qi of growth, and Earth generates summer; when Earth generates bitterness, Heaven generates *zhi*, and the flow of fire’s movement gives rise to red—the image of the Vermilion Bird, paired with the south. Heaven generates the qi of transformation, and Earth generates long summer (the summer season); soil reigns over the four seasons, and the late summer corresponds to Kun, the true soil position—long summer is the time of nurturing. When Earth generates sweetness, Heaven generates *gong*, and the flow of soil’s movement gives rise to yellow—the image of the August Spirit, paired with the central Kun. The August Spirit encompasses all soil spirits.

Heaven generates the qi of harvest, and Earth generates autumn; when Earth generates acridity, Heaven generates *shang*, and the flow of metal’s movement gives rise to white—the image of the White Tiger, paired with the west. Heaven generates the qi of storage, and Earth generates winter; when Earth generates saltiness, Heaven generates *yu*, and the flow of water’s movement gives rise to black—the image of the Dark Warrior, paired with the north.

Earth generates the *Kan* trigram, and Heaven generates the first palace. Earth generates the *Kun* trigram, and Heaven generates the second palace. Earth generates the *Zhen* trigram, and Heaven generates the third palace. Earth generates the *Xun* trigram, and Heaven generates the fourth palace. Earth generates the central soil, and Heaven generates the fifth palace. Earth generates the *Qian* trigram, and Heaven generates the sixth palace. Earth generates the *Dui* trigram, and Heaven generates the seventh palace. Earth generates the *Gen* trigram, and Heaven generates the eighth palace. Earth generates the *Li* trigram, and Heaven generates the ninth palace. The nine palaces correspond to Earth’s eight trigrams, with Heaven’s nine as an odd number—yang—and Earth’s eight as an even number—yin. Thus, Heaven’s odd yang gives rise to creation, and Earth’s even yin gives rise to transformation—this is called *zaohua* (creation-transformation).

Therefore, yang creates and yin transforms—this is the source of creation and transformation. The term *zaohua* signifies the mutual generation of yin and yang; tracing its origin, yin and yang both arise from the Great Beginning. Later, yin and yang generate one another—yang is born within yin, and yin is born within yang. Thus, when yang reaches its extreme, yin is born, and when yin reaches its extreme, yang is born.

Now, the myriad things—grasses, trees, fruits, grains, flowers, and herbs—are the ancestral roots of inherent nature, all formed naturally from the single qi of the great Dao. Thereafter, creation and transformation diverge. The sprout is creation, and the seed is transformation. If one claims the sprout arises from the seed and the seed matures from the sprout, tracing this to its source becomes unfathomable. Rather, it begins with the single qi of Heaven and Earth in their natural state—at this time, root and sprout arise together. Later, the sprout generates the seed, and the seed generates the sprout—thus it is called *zaohua*. Therefore, the sprout is creation, and the seed is the source of transformation. This is the source of all transformations, and so too are the transformations of the five creatures.

The five creatures encompass all living things in the world, divided into five to correspond with the Five Phases. Now, humans correspond to soil as naked creatures, serving as the chief of the five creatures. From the Great Beginning and the Great Ultimate, when Heaven and Earth first opened, the single qi of the great Dao formed naturally. At that time, male and female arose together; later, through union, humans were born. Thus, the body is creation, and yin qi is the source of transformation. Yin qi refers to the male organ and the female genitalia—the source of transformation. The body generates the yin organ, and the yin organ generates humans through union. This is like plants where the sprout generates the seed, and the seed generates the sprout. Or like birds laying eggs—eggs come from birds, and birds come from eggs—thus its source cannot be exhausted. Tracing it to the beginning, when Heaven and Earth first divided, natural transformation was the same: male and female arose together, later diverging into creation and transformation through union. Within the egg, birds are born, each with male and female. Thus, form is creation, and the egg is the source of transformation.

Now, this principle applies to all five creatures and the myriad transformations, all originating from the beginning of Heaven and Earth.

*Suwen Liuqi Xuanzhu Miyu*, Scroll Sixteen, concludes. (Copyist’s note: The character *shi* was originally written as *lion*.)

*Suwen Liuqi Xuanzhu Miyu*, Scroll Seventeen. Recorded by Qixuanzi.

**The Six Yuan Cyclical Return Annals**

The Yellow Emperor asked: What is the governance of Greater Yang?
Qibo replied: It is the cycle of *chen* and *xu*. Greater Yang governs Wood and is thus placed at the beginning.

**Greater Angle** corresponds to the excessive Wood phase of the central movement. *Jiao* is the note of Wood, hence *Greater Jiao*. Greater Yin descends to appear as Greater Yin at the spring.
*Ren-chen* and *ren-xu* years: *xu* governs the proper transformation, while *chen* governs the oppositional transformation. Its movement is the transformation of Wind and Wood, for *ding* and *ren* govern Wood, hence the Wind transformation. Its transformation manifests as the stirring of plain silk, the splitting and unfolding of the first qi—wind whistles, branches sway, plain silk tears, and all things sprout and begin to grow. Its aberration brings shaking, uprooting, and destruction, for Wind’s fundamental nature is Wood; excess harms Wood itself. Its afflictions include dizziness, tremors, and blurred vision, for when qi is excessive, the Liver suffers its own illness.

**Greater Angle** begins with Wood as the initial qi. Thus, *ren-xu* opposes, while *ren-chen* governs the proper phase.
**Lesser Zhi** arises when *ren-xu* generates *gui-hai* and *ren-chen* generates *gui-si*. This is the first element giving rise to the second, for *gui* governs Fire and *si-hai* are Yin, hence *Lesser Zhi*. *Zhi* is the Yin of Fire.
**Greater Gong** arises when *gui-hai* generates *jia-zi* and *gui-si* generates *jia-wu*. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years, hence the excessive *jia* Earth movement, thus *Greater Gong*. *Gong* is the note of Earth, marking the nurturing of the third element.
**Lesser Shang** arises when *jia-zi* generates *yi-chou* and *jia-wu* generates *yi-wei*. *Yi* governs Metal, and *chou-wei* are Yin years of insufficiency, hence *Lesser Shang*. *Shang* is the note of Metal, marking the nurturing of the fourth element.
**Greater Yu** concludes, for Wood begins and Water ends—this is the head and tail of the Six Qi. Thus, the characters *jiao* and *yu* reveal the beginning and end. This occurs when *yi-chou* generates *bing-yin* and *yi-wei* generates *bing-shen*. *Bing* governs Water, and *yin-shen* are Yang years of excess, hence *Greater Yu*. *Yu* is the note of Water, marking the nurturing of the fifth element.

**Lesser Jiao** marks the return to Yin. As the *Suwen* states, "the door does not descend, and the shoes are placed for the cyclical return." This sixth element begins anew, completing the cycle and returning to *jiao*—thus resuming the beginning. There is one more position, initiating a new cycle’s head, this being the sixth element. *Bing-yin* generates *ding-mao*, and *bing-shen* generates *ding-you*. *Ding* governs Wood, hence *Lesser Jiao*, for *mao-you* are Yin years of insufficiency. Thus, *ding* reappears as *ren*. *Ding* and *ren* harmonize their stem virtues, for *ding* and *ren* govern Wood, and *jiao* reappears—hence the term "cyclical return."

Greater Yang governs Fire and is thus placed second, as the Controller of Heaven.
**Greater Zhi** corresponds to the excessive Fire phase of the central movement. *Zhi* is the note of Fire, hence *Greater Zhi*. Greater Yin descends to appear as Greater Yin at the spring.
*Wu-chen* and *wu-xu* years: *xu* governs the proper transformation, while *chen* governs the oppositional transformation. Its movement is the transformation of Heat, for *wu* governs Fire, and *chen-xu* are Yang years where Fire enacts the mandate of Heat, hence Heat. Its transformation manifests as warmth, summerheat, and oppressive heat—all Fire qi in excess, hence extreme Heat. Its aberration brings blazing wildfires and boiling waters, for Fire’s mandate in excess causes wild waters to seethe. This reflects Fire’s excess.

Yet this is not so. If *wu-yin*, *wu-shen*, *wu-zi*, and *wu-wu* all correspond to Heat transformation and govern excess, why is this not the case for *wu-xu* and *wu-chen*? Because Greater Yang Water governs Heaven, they do not correspond. Their afflictions of Heat oppression also do not correspond.
**Lesser Zhi** is the note of Fire. In *wu-chen* and *wu-xu* years, *wu* governs Fire, and *chen-xu* are Yang years—Yang years should be excessive, yet here it is *Lesser Zhi* because the Controller of Heaven’s Water restrains it, hence *Lesser Zhi*.
**Lesser Gong** arises when *wu-chen* generates *ji-si* and *wu-xu* generates *ji-hai*. *Ji* governs Earth, and *ji-hai* is a Yin year of insufficiency, hence *Lesser Gong*. *Gong* is the note of Earth, marking the nurturing of the second element.
**Greater Shang** arises when *ji-si* generates *geng-wu* and *ji-hai* generates *geng-zi*. *Geng* governs Metal, hence *Shang*. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years of excess, hence *Greater Shang*. *Shang* is the note of Metal, marking the nurturing of the third element.
**Lesser Yu** concludes, for *yu* governs Water as the terminal phase. This occurs when *geng-zi* generates *xin-chou* and *geng-wu* generates *xin-wei*. *Xin* governs Water, and *chou-wei* are Yin years of insufficiency, hence *Lesser Yu*. *Yu* is the note of Water, marking the nurturing of the fourth element.
**Greater Jiao** always begins with Wood as the initial qi. This occurs when *xin-chou* generates *ren-yin* and *xin-wei* generates *ren-shen*. *Ren* governs Wood, hence *Jiao*. *Yin* and *shen* are Yang years of excess, hence *Greater Jiao*. *Jiao* is the note of Wood, marking the nurturing of the fifth element.
**Lesser Zhi** arises when *ren-yin* generates *gui-mao* and *ren-shen* generates *gui-you*. *Gui* governs Fire, hence *Zhi*. *Mao* and *you* are Yin years of insufficiency, hence *Lesser Zhi*. *Zhi* is the note of Fire. The previous cycle began with *wu*, and now the sixth element reveals *gui* and *wu*—*gui* and *wu* stems harmonize with Fire, hence the term "cyclical return."

Greater Yang governs Heaven, and the third movement is *Greater Shang*, hence the third position.
**Greater Gong** corresponds to the central Earth movement. *Gong* is the note of Earth. Greater Yin descends to appear as Greater Yang at the spring.
*A-jia-chen* and *jia-xu* are both *sui-hui* years, with *xu* governing the proper transformation and *chen* the oppositional transformation. Their movements coincide with the Earth of the spring, hence the name "same-year convergence." Its movement is the transformation of Yin mist, for

In *chen* and *xu* Yang years, Yang years govern excess, hence *Greater Gong* serves as the primal head. *Lesser Shang* arises when *jia-chen* generates *yi-si*, and *jia-xu* generates *yi-hai*. *Yi* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Ji-hai* is a Yin year, and Yin years are insufficient, hence *Lesser Shang*. This is the second cycle of generative succession.

*Greater Yu* concludes when *yi-si* generates *bing-wu*, and *yi-hai* generates *bing-zi*. *Bing* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years, and Yang years govern excess, hence *Greater Yu*. This is the third cycle of generative succession.

*Greater Jue* initiates when *bing-wu* generates *ding-wei*, and *bing-zi* generates *ding-chou*. *Ding* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years and should be insufficient, yet why is this *Greater Jue*? *Ding* originally resides in *wei*, and here it aligns with the direct correspondence of the celestial stems, hence *Greater Jue*. Thus, *ding-wei* is *Greater Jue*, and *ding-chou* is *Lesser Jue*, giving rise to two interpretations. This is the fourth cycle of generative succession.

*Greater Zhi* arises when *ding-wei* generates *wu-shen*, and *ding-chou* generates *wu-yin*. *Wu* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Yin* and *shen* are Yang years governing excess, hence *Greater Zhi*. This is the fifth cycle of generative succession.

*Lesser Gong* emerges when *wu-yin* generates *ji-mao*, and *wu-shen* generates *ji-you*. *Ji* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. Here, it returns to *jia*, and *jia* and *ji* harmonize, completing the six cycles and beginning anew. Greater Yang governs Heaven, and this is a Metal movement with Greater Yang, hence the fourth position. *Greater Shang* corresponds to the central Metal movement. Greater Yin descends to appear as Greater Yin at the spring.

*Geng-chen* and *geng-xu* years: *chen* governs oppositional transformation, and *xu* governs proper transformation. Their movement aligns with the Metal of the spring, hence its nature is that of frozen Metal. Its transformation manifests as mist and dew, with Metal’s qi dispersing amidst white haze—fog arises on ridges, dew forms, trees wither, and the Metal wind howls. Its mutation brings stern desiccation, with leaves falling before they yellow, governed by the Metal’s desiccating force. Its affliction is dryness: back pain, chest fullness, and Metal’s excess injuring the lungs, eventually reaching the liver, causing chest fullness and rib-side oppression. *Greater Shang* is the note of Metal. *Geng* governs the Metal movement in *geng-chen* and *geng-xu*, Yang years of *chen* and *xu*, hence *Greater Shang*.

*Lesser Yu* concludes when *geng-chen* generates *xin-si*, and *geng-xu* generates *xin-hai*. *Xin* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Ji-hai* is a Yin year of insufficiency, hence *Lesser Yu*. This is the second cycle of generative succession.

*Lesser Jue* arises when *xin-si* generates *ren-wu*, and *xin-hai* generates *ren-zi*. *Ren* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years and should govern excess, yet why is this *Lesser Jue*? Here, *wu* is Fire, and Wood is weakened by Fire, hence *Lesser Jue*. Thus, *ren-wu* is *Lesser Jue*, and *ren-zi* is *Greater Jue*, giving rise to two interpretations. This is the third cycle of generative succession.

*Greater Zhi* emerges when *ren-wu* generates *gui-wei*, and *ren-zi* generates *gui-chou*. *Gui* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years and should be insufficient, yet why is this *Greater Zhi*? *Gui* originally resides in *chou*, named the stem-branch direct correspondence, hence *gui-chou* is *Greater Zhi*, and *gui-wei* is *Lesser Zhi*. This is the fourth cycle of generative succession.

*Lesser Gong* arises when *gui-wei* generates *jia-shen*, and *gui-chou* generates *jia-yin*. *Jia* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. *Yin* and *shen* are Yang years and should govern excess, yet why is this *Lesser Gong*? Here, *shen* is Metal, named the branch-punishing stem deficiency, as *jia* fears *shen*, hence *Lesser Gong*. Thus, *jia-shen* is *Lesser Gong*, and *jia-yin* is *Greater Gong*, giving rise to two interpretations. This is the fifth cycle of generative succession.

*Lesser Shang* emerges when *jia-shen* generates *yi-you*, and *jia-yin* generates *yi-mao*. *Yi* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Mao* and *you* are Yin years, hence *Lesser Shang*. This is the sixth cycle, beginning with *geng* and ending with *yi*, where *yi* and *geng* harmonize in *Shang*, named "cyclical return." Greater Yang governs Heaven, and this is a Water movement with Greater Yang, hence the fifth position. *Greater Yu* corresponds to the central Water movement. Greater Yin descends to appear as Greater Yin at the spring.

*Bing-chen* and *bing-xu* years: *chen* governs oppositional transformation, and *xu* governs proper transformation. Their movement aligns with the Water’s cold mandate, hence the nature of cold transformation. Its transformation brings congealing severity and biting cold, as the governing Heaven’s Water and the central Water movement combine, hence their mutual intensification. Its mutation brings ice, snow, frost, and hail, as the two Waters merge, easily reversing to cold from warmth, producing hail’s destructive force. Winter’s governance is stern and congealing, with great snow spreading transformation. Its affliction is great retention in the stream-valleys, disease in the kidneys, eventually reaching the heart, with blood stagnating below. One may needle the stream-valley points. *Greater Yu* concludes this Water movement, *bing* governing Water, and *Yu* the note of Water. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years of excess, hence *Greater Yu*.

*Greater Jue* initiates when *bing-chen* generates *ding-si*, and *bing-xu* generates *ding-hai*. *Ding* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Ji-hai* is a Yin year and should be *Lesser Jue*, yet why is this *Greater Jue*? Here, *ji-hai* is the year when Greater Yin governs Heaven, and *ding* aligns with the celestial tally, hence *Greater Jue*. This is the second cycle of generative succession.

*Greater Zhi* emerges when *ding-si* generates *wu-wu*, and *ding-hai* generates *wu-zi*. *Wu* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years of excess, hence *Greater Zhi*. This is the third cycle of generative succession.

*Greater Gong* arises when *wu-zi* generates *ji-chou*, and *wu-wu* generates *ji-wei*. *Ji* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years and should be insufficient, yet why is this *Greater Gong*? *Ji* originally resides in *wei*, aligning with the stem-branch direct correspondence, hence *Greater Gong*. Thus, *ji-wei* is *Greater Gong*, and *ji-chou* is *Lesser Gong*, giving rise to two interpretations. This is the fourth cycle.

*Lesser Shang* emerges when *ji-chou* generates *geng-yin*, and *ji-wei* generates *geng-shen*. *Geng* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Yin* and *shen* are Yang years and should govern excess, yet why is this *Lesser Shang*? Here, *yin* and *shen* are governed by Ministerial Fire, which restrains it, named "celestial punishment." This is the fifth cycle of generative succession.

*Lesser Yu* arises when *geng-shen* generates *xin-you*, and *geng-yin* generates *xin-mao*.

"Xin governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. Here, *xin* meets *bing*, and the subsequent Water movement marks the sixth cycle’s return to completion.

The Emperor said: 'I wish to understand the governance of *Yangming*.'
Qibo replied: 'This pertains to the *mao-you* cycle. *Yangming* presides over Heaven, and with the Water movement in *Yangming*, it is thus designated the first.

*Lesser Jue* appears with the Wood movement in the center. *Shaoyin* is seen below as the *Shaoyin* in the Springs. Cold and heat alternate in victory and restoration, corresponding to Wood’s insufficiency. Disaster strikes the third palace: Metal’s clarity overcomes Wood, the victory is extreme, and Fire arrives to restore balance. Metal is overcome by Fire, and Wood is thus pacified—this is termed 'emotional victory,' with heat’s restoration mirroring the initial triumph. *Zhengshang* governs Heaven as *Yangming* Metal. In years with *wei*-restoration, Heaven’s power is not excessive, hence *Zhengshang*.

*Ding-mao* is a *suihui* year, and *ding-wei* is a *yun* year. *Mao* belongs to Wood, and the movement aligns with the year, hence *suihui*. *Ding-you* is a *zhenghua* year, not termed *hui*. Its movements are wind, clarity, and heat: wind is Wood’s transformation; clarity arises when Metal overcomes Wood; heat is Fire’s restoration over Metal—thus three transformations.

*Zhengjue* is the initial *Jue*, the note of Wood, and *ding* governs the Wood movement. *Mao-you* are Yin years, so *Ding-mao* should be *Lesser Jue*, yet as *mao* Wood is a *suihui* year, it should be *Greater Jue*. Here, under Metal’s dominance, it is *Zhengjue*. *Ding-you* is *Lesser Jue*—these are the two interpretations. This marks the cycle’s beginning.

*Lesser Zhi* arises when *ding-mao* generates *wu-chen*, and *ding-you* generates *wu-xu*. *Wu* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years and should govern excess, yet why is this *Lesser Zhi*? It is because the Heavenly *Yangming* Water overcomes it. This is the second cycle of generative succession.

*Lesser Gong* emerges when *wu-xu* generates *ji-hai*, and *wu-chen* generates *ji-si*. *Ji* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. *Ji-hai* is a Yang year and should govern excess, yet it is *Lesser Gong*. This is the third cycle.

*Greater Shang* arises when *ji-hai* generates *geng-zi*, and *ji-si* generates *geng-wu*. *Geng* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years and should govern excess, yet why is this *Lesser Shang*? It is because *Shaoyin* Sovereign Fire presides over Heaven in these *zi-wu* years, and Heavenly Fire overcomes it—termed 'celestial punishment,' hence *Lesser Shang*. This is the fourth cycle.

*Lesser Yu* concludes when *geng-wu* generates *xin-wei*, and *geng-zi* generates *xin-chou*. *Xin* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years, and Yin years govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Yu*. This is the fifth cycle.

*Lesser Jue* begins when *xin-wei* generates *ren-shen*, and *xin-chou* generates *ren-yin*. *Ren* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Yin* and *shen* are Yang years and should govern excess, yet why is this *Lesser Jue*? It is because *shen* is governed by Metal overcoming the Wood movement—termed 'celestial punishment.' Here, *shen* is *Lesser* and *yin* is *Greater*—this completes the cyclical explanation.

*Yangming* presides over Heaven, and with the Fire movement in *Yangming*, it is thus designated the second.

*Lesser Zhi* appears with the Fire movement in the center. *Shaoyin* is seen below as the *Shaoyin* in the Springs, harmonizing with the Fire below—this aligns with *suihui*. Cold and rain alternate in victory and restoration, corresponding to Fire’s insufficiency. Disaster strikes the ninth palace: Water’s cold overcomes it, the victory is extreme, and Earth’s rain restores balance. Fire is thus pacified—hence cold and rain alternate in victory and restoration.

*Gui-mao* and *gui-you* are *you*-*zhenghua* years, with *mao* as the opposing transformation. Its movements are heat, cold, and rain: heat is Fire’s inherent transformation; cold arises when Water overcomes it; rain is Earth’s restoration over Water—thus three transformations.

*Zhengzhi* in *gui-mao* and *gui-you* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Mao-you* are Yin years and should be *Lesser Zhi*, yet here it is *Zhengzhi* because the Earthly *Shaoyin* Fire aligns with it. This marks the cycle’s beginning.

*Greater Gong* arises when *gui-mao* generates *jia-chen*, and *gui-you* generates *jia-xu*. *Jia* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years, and Yang years govern excess, hence *Greater Gong*. This is the second cycle.

*Lesser Shang* emerges when *jia-chen* generates *yi-si*, and *jia-xu* generates *yi-hai*. *Yi* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Si* and *hai* are Yin years, hence *Lesser Shang*. This is the third cycle.

*Greater Yu* concludes when *yi-si* generates *bing-wu*, and *yi-hai* generates *bing-zi*. *Bing* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years, hence *Greater Yu*. This is the fourth cycle.

*Greater Jue* begins when *bing-wu* generates *ding-wei*, and *bing-zi* generates *ding-chou*. *Ding* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years and should be *Lesser Jue*, yet why is this *Greater Jue*? It is because *ding* originally resides in *wei*, aligning with the stem-branch direct correspondence, hence *Greater Jue*. Here, *wei* is *Greater* and *chou* is *Lesser*—these are the two interpretations. This is the fifth cycle.

*Greater Zhi* arises when *ding-wei* generates *wu-shen*, and *ding-chou* generates *wu-yin*. Previously, *gui* met *wu*, and *wu-gui* aligns with Fire—this movement completes the cycle. This marks the sixth return to the beginning.

*Yangming* presides over Heaven, and with the Earth movement in *Yangming*, it is thus designated the third.

*Lesser Gong* appears with the Earth movement in the center. *Shaoyin* is seen below as the *Shaoyin* in the Springs. Wind and frost alternate in victory and restoration, corresponding to Earth’s insufficiency. Disaster strikes the fifth palace: Wood’s wind overcomes it, the victory is extreme, and Metal’s frost restores balance. Wind is overcome by frost, and Earth is thus pacified—hence wind and frost alternate in victory and restoration.

*Ji-mao* and *ji-you* are *you*-*zhenghua* years, with *mao* as the opposing transformation. Its movements are rain, wind, and frost: rain is Earth’s inherent transformation; wind arises when Wood overcomes Earth; frost is Metal’s restoration over Wood—thus three transformations.

*Lesser Gong* in *ji-mao* and *ji-you* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. This marks the cycle’s beginning.

*Greater Shang* arises when *ji-mao* generates *geng-chen*, and *ji-you* generates *geng-xu*. *Geng* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years, and Yang years govern excess, hence *Greater Shang*. This is the second cycle.

*Lesser Yu* concludes when *geng-xu* generates *xin-hai*, and *geng-chen* generates *xin-si*. *Xin* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Si* and *hai* are Yin years and govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Yu*."

This marks the third cycle of generation. *Lesser Jue* begins when *xin-si* generates *ren-wu*, and *xin-hai* generates *ren-zi*. *Ren* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years, which should govern excess, hence *Greater Jue*; yet here it is *Lesser Jue* because *wu* belongs to Fire, and Wood is weakened when encountering Fire—thus *Lesser Jue* in *zi* and *Greater Jue* in *wu*. This is the fourth cycle of generation.

*Greater Zhi* arises when *ren-wu* generates *gui-wei*, and *ren-zi* generates *gui-chou*. *Gui* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years, which should govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Zhi*; yet here it is *Greater Zhi* because *gui* originally resides in *chou*, forming a stem-branch conjunction with the direct tally—thus *Greater Zhi* in *chou* and *Lesser Zhi* in *wei*. This marks the fifth cycle of generation.

*Greater Gong* concludes when *gui-wei* generates *jia-shen*, and *gui-chou* generates *jia-yin*. *Jia* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. Beginning with *ji* and ending with *jia*, *shen* and *si* unite in Earth. This completes the sixth cycle, returning to the beginning.

Yangming governs the heavens, and Metal movement aligns with Yangming—hence the fourth position. *Lesser Shang* is centered in Metal movement. Shaoyin governs the earth below as the lesser Yin in the spring, where Earth overcomes Metal movement. Heat and cold alternate in victory and restoration, for Metal is insufficient: disaster befalls the seventh palace. Fire enacts the heat mandate to overcome it, reaching extreme excess; Metal has its child, Water, which enacts the cold mandate to restore balance. Fire and Metal thus achieve harmony—hence the name "heat and cold alternate in victory and restoration."

*Yi-mao* and *yi-you* are years of the Grand Celestial Tally, where *yi* originally resides in *mao*—hence the name "year tally." The Grand Celestial Tally arises from a triple conjunction: above, Yangming Metal governs the heavens; in the middle, Metal movement prevails; below, *you* belongs to Metal. The three Metals unite—thus named the Grand Celestial Tally. Its movements—frost, heat, cold, and cool—are Metal’s inherent transformations. In this triple conjunction, Metal, though inherently lesser, should govern excess; thus the two transformations of heat and cold do not manifest, and victory and restoration do not arise.

*Greater Shang* in *yi-mao* and *yi-you*: *yi* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Mao* and *you* are Yin years, which should govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Shang*; yet here it is *Greater Shang* due to the Grand Celestial Tally’s triple conjunction. This marks the beginning of the cycle.

*Greater Yu* concludes when *yi-mao* generates *bing-chen*, and *yi-you* generates *bing-xu*. *Bing* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years, governing excess—hence *Greater Yu*. This is the second cycle of generation.

*Greater Jue* begins when *bing-chen* generates *ding-si*, and *bing-xu* generates *ding-hai*. *Ding* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Si* and *hai* are Yin years, which should govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Jue*; yet here it is *Greater Jue* because Jueyin Wood governs the heavens in *si-hai*, aligning the movement with the celestial tally. This marks the third cycle of generation.

*Greater Gong* arises when *wu-wu* generates *ji-wei*, and *wu-zi* generates *ji-chou*. *Ji* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years, which should govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Gong*; yet here it is *Greater Gong* because *ji* originally resides in *wei*, forming a stem-branch conjunction with the direct tally—thus *Greater Gong* in *wei* and *Lesser Gong* in *chou*. This marks the fifth cycle of generation.

*Greater Shang* concludes when *ji-wei* generates *geng-shen*, and *ji-chou* generates *geng-yin*. *Geng* governs the Metal movement, beginning with *yi* and ending with *geng*—*geng* and *yi* unite in Metal movement. This completes the sixth cycle, returning to the beginning.

[The fourth cycle is absent.]

Yangming governs the heavens, and Water movement aligns with Yangming—hence the fifth position. *Lesser Yu* is centered in Water movement. Shaoyin governs the earth below as the lesser Yin in the spring, where Water movement overcomes Earth Fire. Rain and wind alternate in victory and restoration, for Water is insufficient: disaster befalls the first palace. Earth enacts the rain mandate to overcome it, reaching extreme excess; Water has its child, Wood, which enacts the wind mandate to restore balance. Wind overcomes rain, and Water achieves harmony—hence the name "rain and wind alternate in victory and restoration."

*Xin-mao* and *xin-you* govern the right transformation in *you* and the opposing transformation in *mao*. Their movements—cold, rain, and wind—are Water’s inherent transformations; rain arises when Earth overcomes Water, and wind arises when Wood restores victory over Earth—thus three transformations govern the mandate. *Lesser Yu* concludes in *xin-mao* and *xin-you*: *xin* governs the Water movement, and *Yu* is the note of Water. *Mao* and *you* are Yin years, governing insufficiency—hence *Lesser Yu*. This marks the beginning of the cycle.

*Greater Jue* begins when *xin-mao* generates *ren-chen*, and *xin-you* generates *ren-xu*. *Ren* governs the Wood movement, and *Jue* is the note of Wood. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years—hence *Greater Jue*. This is the second cycle of generation.

*Greater Zhi* arises when *ren-chen* generates *gui-si*, and *ren-xu* generates *gui-hai*. *Gui* governs the Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the note of Fire. *Si* and *hai* are Yin years, which should govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Zhi*; yet here it is *Greater Zhi* because the Fire year-branch assists it—thus *Greater Zhi* in *gui-si* and *Lesser Zhi* in *gui-hai*, as both interpretations apply. This marks the third cycle of generation.

*Greater Gong* arises when *gui-si* generates *jia-wu*, and *gui-hai* generates *jia-zi*. *Jia* governs the Earth movement, and *Gong* is the note of Earth. *Zi* and *wu* are Yang years—hence *Greater Gong*. This marks the fourth cycle of generation.

*Greater Shang* concludes when *jia-wu* generates *yi-wei*, and *jia-zi* generates *yi-chou*. *Yi* governs the Metal movement, and *Shang* is the note of Metal. *Chou* and *wei* are Yin years, which should govern insufficiency, hence *Lesser Shang*; yet here it is *Greater Shang* because *chou* and *wei* belong to Earth, which generates Metal, reinforcing it. This marks the fifth cycle of generation.

*Greater Yu* concludes when *yi-wei* generates *bing-shen*, and *yi-chou* generates *bing-yin*. *Bing* governs the Water movement, beginning with *xin* and ending with *bing*—*bing* and *xin* unite in the primordial *Yu* of Water. This completes the sixth cycle, returning to the beginning.

The Yellow Emperor said: "Excellent. What of the governance of Shaoyang?"

Qibo replied: "It pertains to the *yin* and *shen* cycles. Shaoyang governs the heavens, and Wood movement aligns with Shaoyang—hence the first position. *Greater Jue* is centered in Wood movement. Jueyin governs the earth below as the lesser Yin in the spring. Movement and Wood unite in a year tally.

*Ren-yin* and *ren-shen* govern the right transformation in *yin* and the opposing transformation in *shen*. Their movement is the drumming of wind, as Wood movement enacts the wind mandate. Its transformations are the resounding of wind, the purity of spring, the splitting of the earth, and the unfolding of buds—wind’s drumming scatters purity, opens the earth, splits flowers, and awakens spring’s unfolding."

Its transformations are the shaking, uprooting, and snapping of trees in furious winds—thus wind injures Wood, causing collapse and ruin. Its afflictions are dizziness, vertigo, limb distension, rib-side tension, and fright—excess injures the liver, and prolonged harm extends to the spleen.

*Greater Jue* begins with *ren-yin* and *ren-shen*. *Ren* governs Wood movement, and *Jue* is the Wood tone. *Yin* and *shen* are Yang years, hence *Greater Jue*—the primal origin.

*Lesser Zhi* arises when *ren-yin* generates *gui-mao* and *ren-shen* generates *gui-you*. *Gui* governs Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the Fire tone. *Mao* and *you* are Yin years, thus deficient, hence *Lesser Zhi*. This is the second phase of generative assistance.

*Greater Gong* arises when *gui-mao* generates *jia-chen* and *gui-you* generates *jia-xu*. *Jia* governs Earth movement, and *Gong* is the Earth tone. *Chen* and *xu* are Yang years, thus excessive, hence *Greater Gong*. This is the third phase of generative assistance.

*Lesser Shang* arises when *jia-chen* generates *yi-si* and *jia-xu* generates *yi-hai*. *Yi* governs Metal movement, and *Shang* is the Metal tone. *Si* and *hai* are Yin years, thus deficient, hence *Lesser Shang*. This is the fourth phase of generative assistance.

*Greater Yu* concludes when *yi-si* generates *bing-wu* and *yi-hai* generates *bing-zi*. *Bing* governs Water movement, and *Yu* is the Water tone. *Wu* and *zi* are Yang years, thus excessive, hence *Greater Yu*. This is the fifth phase.

*Lesser Jue* begins when *bing-wu* generates *ding-wei* and *bing-zi* generates *ding-chou*. *Ding* governs Wood movement, and *Jue* is the Wood tone. *Ren* at the origin and *ding* at the end unite in Wood movement. This is the sixth phase, completing the cycle and returning to the beginning.

Shaoyang governs the heavens, and Fire movement aligns with Shaoyang—hence the second position. *Greater Zhi* is centered in Fire movement, above harmonizing with heaven. Jueyin governs the earth below as the lesser Yin, with Wood and wind in the spring.

*Wu-yin* and *wu-shen* are celestial correspondences, where correspondence means union. Above, lesser Yang Fire governs heaven; within, *wu* governs Fire movement—above and within unite in virtue. Its movement is summerheat and Fire, its transformation summerheat. Its transformations are warmth, clamor, oppression, and scorching—ministerial Fire transforms in accord with the two qi. Thus all things flourish in warmth and clamor.

Its excesses are blazing fury and seething overflow—fire scorches flowing metal, and wild marshes boil like broth. Its afflictions are upper-body heat and oppression, blood spillage and hemorrhage, heart pain—excess Fire injures the heart, and prolonged harm extends to the lungs. When Fire governs heaven, heat afflictions arise above. Blood spillage is vomiting blood or nosebleed; hemorrhage is bloody stool or rectal bleeding. Heart pain is fullness and pain in the heart.

*Greater Zhi* corresponds to *wu-yin* and *wu-shen*. *Wu* governs Fire movement, and *Zhi* is the Fire tone.

In *yin* and *shen* yang years, excess prevails, hence *Greater Zhi*. This marks the Primordial Origin. *Lesser Gong* arises when *wu-yin* gives birth to *ji-mao*, and *wu-shen* gives birth to *ji-you*. *Ji* governs the Earth phase, and *Gong* is the Earth tone. In *mao* and *you* yin years, it is *Lesser Gong*. This is the Second Origin.

*Greater Shang* arises when *ji-mao* gives birth to *geng-chen*, and *ji-you* gives birth to *geng-xu*. *Geng* governs the Metal phase, and *Shang* is the Metal tone. In *chen* and *xu* yang years, excess prevails, hence *Greater Shang*. This is the Third Origin of Nourishment.

*Lesser Yu* concludes when *geng-chen* gives birth to *xin-si*, and *geng-xu* gives birth to *xin-hai*. *Xin* governs the Water phase, and *Yu* is the Water tone. In *si* and *hai* yin years, deficiency prevails, hence *Lesser Yu*. This is the Fourth Origin of Nourishment.

*Lesser Jue* initiates when *xin-si* gives birth to *ren-wu*, and *xin-hai* gives birth to *ren-zi*. *Ren* governs the Wood phase, and *Jue* is the Wood tone.
